# front:intro
## rx9u
See [[PSA-rx9u]]
# 1:intro
## fan4
See [[PSA-fan4]]
# 1:1
## w56f
See [[PSA-w56f]]
## gz4n
The “advice of the wicked” is spoken of as if it were a path to follow. Alternate translation: “who does not follow the advice of the wicked” or “who does not do what wicked people advise” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## uqr7
Here the word “pathway” represents the way people live. The word “stand” is in parallel with “walk.” Alternate translation: “imitate the behavior of sinful people” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## nk2a
Sitting with people who mock God represents joining people who mock God. Alternate translation: “or join those who mock God” or “or mock God with others who mock him” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 1:2
## izu5
The word “delight” is an abstract noun that can be stated as a verb. A person who can “delight … in the law” is happy because the law is good and because one is obeying it. Alternate translation: “what makes him truly happy is the law of Yahweh” or “what makes him truly happy is to know that he is obeying the law of Yahweh” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## ns4k
This is the name of God that he revealed to his people in the Old Testament. See the translationWord page about Yahweh concerning how to translate this.

# 1:3
## t59m
See [[PSA-t59m]]
## d83j
In the Bible, people are often spoken of as trees. People who delight in Yahweh’s law can do all God wants them to do just as a tree that is planted by water produces good fruit. Alternate translation: “He will be prosperous like a tree … fruit in its season” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## wir5
A tree that is planted by a stream can get enough water to be healthy.

## tag1
Healthy trees produce good fruit at the right time.

## xf3j
If a tree gets enough water, its leaves do not dry out and die.

## c784
“He will be successful at whatever he does”

# 1:4
## g6a7
How they are not like that can be stated clearly. “The wicked are not prosperous” or “The wicked do not prosper” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## lnx8
How they are like chaff can be stated clearly. Alternate translation: “but instead they are worthless like the chaff” (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 1:5
## atv6
Possible meanings are (1) not standing in the judgment is a metonym for being judged by God and having to leave his presence. Alternate translation: “will not continue to stay before God when he judges them” or “will have to leave God’s presence when he judges them as guilty” or (2) not standing in the judgment is a metaphor for being condemned in the judgment. “Alternate translation: “will be condemned in the judgment” or “will be condemned when God judges them” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## va3s
The noun judgment can be expressed as a verb. This probably refers to the final judgment when God judges all people. Alternate translation: “when God judges everyone”

## x8sk
Translators can supply the verb “stand.” Alternate translation: “neither will sinners stand in the assembly of the righteous” or “and sinners will not stand in the assembly of the righteous” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

## nr84
Being accepted by God as righteous is spoken of as standing with the group of righteous people. Alternate translation: “and God will not accept sinners along with the righteous people” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 1:6
## wmx7
These two clauses contrast what happens to righteous people with what happens to wicked people. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## cxy6
How people live is spoken of as if it were a “way” or “road” that they are walking on. Alternate translation: “how the righteous live” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## jy56
How people live and what they do is spoken of as if it were a “way” or “road” that they walk on. Possible meanings are (1) the way perishing represents the wicked perishing because of how they live. Alternate translation: “The wicked will die because of how they live” or (2) the way perishing is a metaphor for no longer being able to live the way they do. Alternate translation: “the wicked will no longer be able to live the way they live” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

# 2:intro
## z14u
See [[PSA-z14u]]
# 2:1
## bht4
See [[PSA-bht4]]
## e4gn
These questions are used to show surprise that the people are doing things that are so wrong and foolish. Alternate translation: “The nations are in turmoil and the peoples are making plots that will fail.” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## zq9d
This probably means that the nations were making a noisy and angry commotion.

## hd4h
This represents either the leaders or the people of the nations. (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## jxy7
These are probably plots against God and his people.

# 2:2
## ag3k
These two clauses have similar meanings. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## pt5v
These phrases mean the same thing, implying that the leaders stand together in order to fight against Yahweh and his Messiah. This can be stated explicitly. Alternate translation: “gather to fight … plan together to revolt” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 2:3
## xw9h
The people of other nations speak of Yahweh and the Messiah’s rule over them as if it were shackles and chains. Alternate translation: “We should free ourselves from their control; we should not let them rule over us any longer” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 2:4
## e8l8
These phrases refer to Yahweh. Yahweh is often called “the Lord” but the words for “Yahweh” and “the Lord” are different.

## t9zx
Here sitting represents ruling. What he sits on can be stated clearly. Alternate translation: “rules in the heavens” or “sits on his throne in heaven” (See: [[figs-explicit]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

## zyd3
“the Lord mocks those people.” Why he mocks them can be stated clearly. Alternate translation: “The Lord mocks them for their foolish plans” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 2:5
## z631
The abstract noun “rage” can be stated as “furious.” Alternate translation: “he will be furious and terrify them” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## jjb4
greatly frighten

# 2:6
## emc4
Yahweh is emphasizing that he, and not someone else, has anointed his king.

## v3q9
“appointed my king to rule”

# 2:7
## d5l7
The person saying this is the king. This can be stated clearly. Alternate translation: “The king says, ‘I will announce a decree of Yahweh.’ He” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## h869
“Yahweh said to me”

## qp2j
Among many peoples in that part of the world then, men could decide to legally adopt children, who would become their heirs. Here Yahweh adopts a man and makes him king of Israel. Alternate translation: “I make you my son. This day I have become your father” or “Now you are my son and am your father”

# 2:8
## sy59
See [[PSA-sy59]]
## vjb5
These phrases express very similar ideas. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## cv7i
“the lands that are very far away”

# 2:9
## uaa7
These phrases express very similar ideas. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## at9u
Defeating the nations is spoken of as breaking them, and his power is spoken of as an iron rod. Alternate translation: “You will defeat them completely by your power” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## a2x4
Destroying nations is spoken of as if they could be smashed like a clay jar. Alternate translation: you will completely destroy them like a clay pot” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-simile]])

## ggd3
A potter is a person who makes clay pots and jars. These are fragile and can be broken easily. Alternate translation: “a clay jar” or “a clay pot” (See: [[translate-unknown]])

# 2:10
## upx2
These two phrases have similar meanings. Alternate translation: “So now, you kings and rulers of the earth, be warned and corrected” (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## j2nx
This can be stated with an active form. Alternate translation: “listen to this warning” or “be wise” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## nyh6
This can be stated with an active form. Alternate translation: “listen to this correction” or “take this correction” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 2:12
## w4m8
People would show their king that they were loyal to him by kissing him, perhaps on the feet. Alternate translation: “Show the son that you are truly loyal to him” or “Bow down humbly before his son” (See: [[translate-symaction]])

## v3bs
This may refer to dying right there, before the person has a chance to go away. Alternate translation: “you will die immediately”

## l654
The king’s anger is spoken of as if it were a fire that could burn. Alternate translation: “when he suddenly becomes very angry” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ty9p
Asking the king for protection is spoken of as seeking refuge in him. Alternate translation: “ask the king to protect them” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 3:intro
## py7j
See [[PSA-py7j]]
# 3:1
## ylp1
See [[PSA-ylp1]]
## g1yb
Possible meanings are (1) David wrote the psalm or (2) the psalm is about David or (3) the psalm is in the style of David’s psalms.

## xp7i
This exclamation shows that David is afraid of his enemies. Alternate translation: “Oh Yahweh, I have so many enemies!” (See: [[figs-exclamations]])

## cj3u
Fighting against someone is spoken of as rising against him. Alternate translation: “come against me” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 3:3
## mj2u
A shield protects a soldier. David speaks as if God were a shield protecting him. Alternate translation: “you, Yahweh, protect me like a shield” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## llc4
“you are my glory.” By calling God his glory, David says that God is the one who gives him glory. Since David has just spoken about his enemies and God being his protector, he probably meant that God gives him glory by giving him victory over his enemies. Alternate translation: “you are the one who gives me glory” or “you are the one who gives me victory” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## hj6j
“you are the one who lifts up my head.” Giving someone courage is spoken of as lifting up his head. Alternate translation: “the one who encourages me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 3:4
## bz2m
Using one’s voice to cry out is spoken of as lifting up his voice. Alternate translation: “I cry out” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 3:6
## q7wy
“have surrounded me to destroy me”

# 3:7
## zax2
David speaks of starting to do something as getting up. Alternate translation: “Take action” or “Do something” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## az5m
These phrases say very similar things. The phrases “my enemies” and “the wicked” refer to the same group of people. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## r6xe
This was a way of insulting people. David speaks as if Yahweh would come and physically hit his enemies. Alternate translation: “For you will insult all my enemies like someone hitting them on the jaw” (See: [[translate-symaction]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## k36i
Animals attack with their teeth. Breaking their teeth takes away their power to attack. David speaks as if Yahweh would come and physically fight against the wicked. Alternate translation: “you will make the wicked unable to harm me like someone breaking the teeth of a ferocious animal” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 3:8
## x9bn
The abstract noun “salvation” can be expressed with the verb “save.” Alternate translation: “Yahweh saves his people” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 4:intro
## b2qk
See [[PSA-b2qk]]
# 4:1
## zjj1
See [[PSA-zjj1]]
## q28k
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## k7md
“people should play stringed instruments with this song”

## f3xk
“Respond to me when I call” or “Help me when I call”

## dd31
“God, who shows that I am righteous”

## n99c
Being in danger is spoken of as being in a narrow space. Alternate translation: “rescue me when I am in danger” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 4:2
## r39v
See [[PSA-r39v]]
## p3x5
David uses this question to rebuke his enemies. Alternate translation: “You people continually turn my honor into shame!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## vy7i
Shaming him instead of honoring him is spoken of as making his honor become shame. Alternate translation: “shame me instead of honoring me” or “bring me shame when you should be honoring me”

## i8ct
David uses this question to rebuke his enemies. Alternate translation: “You continue to love things that are worthless and seek after lies.” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## mvp9
These two phrases are very similar in meaning. The lies are worthless. Alternate translation: “love worthless lies” (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

# 4:3
## w2gh
“Yahweh chooses godly people for himself”

# 4:4
## api1
The relationship between “tremble” and “fear” and who people should fear can be stated clearly. Alternate translation: “Fear Yahweh so much that you tremble” or “Stand in awe of Yahweh” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## u9p9
shake from fear

## l67w
The heart represents a person’s thoughts. Thinking carefully is spoken of as meditating in one’s heart. Alternate translation: “Think carefully” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 4:5
## h8tj
“Offer the right sacrifices”

## ul9j
Here “trust” is spoken of as if it were an object that could be put somewhere. The abstract noun “trust” can be stated as a verb. Alternate translation: “trust in Yahweh” or “trust Yahweh” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 4:6
## k53m
This question is used either to ask for something or to express a wish about something that has not happened. Alternate translation: “Please show us something good!” or “We wish someone would show us something good!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## uvl3
Possible meanings are (1) showing something good represents bringing good things. Alternate translation: “Who will bring good things to us?” or (2) showing something good represents saying that good things have happened. Alternate translation: “Who will say that anything good has happened?” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## stu3
The writer speaks of Yahweh acting favorably towards them as if Yahweh’s face shone a light on them. Alternate translation: “act favorably towards us” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 4:7
## v4vs
The heart represents the person. Alternate translation: “You have given me more gladness” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## b9ht
Here “gladness” is spoken of as if it is an object that can be given. The abstract noun “gladness” can be stated as “glad.” Alternate translation: “You have made me more glad than others are” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## izx5
“New wine” may represent grapes. Alternate translation: “when they reap plentiful harvests of grain and grapes” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 4:8
## b57u
Peace is spoken of as if it were a place. This can be restated to remove the abstract noun “peace.” Alternate translation: “I will be peaceful when I lie down and sleep” or “I will not be afraid of danger when I lie down and sleep” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## p2ce
The words “safe” and “secure” mean basically the same thing and emphasize complete safety. Alternate translation: “make me completely safe” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 5:intro
## e67h
See [[PSA-e67h]]
# 5:1
## k92k
See [[PSA-k92k]]
## q7tu
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## tu54
“This song should be accompanied by people who play wind instruments.”

## xts1
This is a call for help. Alternate translation: “Listen to me as I call to you for help” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## i566
low sounds that people make with the voice when they are suffering

# 5:3
## i42x
These two phrases are very similar in meaning. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## q5qw
“I will make my request” or “I will ask you for what I need”

## rk6n
“wait, expecting you to do what I ask you to do”

# 5:6
## qjt8
Since David is speaking to God in this psalm, this sentence can be stated with the word “you.” Alternate translation: “Yahweh, you despise violent and deceitful men” or “Yahweh, you hate men who do violent acts and deceive others” (See: [[figs-123person]])

# 5:7
## xxs4
The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “because you are faithful to your covenant” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## wus9
This refers to God’s temple. Alternate translation: “your temple”

# 5:8
## nj5y
David speaks of righteousness as if it were a path and of teaching as leading. The phrase “your righteousness” means that God is righteous Alternate translation: “teach me to do what is righteous as you do” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## f99i
David speaks of righteousness as if it were a path. A straight path is easy to see or walk on. Alternate translation: “show me clearly how to live in the right way” or “make it easy for me to do what is right” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 5:9
## vyp8
See [[PSA-vyp8]]
## yu9i
Truth being in the mouth represents speaking truthfully. Alternate translation: “For they never say what is true” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## w7sn
The inward being represents people’s thoughts and desires. Alternate translation: “their thoughts and desires are wicked” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## t93l
The throat represents people’s speech. Alternate translation: “their speech” or “what they say” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## aj6l
Their throat is spoken of as if it were an open tomb, ready for dead bodies to put into it. Possible meanings are (1) “they say that they will kill people” or (2) “What they say kills people” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## c5lk
“they say nice things about people without really meaning it”

## w8tw
The tongue represents what people say. (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 5:10
## b8gr
“may their schemes cause them to experience disasters” or “may they become less important because of their schemes”

## llj1
plans to harm people

## se86
This is something that causes a person to experience disasters or to lose power. Experiencing disaster or becoming less important is spoken of as falling. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 5:11
## p2xk
God is spoken of as if he were a refuge, a place where people can be protected. Alternate translation: “May all those who go to you for protection rejoice” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## w32e
These two clauses express similar thoughts. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## h7eq
Going to Yahweh for protection is spoken of as taking refuge in him. Alternate translation: “go to you for protection” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## jnt7
God’s name represents him. Alternate translation: “those who love you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 5:12
## t1zz
God’s favor is spoken of as if it were a shield. Alternate translation: “you will favor them and protect them as a soldier protects himself with his shield” or “because you are kind to them, you will protect them (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 6:intro
## gpl3
See [[PSA-gpl3]]
# 6:1
## qy9s
See [[PSA-qy9s]]
## z78f
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## w19w
“people should play stringed instruments with this song”

## p2j3
This may refer to a style of music.

# 6:2
## at9c
The bones represent the whole body. His body may have been shaking because he was sick or extremely tired. Alternate translation: “my whole body is shaking” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 6:3
## sd1q
“terrified” or “worried”

## vw88
David uses this question to show that he does not want to continue feeling weak and troubled. Alternate translation: please, do not let this continue!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

# 6:4
## rce3
David speaks of God being kind to him as God returning to him. Alternate translation: “Yahweh, come back to me” or “Have mercy on me, Yahweh” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## fuw3
The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “Save me because you are faithful to your covenant” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 6:5
## qb7p
These two sentences express similar meanings. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## pn4j
The abstract noun “remembrance” represents praise. Alternate translation: “For when people die, they no longer praise you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## mb1j
David uses this question to emphasize that no one in Sheol thanks God. Alternate translation: “No one in Sheol will give you thanks!” or “The dead cannot praise you!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

# 6:6
## ge93
His groaning represents the pain or distress that he feels. Alternate translation: “I am very tired because of my pain” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## bay4
These two sentences express the same meaning. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## c1qb
“I make my bed wet with my tears” or “My bed is very wet because of my tears”

## isr5
“I make my couch wet with my tears”

# 6:7
## fup4
The ability to see is spoken of in terms of the eyes. Alternate translation: “My vision is blurry” or “I cannot see clearly” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## gny4
Grief here represents crying. Alternate translation: “from crying” or “because I cry so much” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 6:9
## j23z
These two lines have very similar meanings. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## dq36
Being willing to do what David has prayed for is spoken of as accepting his prayer. Alternate translation: “Yahweh will respond to my prayer” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 7:intro
## zey1
See [[PSA-zey1]]
# 7:1
## wzv4
See [[PSA-wzv4]]
## v239
“This is a song that David wrote”

## huv1
Going to Yahweh for protection is spoken of as taking refuge in him. Alternate translation: “go to you for protection!” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 7:2
## rzk1
David speaks of his enemies attacking him as if they would rip his body apart and tear it in pieces as a lion would. Alternate translation: “they will violently kill me like a lion ripping apart its victim’s body and tearing it in pieces” or “they will violently kill me” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## x9fh
“and no one else will be able to save me”

# 7:5
## ej18
The life represents the person. Alternate translation: “me” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## us9e
This represents capturing him. Alternate translation: “capture me” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## txr8
Here “my life” represents the writer. Alternate translation: “allow him to destroy me” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## hav6
This refers to lying dead and unburied in disgrace.

# 7:6
## phd3
Arising represents doing something or taking action. Alternate translation: “Do something in your anger” or “Be angry at my enemies and take action: (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## a9lp
Fighting against people is spoken of as standing up against them. Alternate translation: “fight against the rage of my enemies” or “attack my enemies who rage against me” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## q1qt
Their rage represents their attacks. Alternate translation: “the attacks of my enemies” or “my enemies who attack me” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## x2us
Waking up represents starting to do something or take action. Alternate translation: “Take action” or “Do something” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## sml1
“for me” or “to help me”

# 7:7
## pk8y
Here the word “countries” represents all of the armies that have gathered to attack. (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## rb6b
Ruling people is spoken of as being over them. Yahweh’s rightful place refers either to heaven or to ruling in general. Alternate translation: “Rule over them from heaven” or “Rule over them” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 7:8
## e8kb
“show them that I am not guilty”

# 7:9
## pw1n
“make the righteous people strong” or “make the righteous people prosper”

## zql9
The hearts and minds represent people’s desires and thoughts. Alternate translation: “you who know our inner thoughts” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 7:10
## c7u4
The word “shield” represents God’s protection. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 7:11
## j5zn
Who God is angry with can be stated explicitly. Alternate translation: “a God who is angry with the wicked every day” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 7:12
## y4zk
In verses 12 and 13, David speaks of God deciding to punish the wicked as if God were a warrior preparing to fight against them with weapons. Alternate translation: “God will take action against him like a warrior who sharpens his sword and prepares his bow for battle” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 7:14
## l54a
David speaks of the things that a wicked person does as if the person were pregnant and wickedness was the baby. Alternate translation: “the wicked person. He makes plans to destroy people and produces harmful lies” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 7:16
## p524
Destruction and violence are spoken of as if they hit a person’s head or fall down on it. Alternate translation: “His own destructive plans destroy him, for his violence attacks him” or “When he plans to destroy others, others destroy him; when he attacks others, others attack him” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 8:intro
## rs24
See [[PSA-rs24]]
# 8:1
## lk7t
See [[PSA-lk7t]]
## i9hb
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## ye1p
This may refer to a style of music.

## hn59
God’s “name” represents his whole being. Alternate translation: “people all over the world know that you are very great” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 8:2
## u11e
Possible meanings are (1) praise is spoken of as a solid object that God takes out of babies’ mouths and sets up as a defensive wall or (2) God has created the world so that true praise comes to him from babies. Alternate translation: “You have given babies and infants the ability to praise you” or “It is babies and infants who truly praise you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 8:3
## uj2i
God’s fingers represent him. Alternate translation: “the heavens which you have made” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 8:4
## yhh5
These remarks have been expressed in the form of a question to add emphasis. Alternate translation: “It is amazing that you think about people and are concerned about them!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## k9i2
Both of these phrases refer to people in general.

# 8:5
## sr48
Glory and honor are spoken of as if they were crowns. The words “glory” and “honor” are similar in meaning. Alternate translation: “have given them glory and honor” or “have caused them to be like kings” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-doublet]])

# 8:6
## x6z3
These two clauses express similar meanings. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## rc4e
“you make them … under their feet.” The words “him” and “his” here refer to people.

## xti1
The hands represent what God has done. Alternate translation: “the things that you made” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## py2w
Having authority to rule others or control things is spoken of as having them under one’s feet. This means God gave people authority over all that he created. Alternate translation: “you have given him authority over all things” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 8:9
## y339
With this exclamation, David shows his joy and awe about how great God is. Alternate translation: “your name is wonderfully magnificent in all the earth” or “people in all the earth know how magnificent you are” (See: [[figs-exclamations]])

## dvi7
God’s “name” represents him or his reputation. Alternate translation: “your reputation” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## bf2u
excellent, great

# 9:intro
## zq96
See [[PSA-zq96]]
# 9:1
## xxu5
See [[PSA-xxu5]]
## w9iy
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## nqw5
This may refer to a style of music.

## lr4k
Since this song is addressed to Yahweh, Yahweh can be referred to as “you.” Alternate translation: “Yahweh, I will give thanks to you with all my heart” (See: [[figs-123person]])

## f4r1
The noun “deeds” can be expressed with the verb “do.” Alternate translation: “all the marvelous things you do” or “all the marvelous things you have done” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 9:2
## vh6j
Here God’s name represents God. Alternate translation: “I will sing praise to you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 9:3
## j685
“retreat” or “flee in fear”

# 9:4
## nvz1
Kings had authority to judge people, and they would sit on their throne when they judged. David speaks as if God were an earthly king. Alternate translation: “you judge like a king who sits on his throne, and you are righteous” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 9:5
## cw1j
Causing people to be forgotten is spoken of as blotting out their name. Alternate translation: “you have caused them to be forgotten as if their name was blotted out” or “no one will ever remember them again” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## bs94
“erased”

# 9:6
## dj3h
The enemy is spoken of as if it were a city full of broken down buildings. Alternate translation: “Our enemies were destroyed” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## b9n1
“when you destroyed their cities”

## pi7j
Here “remembrance” is spoken of as if it were a living being that could die. Alternate translation: “All remembrance of them has stopped” or “There is no longer any remembrance of them” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## c6yp
The abstract noun “remembrance” can be expressed with the verb “remember.” Alternate translation: “No one remembers them at all” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 9:7
## x7xg
“Remain” probably represents sitting on the throne as king. Alternate translation: “Yahweh sits on his throne forever” or “Yahweh rules forever” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## h8nu
The phrase “his throne” represents God’s rule. Possible meanings are (1) “He rules in order to judge people” or (2) “He rules over people justly” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 9:8
## pgg5
These two clauses express the same meaning. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## dz3w
Here “the world” refers to all the people in the world. Alternate translation: “He will judge all the people of the world righteously” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 9:9
## y7hd
God is spoken of as if he were a place that people could go to for safety. Alternate translation: “Yahweh will also protect the oppressed” or “Yahweh will also provide safety for those who are oppressed” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 9:10
## mb1z
Here the words “your name” represent God. Alternate translation: “Those who know you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## dj61
“do not forsake” or “do not leave”

# 9:11
## nb7x
“who lives in Jerusalem”

## i7js
Here “the nations” represents the people of the nations. (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 9:12
## lcs5
What he remembers can be stated clearly. Alternate translation: “For the God who avenges bloodshed remembers those who were killed” or “For God remembers those who were killed and he punishes the killers” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## wk9a
“He does not ignore the cry”

# 9:13
## j8i9
This can be expressed in active form. Alternate translation: “see how those who hate me oppress me” or “see how badly my enemies treat me” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## p41p
Death is spoken of as if it were a city that had gates through which people enter it. If someone is near the gates of death, it means that he will die soon. Keeping someone from dying is spoken of as taking him away from the gates of that city. Alternate translation: “you who can rescue me from death” or “you who can keep me from dying” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 9:15
## re95
People dig pits so they can catch animals that fall into them. Here digging a pit represents making plans to destroy people. Alternate translation: “The nations are like people who dig a pit for others and then fall into it” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## g4gq
People hide nets so they can catch animals that get caught in them. Here hiding a net represents making plans to destroy people. Alternate translation: “they are like people who hide a net and get trapped in it” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 9:16
## fy3r
Here “wicked” is a nominal adjective that refers to any wicked person. A wicked person acting to harm other people is spoken of as if the wicked person had made a trap and then fallen into it and been unable to escape. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “when a wicked person tries to harm other people, his actions will end up harming him” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## z41t
“is trapped”

# 9:17
## bw3u
“rejected”

## wmb4
This refers to “the wicked.”

# 9:18
## f28n
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “God will not always forget the needy” or “God will remember the needy” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## ln7u
Hopes are spoken of as if they were objects that could be broken or destroyed. Hopes being destroyed represents the things that people hope for never happening. Alternate translation: “and the oppressed will not hope forever without results” or “and someday what the oppressed hope for will happen” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 9:19
## zrv7
Getting up represents starting to do something. Alternate translation: “Do something” or “Take action” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## dw6d
people

## f879
Here judging represents punishing. Alternate translation: “be punished” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## dca3
Here sight represents presence. Alternate translation: “in your presence” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## xin9
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “judge the nations in your presence” or “take the nations into your presence and punish them” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 10:intro
## h366
See [[PSA-h366]]
# 10:1
## he97
See [[PSA-he97]]
## l729
The speaker uses these questions to express his distress that God has not helped him. Alternate translation: “Yahweh, it seems as though you are far away from me and you hide from me whenever I am in trouble” (See: [[figs-rquestion]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 10:2
## ml6r
evil plans

# 10:3
## hd9r
This refers to wicked people in general. Alternate translation: “wicked people” (See: [[figs-genericnoun]])

## lk5v
The noun “desires” can be expressed with the verb “want. “Alternate translation: “the things that he wants very much to do” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## bcd9
“greedy people”

# 10:4
## nkz2
This refers here to wicked people in general. Alternate translation: “the wicked person” (See: [[figs-genericnoun]])

## es9w
A raised face represents pride or arrogance. Alternate translation: “has an arrogant attitude” or “is proud” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## je9x
Seeking God represents either (1) asking God for help or (2) thinking about God and obeying him. Alternate translation: “he does not ask God for help” or “he does not think about God” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 10:5
## h3lz
“He is safe at all times.” He is not really safe, but he thinks that he is.

## ee2m
Something that is hard to understand is spoken of as if it were too high to reach. Alternate translation: “he cannot understand your righteous decrees” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## bbt7
People snort at their enemies when they think that their enemies are weak and worthless. Alternate translation: “he thinks that all his enemies are weak and worthless” or “he sneers at all his enemies” (See: [[translate-symaction]])

## dxb3
This means that he blows air out noisily through his nose.

# 10:6
## j7qk
“The wicked man says”

## xus1
This probably simply means “forever.”

## y26y
Experiencing adversity is spoken of as meeting it. Alternate translation: “I will not have any troubles” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 10:7
## d42j
What people say is spoken of as being in their mouth. Alternate translation: “He always curses people, tells lies, and threatens to harm people” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## xj9b
Here the tongue represents speaking. Alternate translation: or “what he says injures and destroys people” or “he speaks words that threaten and hurt people” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 10:8
## x2zt
The word “he” refers to the wicked man.

## urg9
The eyes represent him. Alternate translation: “he looks for some helpless victim” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 10:9
## sd5u
This speaks of the wicked person as if he were a lion. Alternate translation: “He hides while he waits for the weak to walk near him, the same way a lion quietly waits in the bush for the animal it wants to attack” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## jkf7
This means to hide or wait with intent to harm or kill.

## ug79
“lies down waiting” or “he hides and waits”

## g5jl
The writer speaks of the wicked person catching people as if he were a hunter using a net to catch animals. Alternate translation: “He catches the oppressed like a hunter that catches an animal in a net and drags it away” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 10:10
## bcg4
The writer continues to speak of the wicked person catching people as if he were a hunter, his plans were nets, and the people were animals that fall into his net. Alternate translation: “his victims are caught by his plans like animals that fall into a hunter’s strong nets” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 10:11
## y4zx
The word “He” refers to the wicked person, and to wicked people in general. (See: [[figs-genericnoun]])

## ty8w
Refusing to pay attention to what people do is spoken of as forgetting. Alternate translation: “God does not pay attention” or “God does not care about what I do” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## vdi5
Refusing to pay attention to what someone does is spoken of as covering one’s face. Alternate translation: “God refuses to see what is happening” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## xd2r
Paying attention to what someone does is spoken of as looking at it. Alternate translation: “he will not bother to pay attention” or “he will not care” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 10:12
## l9k2
Starting to do something is spoken of as getting up. Alternate translation: “Do something” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## k3kx
Here lifting the hand to hit someone represents punishing him. Alternate translation: “Hit him hard” or “Punish the wicked person” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 10:13
## w9gj
The speaker uses this question to show that he is very sad that wicked people do these things. Alternate translation: “Wicked people are always rejecting God and saying … ‘You will not hold me accountable.’” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## tfq6
“You will not require me to tell you why I do what I do.” Holding someone accountable here represents punishing him. Alternate translation: “You will not punish me” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 10:15
## v9ju
Here “arm” represents power. Alternate translation: “Destroy the power of the wicked and evil man” or “Make the wicked and evil man weak” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## z4yy
These words have the same meaning. You can use one word to express both concepts. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## m5mv
Making someone account for his evil deeds represents punishing him. Alternate translation: “Punish him for the evil things he has done” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 10:16
## zc2f
This can be stated in active form. “Yahweh forces the people of other nations to leave his land” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 10:17
## d6nx
It is implied that the oppressed people cried out to God. Alternate translation: “when oppressed people cried out to you, you listened to them tell you what they need” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## yqz9
A strong heart represents courage, and making people’s hearts strong represents encouraging them. Alternate translation: “you encourage them” or “you make them confident” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 10:18
## w3s1
“no one … will cause people to be afraid again”

## w9wb

## ckb5
“faithful people have all vanished”

# 12:2
## p59u
The two occurrences of “everyone” are exaggerations, used to emphasize that this is true of very many people. (See: [[figs-hyperbole]])

## k6d8
Here “lips” is a metonym for what people say, and “a double heart” is a metaphor for deception. Alternate translation: “everyone speaks with flattering words and deception” or “everyone praises people falsely and tells lies” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 12:3
## cis2
Here “flattering lips” is a metonym for people who flatter others. Possible meanings are (1) “cut off” is a metaphor for killing. Alternate translation: “kill all who flatter others” or (2) “cut off” is a metaphor for stopping something. Alternate translation: “stop all those who flatter others” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

## g9k2
Here “every tongue” represents every person who declares great things. Alternate translation: “every person who boasts” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 12:4
## j1nx
Here the word “tongues” represents what people say. Alternate translation: “We will prevail because of what we say” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## ay1a
“we will succeed” or “we will win” or “we will be victorious”

## n8z2
Here the “lips” represents the people who speak. Alternate translation: “When we speak” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## le51
This rhetorical question is asked to emphasize that they believed no one could rule over them. It can be translated as a statement. Alternate translation: “no one can rule over us!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

# 12:5
## bgl1
These are deep sounds that people make because of pain or some strong emotion.

## qr86
This means Yahweh will do something to help the people.

## jt35
Yahweh’s words are compared to silver that has been purified. Alternate translation: “they are without any imperfection” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## txp6

## q4v9

## vsr8

## hwf6
“This is for the director of music to use in worship.”

## xg9c
This question is asked to get the reader’s attention and to add emphasis. It can be translated as a statement. Alternate translation: “Yahweh, it seems that you have forgotten about me!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## v3px
The words “your face” represent God’s whole being. This rhetorical question is asked to add emphasis. It can be translated as a statement. Alternate translation: “It seems like you are hiding from me!” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-rquestion]])

# 13:2
## pg6n

## x789

## t9hl
To “sleep in death” means to die. (See: [[figs-euphemism]])

# 13:4
## ucm3

## x5p1

# 13:5
## l1in
The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “I have trusted that you are faithful to your covenant” or “I have trusted you because you are faithful to your covenant” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## s3s4
Here “my heart” represents the whole person. Alternate translation: “I will rejoice because you have rescued me” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

This is an idiom that means to say to oneself or to think to oneself. Alternate translation: “A foolish person says to himself” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## r75x
The word “they” refers to all foolish human beings who say there is no God.

# 14:2
## zm7b
This phrase refers to all humans.

## vw7w
This describes those who desire to know God as if they were actually following him on a path. Alternate translation: “who desire to know him” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 14:3
## l4ef
This describes people who have rejected God as if they had stopped walking on the right path and had gone in another direction. Alternate translation: “They have all turned away from Yahweh” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 14:4
## v11h
This rhetorical question is asked to add emphasis. It can be translated as a statement. Alternate translation: “They act as if they do not know anything … who do not call on Yahweh. But they know what they are doing!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## a11q
The abstract nouns “iniquity” can be stated as “evil deeds.” Alternate translation: “those who do evil deeds” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## amq1
This refers to those who do evil things and destroy God’s people as if they were eating food. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 14:5
## g962
The word “they” refers to those who do evil things.

## p7fp
To say that “God is with” those who are righteous means that he helps them. This can be stated clearly in the translation. Alternate translation: “God helps those who act righteously” or “God helps those who do the right things” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 14:6
## a6ad
The word “you” here refers to the wicked people.

## eb9r
“to make the person who is poor feel ashamed”

## ysx7
This speaks of the protection that Yahweh provides as if he were a shelter that one might seek in a storm. Alternate translation: “Yahweh is like a shelter of protection to him” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 14:7
## uji3
This is an exclamation. The writer is saying what he wishes or longs for God to do. Alternate translation: “I wish so much that the salvation of Israel would come from Zion!” (See: [[figs-exclamations]])

## xxx6
Here “the salvation of Israel” is a metonym for Yahweh, the one who saves Israel. Alternate translation: “Oh, that Yahweh would come from Zion and save Israel!” or “I wish that Yahweh would come from Zion and rescue his people Israel!” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## h25q
These two phrases mean the same thing. Here both “Jacob” and “Israel” represent the people of Israel. The two phrases can be combined in the translation. Alternate translation: “then all the people of Israel will rejoice greatly” (See: [[figs-parallelism]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 16:3
## b6f8

# 16:4
## j4m1

## b7s4

## xj7h
Lifting up their names is a metaphor for praising them, and “lips” is a metonym for what one says. Alternate translation: “or praise them with my words” or “and I will not praise their gods” (See: [[figs-exmetaphor]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

# 16:5
## v4p8
Here David speaks of Yahweh as if he were a portion of land that has been given to him. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## b3bh
Here David speaks of Yahweh as if he were a cup that contains many blessings. Alternate translation: “the one who blesses me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## efb4
“You determine my future” or “You control what will happen to me”

# 16:6
## qf7f
Here laying down measuring lines is a metonym for measuring land and giving it to someone, and here this is a metaphor for God blessing David in many great ways. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “You have measured off land for me in pleasant places” or “You have given me land in pleasant places” or “You bless me like one who gives land in pleasant places” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

## ag3m
These are ropes that people use to measure a plot of land and mark its boundaries.

## af57
Here David speaks of Yahweh’s blessings as if they were an inheritance that he has received. Alternate translation: “I am delighted with all the things that he has given me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 16:8
## z682
“I always remember that Yahweh is with me”

# 16:9
## in9q
See [[PSA-in9q]]
## p2bc
Here the “heart” represents the speaker’s thoughts and emotions. Alternate translation: “Therefore I am glad” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## e6e1
Possible meanings are (1) the word “glory” represents the honor a person feels. Alternate translation: “I am honored to rejoice in God” or (2) the word translated “glory” really means “liver” and represents the speaker’s emotions. Alternate translation: “I am rejoicing”

# 16:11
## b54u
“great joy” or “a large amount of joy”

## hxq5
The writer speaks of “joy” as if it were a person. (See: [[figs-personification]])

## v4yr
The words “right hand” indicate being in God’s special presence. Alternate translation: “when I am near you” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 17:intro
## thd2
See [[PSA-thd2]]
# 17:1
## y32y
See [[PSA-y32y]]
## z6y3
The phrase “give ear” is a metaphor for listening, and “lips without deceit” is synecdoche for a person who does not lie. Alternate translation: “Listen to my prayer for I speak without deceit” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 17:2
## k4su
Vindication coming from God represents God judging someone and declaring him innocent. God’s “presence” is a metonym for God himself. Alternate translation: “Let my vindication come from you” or “Declare that I am innocent” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

## t9kx
Here “your eyes” is synecdoche for God himself, and “see” is a metaphor for paying attention and firmly deciding to do something. Alternate translation: “please see what is right” or “do what is right” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 17:3
## pi85
Here “test my heart” means to examine my thoughts and motives. Alternate translation: “If you examine my thoughts in the night” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## w51q
Here the mouth is spoken of as if it were capable of acting on its own. It also represents the words that a person speaks. Alternate translation: “I will not tell lies or sin with my words” (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 17:4
## u1m8
Here “the word of your lips” is a metonym for God’s instruction, and “the ways of the lawless” is a metaphor for the things that lawless people do. Alternate translation: “it is by obeying your instruction that I have kept myself from doing the things that lawless people do” or “your instruction has caused me to avoid doing wicked things” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 17:5
## nw8l
Both of these clauses mean the same thing. The repetition adds emphasis. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## ve61
The writer speaks of his obedience to God as if he were walking on a path. Alternate translation: “I am determined to follow your ways” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-litotes]])

# 17:6
## fh7p
These phrases mean the same thing. Here “your ear” refers to God’s willingness to hear someone who prays to him. Alternate translation: “pay attention to me … listen when I speak” (See: [[figs-parallelism]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

# 17:7
## m4v2
The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “Show in a wonderful way that you are faithful to your covenant” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## g2x5
The “right hand” refers to God’s power. Alternate translation: “your mighty power” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## ll6h
Going to Yahweh for protection is spoken of as taking refuge in him. Alternate translation: “go to you for protection” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 17:8
## ar64
The “apple of your eye” refers to something that is valuable. Alternate translation: “Protect me as you would something most valuable and precious” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## f3hh
David speaks of God’s protection as if he were a bird protecting its young under its wings. Alternate translation: “Keep me safe as a mother bird protects her babies by gathering them under her wing” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 17:10
## rd6l
Here “their mouths speak” represents his enemies when they speak. Alternate translation: “they speak with pride” or “they are always boasting” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 17:11
## yzx5
Here “surrounded my steps” represents how David’s enemies have followed him everywhere he goes in order to capture him. Alternate translation: “My enemies have surrounded me” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 17:12
## iq89
These two phrases express very similar ideas. The repetition adds intensity. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## c8wr
The writer feels pursued the way a lion hunts its prey (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 17:13
## p2s3
This is a metaphor for Yahweh’s power and for violent death in war. Alternate translation: “by having them die in war” or “by killing them in battle” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 17:14
## mf1x
This clause adds intensity to the words “Rescue my life from the wicked by your sword” ([Psalms 17:13](../017/013.md)). (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## wh2m
These words represent the power of Yahweh and add intensity to the words “by your sword” ([Psalms 17:13](../017/013.md)). (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## xg3n
The ancient text is hard to understand. Possible meanings are (1) “treasured” is a metaphor for loved, and “your treasured ones” refers to the people whom God loves. Alternate translation: “you will fill the bellies of the people you love with riches” or (2) “your treasured ones” refers to treasures that God gives to people, the “men of this world” Alternate translation: “you will fill their bellies with rich treasures” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## knu1
Here “fill the bellies … with riches” is a metaphor for giving them many valuable things. Possible meanings are (1) “You will give many riches to the people you love” or (2) “you will give the men of this world many riches” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 17:15
## ck39
Here “face” represents Yahweh in all of his being. David is confident he will see Yahweh. Alternate translation: “because I act in the right way, I will be with you one day” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## bpx8
David believes that after he dies, he will be with Yahweh. This can be made clear in the translation. Alternate translation: “After I die, I will be happy to wake up in your presence” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 18:intro
## enj7
See [[PSA-enj7]]
# 18:1
## xfk3
See [[PSA-xfk3]]
## ig1a
“This is for the director of music to use in worship.”

## vm1x
Possible meanings are (1) David wrote the psalm or (2) the psalm is about David or (3) the psalm is in the style of David’s psalms.

## p2da
“he sang this song to Yahweh”

## rhv3
“after Yahweh had rescued him”

## hna8
Here “hand” stands for the power of Saul. Alternate translation: “from Saul’s power” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 18:2
## tcf6
David speaks of Yahweh as if he were a rock. The word “rock” is a picture of a safe place. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## bmi2
Here the words “rock” and “fortress” share similar meanings and emphasize that Yahweh provides safety from enemies. (See: [[figs-doublet]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## v8xz
Going to Yahweh for protection is spoken of as taking refuge in him. Alternate translation: “go to him for protection” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## k49n
David speaks of Yahweh as if he were a “shield,” “the horn” of his salvation, and his “stronghold.” Yahweh is the one who protects him from harm. Here a similar idea is repeated three ways for emphasis. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 18:3
## d5g1
“I will be rescued from my enemies”

# 18:4
## fsd4
David speaks of death as if it were a person who could capture him and bind him with ropes. Alternate translation: “I was about to be killed” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-personification]])

## m5rx
David is as helpless as if he were being carried away by a rushing flood of waters. Alternate translation: “I felt completely helpless” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 18:5
## e9l1
Here “Sheol,” the place of the dead, and “death” are spoken of as if they were people who could surround and trap him. These two clauses have similar meanings and the idea is repeated for emphasis. Alternate translation: “I felt trapped and thought I was going to die” (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-parallelism]])

# 18:6
## s721
“In my great need” or “In my despair”

## jr71
Here David speaks of his “call for help” as if it were a person who could come into the presence of Yahweh. Alternate translation: “I prayed to him” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## fs4g
Here David speaks of how Yahweh heard his cry for help. The idea is repeated for emphasis. Alternate translation: “he heard my appeal” (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

# 18:7
## dal8
God’s being angry is spoken of as if the there was a terrible earthquake. Alternate translation: “God was so angry that it was as if the earth … shaken” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## xka3
The words “shook” and “trembled” mean basically the same thing and emphasize how greatly the earth shook. Alternate translation: “the land moved back and forth” or “the ground moved up and down” or “there was a violent earthquake” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## svs2
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “the foundations of the mountains also trembled and shook” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 18:8
## al4i
David speaks of Yahweh as if he were breathing fire. This is a picture of how angry God was. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## zsk4
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “blazing fire came out of his mouth and ignited coals” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 18:9
## fkd8
The word “He” refers to Yahweh.

## aw5e
Though Yahweh does not actually have feet, the Psalmist gives him human characteristics. Alternate translation: “thick darkness was beneath him” (See: [[figs-personification]])

# 18:10
## wt4l
Here the Psalmist speaks of the wind as if it had wings like an angel. (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 18:11
## a2gi
Here the words “He” and “him” refer to Yahweh.

## edg2
Here darkness is spoken of as if it were a tent. Alternate translation: “He made darkness a covering” or “He made darkness a hiding place” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## jnx8
“clouds heavy with rain” or “thick, dark rainclouds”

# 18:12
## t3xj
stones made of ice

# 18:13
## dn6a
Yahweh’s voice sounded like thunder. (See: [[figs-simile]])

## dvy3
“the Most High” refers to Yahweh.

# 18:14
## cw24
Both of these clauses have similar meanings. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## h2p3
Here lighting strikes are being spoken of as if they were arrows (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## p7tz
“sent them in different directions”

# 18:15
## b39a
See [[PSA-b39a]]
## jfu2
These two clauses have similar meanings. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “Then the water channels appeared and the bottom of the ocean became visible; you exposed the foundations of the world” (See: [[figs-parallelism]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

## a125
Though God does not have human physical characteristics as described here, this pictures his mighty strength. The wind is spoken of here as if it came as a mighty blast from God’s nostrils. (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 18:16
## m4pi
The word “He” in these verses refers to Yahweh.

## kef1
Here the Psalmist speaks of the dangers of his enemies as if they were huge waves or forceful waters, from which Yahweh has rescued him. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 18:18
## eej1
Here “They” refers to the strong enemies in verse 17.

## s1sk
The abstract noun “distress” can be stated as an adjective. The abstract noun “support” can be stated as “protected.” Alternate translation: “Strong enemies attacked me on a day when I was distressed, but Yahweh protected me” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 18:20
## a3vx
Here having clean hands represents being innocent of wrongdoing. Alternate translation: “I was innocent” or “my actions were right” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 18:21
## y3m6
The laws of Yahweh are spoken of as if they were the paths on which one should walk. Alternate translation: “I have obeyed Yahweh’s laws” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## tu8a
Here being wicked is spoken of as if one left the right path and took the wrong path. Alternate translation: “have not done wickedly by turning away from my God” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 18:22
## t97s
Both of these clauses have similar meanings. The writer repeats these ideas for emphasis. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## gtv3
“have guided me” or “I have remembered”

# 18:23
## gug9
“innocent according to him”

## gz4q
“I have not sinned”

# 18:24
## tu18
To have “clean hands” means that one is innocent of wrongdoing. See how you translated this in [Psalms 18:20](../018/020.md): Alternate translation: “I was innocent” or “my actions were right” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## t3bt
This refers to God’s presence. Alternate translation: “before him” or “according to him” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 18:25
## tb5y
See [[PSA-tb5y]]
## h851
Here “faithful” means to do what God commands one to do. You can state this clearly. Alternate translation: “to those who faithfully obey your commandments” or “to those who faithfully do your covenant” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 18:26
## cn7t
“you outwit anyone who is not honest”

# 18:27
## v6yq
“you humiliate”

## w4ji
This idiom refers to those who are proud. Alternate translation: “who are proud” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 18:28
## w4pi
The writer speaks of Yahweh’s presence as if he were a light. These clauses have similar meanings. (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-parallelism]])

# 18:29
## jv31
“For with your help I can cross any obstacle”

# 18:30
## v53y
A shield protects a soldier. David speaks as if God were a shield protecting him. See how you translated this in [Psalms 3:3](../003/003.md). Alternate translation: “You, Yahweh, protect like a shield everyone who takes refuge in you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 18:31
## d8xy
The implied answer is no one. Alternate translation: “Only Yahweh is God! Only our God is a rock!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## xn5i
David speaks of Yahweh as if he were a rock that he could climb to get away from his enemies. See how you translated this in [Psalms 18:2](../018/002.md). (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 18:32
## w9ef
God gives strength to David as if it were a piece of clothing. (See: [[figs-simile]])

## z4ka
Here David speaks of living a life that is pleasing to God as if he were being placed on the right path. Alternate translation: “causes the blameless person to live a righteous life” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 18:33
## w92y
This refers to enabling a person to run fast. Alternate translation: “makes me run very fast” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## g696
The deer is especially quick and stable in the mountains. (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 18:34
## q1v4
Here “my hands” refers to the person. Alternate translation: “He trains me” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## tq4k
This refers to the person. Alternate translation: “me” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 18:35
## juz2
Here the writer speaks of God’s protection as if it were a shield. The abstract noun “salvation” can be stated with the verb “save.” Alternate translation: “your protection and saved me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## x6rm
Here God’s right hand represents his power. Alternate translation: “Your power has supported me” or “You have supported me by your power” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## yr5f
Here God’s favor represents him acting according to his favor. Alternate translation: “You have made me great according to your favor” or “By your kindness, you have made me great” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 18:36
## ui92
The writer speaks of the safety that God has provided as if it were a wide place for him to stand. Here “my feet” represent the person. Alternate translation: “a safe place for me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

## qhq7
Here “my feet” refers to the person. The writer refers to the safety of God’s protection as if he were standing on a place where he will not slip or fall. Alternate translation: “I have not slipped” or “I am doing well” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 18:38
## v638
“I crushed them” or “I broke them to pieces”

## z8w8
“unable to stand”

## af9q
This idiom means the Psalmist has defeated his enemies. Alternate translation: “I have defeated all of them” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 18:39
## t3xr
The Psalmist says that Yahweh has given him strength that surrounds and supports him like a belt. See how you translated this in [Psalms 18:32](../018/032.md). (See: [[figs-simile]])

## xyh3
Here the Psalmist speaks of the defeat of his enemies as if he were standing on them. Alternate translation: “you defeat for me” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## xyp2
This refers to those who oppose the Psalmist. Alternate translation: “those who are my enemies” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 18:40
## h5yv
This represents God giving David victory over his enemies. Alternate translation: “You gave me victory over my enemies” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## m3tx
This represents God giving David victory over his enemies. Possible images are (1) David could cut his enemies’ heads off at the neck or (2) David could put his foot down on his enemies’ necks or (3) David could see his enemies’ backs when they ran away from him. (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## gp8b
“I defeated those who hated me” or “I destroyed completely those who hated me”

# 18:41
## whl5
This means Yahweh did not provide any help. Alternate translation: “but he did not help them” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 18:42
## tjm8
The psalmists enemies are compared to dust to show how defeated they are. (See: [[figs-simile]])

## vu6f
The psalmist’s enemies are compared to mud in the streets to show how defeated they are. (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 18:43
## t95d
disagreements, arguments

## i9s6
Here “head” represents the ruler. Alternate translation: “appointed me to be the ruler over many nations” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 18:44
## c7dv
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “God forced foreigners to bow” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 18:45
## t4uc
Here “trembling” shows that they were very afraid. This can be stated clearly in the translation. Alternate translation: “foreigners came shaking, showing that they were very afraid” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 18:46
## w5z5
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “he is my rock and he should be praised” or “may people praise my rock” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## mv1z
Here the writer speaks of Yahweh’s protection as if he were a rock that prevented his enemies from reaching him. See how you translated this in [Psalms 18:2](../018/002.md). (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## h9ey
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “May people exalt the God of my salvation” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## xf2h
The abstract nouns “salvation” can be stated as “saved” or “rescued.” Alternate translation: “the God who rescued me” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 18:47
## v7ab
To “execute vengeance” means to punish people for their evil actions. This can be restated to remove the abstract noun “vengeance.” Alternate translation: “the God who punishes people for the evil things they have done to me” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 18:48
## l9y3
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “God has set me free” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## z54b
Yahweh’s protection of the writer is spoken of as if he lifted the writer up so high that his enemies could not reach him to harm him. Alternate translation: “you put me in a safe place high above” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## k73f
“who attacked me” or “who rebelled against me”

## inl3
“cruel men” or “savage men”

# 18:49
## f8x9
Here the writer means that he will give thanks to Yahweh so that all people will hear of Yahweh’s greatness. Alternate translation: “so all the nations will hear about it” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## qvh1
Here “name” represents God himself. Alternate translation: “in honor of your name” or “to you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 18:50
## ggt6
By using the words “his king,” David is referring to himself as king. (See: [[figs-123person]])

## sw5u
“he faithfully loves me as he promised in his covenant, and he will love my descendants forever”

# 19:intro
## sn29
See [[PSA-sn29]]
# 19:1
## s9h1
See [[PSA-s9h1]]
## j4zh
“This is for the director of music to use in worship.”

## mn6q
The heavens are described as if they were a person. Alternate translation: “The heavens show” or “The heavens look like they declare”

## iz5q
The skies are described as if they were a teacher. Alternate translation: “The skies seem to make God’s handiwork known to us” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## a8iy
“his creation” or “the world that he has made”

# 19:2
## c72h
What is beautiful about creation is compared to speaking, as if creation were a person. Then those words are compared to water that flows everywhere. Alternate translation: “creation is like a person speaking to everyone” (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 19:3
## lmv7
These phrases express clearly that the first two verses were a metaphor. Alternate translation: “There is no real speech or spoken words; no one hears an actual voice with their ears”

## pa4x
Other translations read “where their voice is not heard,” emphasizing that creation’s “speech” is available everywhere.

# 19:4
## w3s6
See [[PSA-w3s6]]
## c2us
This refers to the unspoken “words” of creation that show God’s glory.

## r4zj
The words are described as if they were people who go out with a message. Alternate translation: “the words that creation speaks are like people who go out” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## kf9h
The implied words can be included in the translation. Alternate translation: “their speech goes out to the end of the world” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

## bdz7
Here the writer speaks of the place that Yahweh created for the sun as if it were a tent. Alternate translation: “He created a place for the sun” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## n177
The word “them” probably refers to the heavens.

# 19:5
## s244
The writer speaks of the sun’s coming out as if it were a bridegroom. Alternate translation: “The sun is like a bridegroom walking joyfully toward his bride” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## xes3
This compares the sun to an athlete to emphasize the strength and brightness of the sun. (See: [[figs-simile]])

## l7b8
“a fast runner”

# 19:6
## tah2
the line where the earth and the sky meet

## wz8h
Here “other” refers to the other horizon. This can be stated clearly in the translation. Alternate translation: “to the other horizon” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## unx8
This can be stated in positive form. Alternate translation: “everything feels its heat” (See: [[figs-doublenegatives]])

# 19:7
## z9pg
The words “the soul” refer to the whole person. Alternate translation: “making a person strong again” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## a789
“those who have no experience” or “those who have not learned”

# 19:8
## spr1
These words refer to the whole person. Alternate translation: “a person” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## nuk1
“are true” or “are correct”

## t8c5
Possible meanings are (1) “bringing understanding to a person” or (2) “making a person healthy again”

# 19:9
## xac8
“completely right”

# 19:10
## x983
Yahweh’s decrees are spoken of as if they could be bought and tasted. Alternate translation: “If you could buy them, they would be of greater value than gold … if you could taste them, they would be sweeter than honey” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## e6s3
The word “valuable” is understood from the previous phrase and can be repeated. Alternate translation: “even more valuable than a lot of fine gold” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

## k6x4
“pure gold” or “expensive gold”

# 19:11
## y6a9
This word marks that there is more to the truth than what has just been said. Alternate translation: “Moreover”

## s1f4
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “they warn your servant” or “they are a warning for your servant” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## e73b
The word “them” refers to Yahweh’s righteous decrees.

## nk1k
David calls himself “your servant” when speaking to God as a sign of respect. Alternate translation: “I am warned” (See: [[figs-123person]])

# 19:12
## uj5e
This appears in the form of a question to add emphasis and can be translated as a strong statement. Alternate translation: No one can be aware of his own errors!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## gsx9
“from secret mistakes I have made”

# 19:13
## j82u
This idiom pictures the servant as being removed from the sins he does not wish to commit. Alternate translation: “Also, protect your servant from doing” or “Also, make sure that I do not commit” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## z1tt
David calls himself “your servant” when speaking to God as a sign of respect. See how you translated this in [Psalms 19:11](../019/011.md). Alternate translation: “I” (See: [[figs-123person]])

## b3bd
Sins are described as if they were a king that could rule over someone. Alternate translation: “do not let my sins become like a king who rules over me” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## axe2
“innocent of rebelling against you” or “innocent of committing many sins”

# 19:14
## l16r
These expressions taken together describe everything a person says and thinks. Alternate translation: “the things I say and the things I think about” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## t28d
“receive approval in your sight” or “be pleasing to you”

## bu1w
Here sight represents judgment or evaluation. Alternate translation: “in your judgment” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## vn8k
The writer speaks of God as if he were a rock that one could climb and be protected from his enemies. Alternate translation: “Yahweh, you are like my rock” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 20:intro
## h99t
See [[PSA-h99t]]
# 20:1
## v6pl
See [[PSA-v6pl]]
## h9gw
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## vrb5
The word “you” in this Psalm is singular and refers to the king.

## pt3b
“in times of trouble” or “when you are in trouble”

## dp3k
Possible meanings are (1) here “name” is a metonym for God’s power. Alternate translation: “may the power of the God of Jacob protect you” or “may the God of Jacob protect you by his power” or (2) here “name” is a metonym for God himself. Alternate translation: “may the God of Jacob protect you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 20:2
## b9ek
God helping from his holy place is spoken of as if God were sending help. Alternate translation: “may Yahweh help you from his holy place” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## y51h
Both of these refer to God’s temple in Jerusalem. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 20:3
## yz44
The phrase “call to mind” is a way of saying “remember.” It does not mean God forgot. It means to consider or think about. Alternate translation: “May he remember” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## kyh3
The word “he” refers to Yahweh.

# 20:4
## r6y3
“May he give”

## wht8
Here “heart” stands for the entire person. The abstract noun “desire” can be stated as a verb. Alternate translation: “what you desire” or “what you want” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## u619
The abstract noun “plans” can be stated as a verb. Alternate translation: “may he help you to accomplish everything that you plan to do” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 20:5
## h4h3
Here “we” refers to the people. They will rejoice in the king’s victory. (See: [[figs-exclusive]])

## bw3j
Here “name” represents honor or reputation. Alternate translation: “in honor of our God” or “for the reputation of our God” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## p9n1
“we will raise victory flags.” They would do this to show that they were praising God because he gave their king victory over his enemies. (See: [[translate-symaction]])

## k3dy
“give you everything you request from him”

# 20:6
## zm9a
This word is used here to mark a break in the psalm. It transitions from the people speaking to the king speaking.

## nu7b
The word “I” probably refers to the king who is speaking in this section.

## d8xz
The king is speaking about himself in the third person. This can be stated in first person. Alternate translation: “me, his anointed one … answer me … rescue me” (See: [[figs-123person]])

## bd3g
God dwells in heaven as well as in the temple in Jerusalem ([Psalms 20:2](../020/002.md)).

## xcm6
God’s right hand represents his power. Alternate translation: “with his great strength he will rescue him” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 20:7
## f9cd
Here “chariots” and “horses” represent a king’s army. (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## xr24
The word “trust” is understood. Alternate translation: “other trust in horses” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

## mwu6
Here “we” refers to the writer and the readers. (See: [[figs-exclusive]])

# 20:8
## e7uq
Here “we” refers to the writer and the readers. (See: [[figs-exclusive]])

## q1tp
The word “They” refers to the people who trust in chariots and horses. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “God will bring them down and make them fall” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## g7uv
Both these verbs mean basically the same thing. Both of these stand for losing in battle. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## y7lr
“we will get up and stand up straight.” These two phrases mean basically the same thing. Both of these stand for victory in battle. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 20:9
## c5i4
Possible interpretations are (1) the people ask God to protect the king or (2) the king continues to speak about himself in the third person.

## brk5
Some translations understand the Hebrew differently. Some translate it as the people speaking to Yahweh their king. Alternate translation: “King, help us when we call you”

# 21:1
## k12k
