## h69b
“This is for the director of music to use in worship.”

## bt8s
It is implied that this is strength Yahweh has given the king to defeat his enemies. Alternate translation: because you, Yahweh, have made him strong enough to defeat his enemies”

## bka2
“He rejoices greatly”

## r5nd
It is implied that God has saved the king from his enemies. The abstract noun “salvation” can be stated as a verb. Alternate translation: “because you have saved him from his enemies” (See: [[figs-explicit]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 21:2
## cey2
“his heart’s wish.” Here “heart” stands for the whole person. Alternate translation: “his desire” or “what he wished for” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## gez6
“have not refused him.” This can be stated in positive form. Alternate translation: “you have given him” (See: [[figs-doublenegatives]])

## f8dh
Here “lips” stands for the whole person. Alternate translation: “his request” or “what he requested of you” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 21:3
## q3ts
The abstract noun “blessings” can be stated as “bless” or “good things.” Alternate translation: “you bless him greatly” or “you give him many good things” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## px6p
To place a crown on a person’s head is a symbol of making him a king. (See: [[translate-symaction]])

## za3g
Here “purest gold” represents the great honor given to the king.

# 21:4
## yzs5
The abstract noun “life” can be stated as a verb. Alternate translation: “He asked that you cause him to live for a long time; you caused it to happen” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## y4ml
The idiom “the length of his days” refers to the duration of his life. Alternate translation: “a long life that lasts forever” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 21:5
## i6i4
“The king’s honor” or “The king’s fame”

## k3gt
“you have placed on him splendor and majesty.” Causing the king to be wealthy and powerful is spoken of as if splendor and majesty are objects that are placed on him. Alternate translation: “you have made him wealthy and powerful” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 21:6
## w2zk
“you allow him to have” or “you agree to give him”

## rf4f
“a blessings that will last” or “a blessings that will stay”

## v3m2
“the joy of being in your presence” or “the joy that comes from you being near to you”

# 21:7
## mbf3
The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “because the Most High is faithful to his covenant” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## j1gh
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “no one will remove him as king” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 21:8
## w7ck
Here “hand” represents power. Alternate translation: “Your power will seize” or “You will powerfully seize” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## irz4
Possible meaning of all occurrences of “your” and “you” are (1) they refer to the king or (2) they refer to God.

## yew7
This means the same thing as the first part of the sentence. It emphasizes that God will give the king the power to stop his enemies. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

# 21:9
## lmc9
“When you are angry and begin to act”

## hhy3
The words “your” and “you” refers to either (1) God or (2) the king.

## xdq2
Yahweh or the king destroying their enemies is spoken of as if their enemies are wood and Yahweh or the king will throw them into a furnace. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## fc6d
Both clauses mean basically the same thing. Yahweh completely destroying his enemies is spoken of as if his wrath is a fire that completely burns up his enemies. (See: [[figs-parallelism]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 21:10
## wsu5
The word “you” refers to either (1) God or (2) the king.

## i3zy
Both phrases mean the same thing. They emphasize that absolutely none of their enemies will survive. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

# 21:11
## fhu8
“they planned.” The word “they” refers to the enemies of God and the king.

## z63c
“to do evil things to you”

## h29d
“they made a plan” or “they created a scheme”

# 21:12
## bsd1
Possible meanings for “you” and “your” are (1) they refer to the king or (2) they refer to God and speak about him as if he were a warrior with a bow and arrows. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ti25
This is a way of saying that God and the king will defeat their enemies in battle. (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## ge87
This implies that he actually shoots his arrows at his enemies. (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 21:13
## aul7
Possible meanings are (1) “Yahweh, show us that you are very strong” or (2) “Yahweh, because you are strong we will exalt you”

## w52b
The words “sing” and “praise” share similar meanings. Here the word “power” represents God and his power. Alternate translation: “with singing we will praise you because you are powerful” (See: [[figs-doublet]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

# 22:intro
## y7hl
See [[PSA-y7hl]]
# 22:1
## lw3l
See [[PSA-lw3l]]
## k951
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## ux16
This may refer to a style of music.

## smt9
The writer repeats “My God” to emphasize that he is desperate for God to hear him.

## a733
The writer uses a question to emphasize that he feels like God has abandoned him. It may be best to leave this as a question. It can also be translated as a statement. Alternate translation: “my God, I feel like you have abandoned me!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## z48u
“you left me all alone”

## fnk8
Again the writer uses a question to emphasize that he feels like God is far away from him. It may be best to leave this as a question. It can also be translated as a statement. Alternate translation: “You are far from saving me and far from the words of my anguish!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## y7ec
The writer feeling like God is not listening to him is spoken of as if God were far from his words of anguish. Alternate translation: “why do you not listen when I speak to you about the anguish I feel” or “I have told you about my suffering but you do not come to me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 22:2
## dzu2
The writer uses the words “daytime” and “night” to mean he prays to God all the time. (See: [[figs-merism]])

## j5c4
This can be stated in positive form. Alternate translation: “I still speak” (See: [[figs-litotes]])

# 22:3
## zle3
“the praises of Israel are the throne on which you sit as king.” The praises of Israel are described as if they are a throne upon which God can sit and rule, or as a house in which God can live. Alternate translation: “you are king and the people of Israel praise you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## viy1
Here “Israel” represents the people of Israel. (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 22:5
## u4pd
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “you did not disappoint them” or “you did not fail them” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## vjq8
This can be stated in positive form. Alternate translation: “you saved them” or “you did for them what they needed you to do” (See: [[figs-doublenegatives]])

# 22:6
## m3yz
The writer speaks of himself as if he were a worm. This emphasizes that he feels worthless or that the people treat him as if he were worthless. Alternate translation: “But it is like I am a worm and not a man” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## xml4
Both of these phrase mean basically the same thing. The phrase “despised by the people” can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “everyone thinks I am worthless and the people hate me” (See: [[figs-parallelism]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

# 22:7
## gq6v
These three phrases share similar meanings and emphasize how much people disrespect him. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## nu8j
This describes an action used to mock someone. (See: [[translate-symaction]])

# 22:8
## v7ta
The people are saying this to mock the writer. They do not really believe Yahweh will rescue him. (See: [[figs-irony]])

## ip8x
“Let Yahweh rescue him”

## h2ys
Possible meanings are (1) “for Yahweh delights in him” or (2) “for he delights in Yahweh”

# 22:9
## lz9a
The writer uses the word “For” to begin explaining why he is confused and asking God why he is not coming to help. (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## g6i1
This is a way of saying “you caused me to be born.” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## h37n
This means that he has been trusting in Yahweh since he was very young. Alternate translation: “even from the time that I drank milk from my mother’s breasts” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 22:10
## ua28
The phrase “have been thrown on” is a way of saying that Yahweh has taken care of him as if Yahweh had adopted him as his own child. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “It was as though you had adopted me right when I was born” (See: [[figs-idiom]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

## qi4n
This implies that Yahweh has always taken care of the writer. Alternate translation: “you, God, have taken care of me” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## bd6c
“since before I was born”

# 22:11
## tz1y
This can be stated in positive form. Alternate translation: “Come close to me” (See: [[figs-litotes]])

## mc7w
The writer speaks about “trouble” as if it were an object that is near him. Alternate translation: “for my enemies are near me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## sub2
“there is no helper”

# 22:12
## e14p
The writer speaks about his enemies as if they were bulls. This emphasizes how dangerous and powerful his enemies are. Alternate translation: “I have many enemies and they are like bulls that surround me; they are like strong bulls from Bashan that surround me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-parallelism]])

# 22:13
## tfu9
The writer speaks about his enemies as if they were lions with the mouths open ready to eat him. His enemies may be speaking lies to discredit him. Or they may be threatening him and attacking him. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## qv8i
The writer speaks about his enemies as if they were lions. This emphasizes how powerful and dangerous his enemies are. (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 22:14
## q64m
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “It is like someone is pouring me out like water” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## d2h5
The writer speaks about feeling completely exhausted and weak as if he were water being poured out of a jar. (See: [[figs-simile]])

## pjf3
“all my bones are out of place.” It is possible the writer is in some kind of physical pain. Or he may be speaking of his emotional pain as if it were physical pain. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ws5l
The writer speaks about no longer having courage as if his heart melted like wax. Here “heart” represents “courage.” (See: [[figs-simile]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

## y32r
a soft substance that melts at a relatively low temperature

## k6ki
“inside of me”

# 22:15
## fpb6
The writer speaks about feeling weak as if his strength were like a dry piece of pottery that can easily break. (See: [[figs-simile]])

## w7be
an object made of baked clay that can be used in the house

## g95x
“my tongue sticks to the top of my mouth.” The writer may be describing his extreme thirst. Or he may be continuing to speak about being weak as if he were completely dry. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## z793
Possible meanings for “dust of death” are (1) it refers to a person turning to dust after they die. Alternate translation: “You are about to let me die and become dust” or (2) it is a way of speaking about the grave, which would mean God is causing the writer to die. Alternate translation: “You have laid me in my grave” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## m487
The “you” is singular and refers to God. (See: [[figs-you]])

# 22:16
## un7f
The writer speaks about his enemies as if they were dogs. His enemies are coming close to him like wild dogs do to a dying animal. Alternate translation: “my enemies are like dogs that have surrounded me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## np5i
“a group of evildoers” or “a gang of evildoers”

## i2n1
stood in a circle

## x42c
This continues the dog metaphor. The writer speaks about his enemies as if they were dogs that are biting and piercing his hands and feet with their teeth. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ai5d
stabbed through something with a sharp object

# 22:17
## est5
Possible meanings are (1) the writer is so thin that he can see his bones. Alternate translation: “I can see all of my bones” or “I can feel each of my bones” or (2) this continues the dog metaphor and the writer can see his bones after the dogs have ripped his flesh. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ce23
The words “look” and “stare” mean basically the same thing and emphasize that people look at him awkwardly and make fun of him. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 22:18
## fb7u
“my clothes”

# 22:19
## v12t
This can be stated in positive form. Alternate translation: “Be very close” (See: [[figs-litotes]])

## y71k
Here “strength” represents Yahweh who gives him strength. Alternate translation: “you who give me strength” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 22:20
## ly82
Here “soul” stands for the whole person. Alternate translation: “Rescue me” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## a8wk
The sword is a common way of referring to a violent enemy. Alternate translation: “those who want to kill me” or “my enemies” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## li5b
“my precious life” or “the only life I have”

## a1qv
The writer speaks about his enemies as if they were dogs to emphasize how dangerous his enemies are. Also, the claws stand for the animals as a whole in a synecdoche. The writer emphasizes this part of the animal because it is what the animals would use to kill someone. (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

## h8vu
The word “wild” here means that no one has captured and tamed the animal.

# 22:21
## vl96
The writer speaks about his enemies as if they were lions and wild oxen to emphasize how dangerous his enemies are. Also, the mouth and horns stand for the animals as a whole in a synecdoche. The writer emphasizes these parts of the animals because they are what the animals would use to kill someone. (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

## wgw6
The word “wild” here means that no one has captured and tamed the animal.

# 22:22
## vq9v
“I will make known your name.” Here “name” stands for God’s character or reputation. Alternate translation: “I will talk about your character” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## k6ii
Here “brothers” means “my fellow Israelites” or “my fellow worshipers of Yahweh”

## t5p8
“when my fellow Israelites and I gather together” or “when I am surrounded by my fellow worshipers of Yahweh”

# 22:23
## wl3v
Here “You” is plural. (See: [[figs-you]])

## yc8l
Both of these refer to the same group of people. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## rs9u
“Be full of awe for him” or “Let God’s power amaze you”

# 22:24
## t6pw
Possible meanings are (1) he has not despised the afflicted one because he is suffering or (2) he has not belittled the suffering of the afflicted one

## q54x
These two words mean basically the same thing and emphasize that God has not forgotten the one who is afflicted and suffering. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## w7tf
strongly disliked or hated

## h5t5
Here, suffering is a metonym for the person who suffers. To abhor something is to think of it as horrible. Alternate translation: “he has not … thought of the afflicted one who suffers as horrible” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## y2dq
Possible meanings are (1) the author was speaking about how God treats people who are suffering. Alternate translation: “those who suffer … from them … those who are suffering cried” or (2) the author was speaking specifically about how God treated him. Alternate translation: “my suffering because of my affliction … from me … I cried” (See: [[figs-genericnoun]] and [[figs-123person]])

## r4zy
Hiding one’s face from someone represents ignoring him. Alternate translation: “has not turned his attention away from him” or “has not ignored him” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## fci1
“he listened.” It is implied that he responded when he heard their cry. Alternate translation: “he answered” or “he helped” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 22:25
## q298
Here “you” refers to Yahweh. (See: [[figs-you]])

## w4ny
This refers to sacrifices the writer promised to offer to God. (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## zq18
Here “him” refers to Yahweh. It can be stated as “you.” Alternate translation: “in the presence of those who fear you” (See: [[figs-123person]])

# 22:26
## fhl9
This refers to the fellowship meal which occurs after the writer offers to God the sacrifices that he promised. He will invite those who were suffering to eat a part of the animal he sacrificed. (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## jvb2
Those who want to know Yahweh and please him are spoken of as if they are literally seeking to find Yahweh. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## x7ys
Here “hearts” represent the whole person. Alternate translation: “May you live forever” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## lv3f
Here “your” is plural and refers to the oppressed people. (See: [[figs-you]])

# 22:27
## sti4
Starting to obey Yahweh is spoken of as if the people physically turn toward Yahweh. Alternate translation: “will remember Yahweh and obey him” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## s5k2
This means the same thing as the first part of the sentence. The writer is emphasizing that everyone from every place will worship and obey Yahweh. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## ves3
This is a sign of giving honor and respect to someone. (See: [[translate-symaction]])

## n554
Here “you” refers to Yahweh. It can be translated in the third person to match the first part of the sentence. Alternate translation: “before him” (See: [[figs-you]] and [[figs-123person]])

# 22:28
## yp9r
“For the kingdom belongs to Yahweh.” Here “kingdom” represents God’s rule as king. Alternate translation: “For Yahweh is king” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## y3zn
Here “nations” represents the people of the nations. Alternate translation: “he rules the people of the nations” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 22:29
## pb3y
The people will eat together at the feast. Alternate translation: “will eat together” or “will eat a festive meal together”

## b7d2
Both phrases refers to the same group. They both refer to all people because all people will die. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## fkt1
Here “dust” represents the grave. The phrase “descending into the dust” is a way of referring to someone dying. Alternate translation: “those who are dying” or “those who die” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-idiom]])

## wbb7
“those who cannot save their own lives” or “those who cannot keep themselves from dying”

# 22:30
## tak2
Here “A generation” represents the people of a generation. The phrase “to come” speaks about a future time as if it were something that travels and arrives somewhere. Alternate translation: “People in the future generations” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## l73k
Here “generation” represents the people of that generation. Alternate translation: “the people of the next generation” or “their children” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## j95t
“about the Lord” or “about what the Lord has done”

# 22:31
## lt28
The abstract noun “righteousness” can be stated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “tell of the righteous things he has done” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 23:intro
## r1f6
See [[PSA-r1f6]]
# 23:1
## h1x8
See [[PSA-h1x8]]
## t39n
The writer speaks about Yahweh as if he were a shepherd. This emphasizes how God cares for people as a shepherd cares for his sheep. Alternate translation: “Yahweh is like a shepherd to me” or “Yahweh cares for me as a shepherd cares for his sheep” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## gb7q
This can be stated in positive form. Alternate translation: “I have everything that I need” (See: [[figs-litotes]])

# 23:2
## ez87
The writer speaks about himself as if he were a sheep, and he speaks about Yahweh as if he were a shepherd. Alternate translation: He gives me rest like a shepherd who leads his sheep to lie down in green pastures” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## p2p4
The writer speaks about himself as if he were a sheep, and he speaks about Yahweh as if he were a shepherd. Alternate translation: “he provides what I need like a shepherd who leads his sheep beside tranquil water” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## l7sx
“calm water” or “water that flows gently.” This water is safe to drink.

# 23:3
## jdm7
See [[PSA-jdm7]]
## ic3m
This means God makes a person who is weak and tired to be strong and rested again.

## nx5d
Showing a person how to live in a way that pleases God is spoken of as if it were a shepherd showing a sheep the right path to take. Alternate translation: “He shows me how to live right” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ta7y
The phrase “his name” here refers to his reputation. Alternate translation: “for his reputation” or “so that people will honor him” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 23:4
## a7b6
See [[PSA-a7b6]]
## fi66
The writer describes a person experiencing terrible trouble as if he were a sheep walking through a dark and dangerous valley. There a sheep could get lost or attacked by a wild animal. Alternate translation: “Though my life is like walking through a dark and dangerous valley” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## me3c
The abstract noun “harm” can be stated as a verb. Alternate translation: “I will not be afraid of something harming me” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## hqa2
Here “you” refers to Yahweh. (See: [[figs-you]])

## yre6
The rod and staff represent protection because shepherds use them to protect their sheep from danger. Alternate translation: “I am not afraid because you protect me like a shepherd who protects his sheep with his rod and staff” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 23:5
## ksk5
See [[PSA-ksk5]]
## nqn4
A table represents a feast because people would put all the food on a table. (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## b3bs
The meaning here is that the writer is not worried about his enemies because he is an honored guest of the Lord and therefore protected from harm. Alternate translation: “despite the presence of my enemies”

## hh1r
People sometimes put oil on their guests’ heads in order to honor them.

## w1iw
Here a cup of wine that overflows represents many blessings. Alternate translation: “You fill my cup so much that it overflows” or “You give me many blessings” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 23:6
## y8zc
Yahweh being good and faithful to a person is spoken of as if goodness and covenant faithfulness are things that pursue after a person. The abstract nouns “goodness” and “faithfulness” can be translated as adjectives. Alternate translation: “Surely you will be good and faithful to me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## ep2g
The abstract noun “life” can be stated as a verb. Alternate translation: “as long as I live” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## u2bl
Possible meanings are that (1) this refers to Yahweh’s eternal home, or (2) this refers to Yahweh’s temple in Jerusalem. If possible, translate it so that both meanings could be understood.

## u53m
This idiom refers to the duration of his life. Alternate translation: “as long as I live” or “forever” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 24:intro
## cw5j
See [[PSA-cw5j]]
# 24:1
## nne9
See [[PSA-nne9]]
## hma5
The abstract noun “fullness” can be stated with the verb “fills.” Alternate translation: “everything that fills it” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 24:2
## v6lt
Here “founded it upon the seas” and “established it on the rivers” mean basically the same thing. The Hebrews of that time believed their land was supported by the oceans and deep underground rivers. Alternate translation: For he formed its foundation on the seas and built it on the deep waters” (See: [[figs-parallelism]] and [[figs-explicit]])

## d2bq
These phrases are used together to refer to the huge deep ocean below the earth.

## h6kl
“the water that is deep below”

# 24:3
## e3ya
Both of these questions mean basically the same thing. The speaker is asking about who is allowed to go and worship Yahweh. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## bda3
“will go up” or “will climb”

## mz8v
This refers to Mount Zion in Jerusalem.

## vj27
This refers Yahweh’s temple. His temple is on Mount Zion in Jerusalem.

# 24:4
## g1lm
Here “He” does not refer to a specific person. Alternate translation: “Those who have … who have … and have not” (See: [[figs-genericnoun]])

## vsk8
The word “hands” represents what a person does. For his “hands” to be clean means he does what is right. Alternate translation: “who does what is right” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## ikc9
Here “heart” represents a person’s thoughts or motives. Alternate translation: “thinks good thoughts” or “does not think about doing what is wrong” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## u76e
Here “falsehood” represents a false idol. To “lift up” means to worship. Alternate translation: “who has not worshiped an idol” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-idiom]])

# 24:5
## z3wj
The word “he” does not refer to a specific person. It refers to the ones with pure hearts mentioned in previous verse. The abstract noun “blessing” can be stated as a verb. Alternate translation: “Yahweh will bless them” (See: [[figs-genericnoun]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## bc4f
The abstract noun “righteousness” can be stated as “righteously.” And, “salvation” can be stated as “save.” Alternate translation: “God will deal righteously with him and save him” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 24:6
## n5aj
Here “generation” represents people in general. Alternate translation: “The people who seek him are like this” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## h9nq
Both statements mean the same thing. They both refer to those who go to the temple to worship God. Alternate translation: “the ones who approach God, they are the ones who may worship God, the one we Israelites worship” (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## fbc7
Going to the temple to worship Yahweh is spoken of as if the person is literally seeking to find him. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## tsi7
Here “face” stands for the whole person. Alternate translation: “the God of Jacob” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 24:7
## yi4r
The two phases are very similar in meaning. The words “gates” and “doors” refer to the gates of the temple. The writer is speaking to the gates as if they were a person. A gatekeeper would be the one to open the gates. Alternate translation: “Open up, you ancient gates” or “Open these ancient gates” (See: [[figs-parallelism]] and [[figs-personification]])

## z61a
It is uncertain what specific part of the gate is the “head.” But, it stands for the gate as a whole. (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 24:8
## bp2e
The writer speaks about Yahweh as if he were a mighty warrior who fights in battles. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 24:9
## hl69
The two phases are very similar in meaning. The words “gates” and “doors” refer to the gates of the temple. The writer is speaking to the gates as if they were a person. A gatekeeper would be the one to open the gates. See how you translated this in [Psalms 24:7](../024/007.md). Alternate translation: “Open up, you ancient gates” or “Open these ancient gates” (See: [[figs-parallelism]] and [[figs-personification]])

## fk49
It is uncertain what specific part of the gate is the “head.” But, it stands for the gate as a whole. (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 25:intro
## utp4
See [[PSA-utp4]]
# 25:1
## sq2m
See [[PSA-sq2m]]
## z3ls
The phrase “lift up my life” is a metaphor. Possible meanings are (1) the writer is giving himself to Yahweh, which means he is completely depending on Yahweh. Alternate translation: “I give myself to you” or (2) he is offering prayer and adoration to Yahweh. Alternate translation: “I worship and adore you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 25:2
## m2b6
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “Do not let my enemies humiliate me” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## ff1t
“rejoice in triumph over me.” The phrase “over me” implies that his enemies have defeated him and stand above in victory. Alternate translation: “defeat me and rejoice about it” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 25:3
## jw7y
“Do not let those who hope in you be disgraced.” Disgrace could come from being defeated by their enemies. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “Do not let enemies defeat those who hope in you” (See: [[figs-explicit]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

## haz8
“who trusts you”

## r1zd
“act deceitfully” or “act with trickery”

## le6f
“without a reason”

# 25:4
## a1rg
Both statements mean the same thing. God teaching a person how they should behave is spoken of as if he were showing a person the correct path on which a person should travel. (See: [[figs-parallelism]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 25:5
## ji5y
“I depend on you” or “I wait patiently for you”

## t3bw
Guide and teach mean the same thing, to give instruction. Alternate translation: “Instruct me to conduct my life by obeying your truth” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## zz1y
The abstract noun “salvation” can be stated as “saves.” Alternate translation: “the one who saves me” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 25:6
## f922
This is an idiom. This does not mean God forgot something. The writer is asking God to think about and consider his acts of compassion and faithfulness. Alternate translation: “Remember” or “Think about” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## uw7b
The abstract nouns “compassion” and “faithfulness” can be stated as adjectives. Alternate translation: “how you have been compassionate and faithful to your covenant” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## y7a2
Here “they” personifies God’s compassion and covenant faithfulness. Alternate translation: “for that is how you have always been” (See: [[figs-personification]])

# 25:7
## ym66
The abstract noun “sins” can be stated as “sinned.” Alternate translation: “Do not think about how I sinned against you when I was young” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## ayg8
The abstract noun “rebelliousness” can be stated as “rebelled.” Alternate translation: or about how I have rebelled against you” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## rmx6
This is an idiom. This does not mean God forgot something. The writer is asking God to think about him. Alternate translation: “Remember me” or “Think about me” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## dzp2
The abstract nouns “faithfulness” and “goodness” can be stated as adjectives. Alternate translation: “and be faithful to me because of your covenant, because you are good” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 25:8
## fe3c
How God wants a person to behave is spoken of as if it were a way or path on which a person travels. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 25:9
## sd77
This nominal adjective can be stated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “humble people” or “those who are humble” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## g5rh
How God wants a person to behave is spoken of as if it were a way or path on which a person travels. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 25:10
## y1ce
The word “paths” is a metaphor for ways. Alternate translation: “Yahweh always loves us because of his covenant and he is always trustworthy” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 25:11
## i29u
The phrase “your name” here refers to Yahweh’s reputation. Alternate translation: “For your reputation” or “So that people will honor you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## zdw5
The abstract noun “sin” can be stated as “sinned.” Alternate translation: “please forgive me, for I have sinned much” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 25:12
## uen3
This question introduces “the man who fears Yahweh” as a new topic. Alternate translation: “I will tell you about the man who fears Yahweh.” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## r5gg
These words refer to any person who fears Yahweh, not a specific person. Alternate translation: “are those who fear … instruct them … they should” (See: [[figs-genericnoun]])

## e57l
Yahweh teaching people how they should behave is spoken of as if Yahweh were teaching the people what way or path they should travel. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 25:13
## vwm7
These words refer to any person who fears Yahweh, not a specific person. Alternate translation: “Their lives … their descendants” (See: [[figs-genericnoun]])

## f8pb
“God will cause him to prosper” or “God will cause them to prosper”

# 25:14
## m7sj
“Yahweh is a friend to those.” Some translate it as “Yahweh confides in those.” His confiding in them shows the intimate friendship he has with them.

# 25:15
## utj9
Here “eyes” represents looking. It is implied that he looks to Yahweh for help. Alternate translation: “I always look to Yahweh to help me” or “I always depend on Yahweh to help me” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-explicit]])

## mb6a
A net is a trap. A person who is in danger is spoken of as if their feet are tangled in a net. Alternate translation: He will rescue me from danger” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 25:16
## jm85
Yahweh paying attention to a person and considering him is spoken of as if Yahweh were physically turning towards the person. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 25:17
## lu85
Here “heart” represents a person’s emotions. Alternate translation: “I feel more and more troubled” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## t6l8
“bring me out of my distress.” This speaks of distress as if it were a place that a person can be brought out of. Alternate translation: “rescue me from my distress” or “relieve me of my distress” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## px9i
The word “distress” is an abstract noun. Alternate translation: “the things that distress me” or “the things that cause me to be afraid” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 25:18
## gp57
“Notice my affliction”

## kwp4
The abstract noun “affliction” can be stated as a verb. Alternate translation: “the things that afflict me” or “how afflicted I am” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## my25
The word “toils” is an abstract noun. Alternate translation: “the things that trouble me” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 25:19
## it1s
“they hate me cruelly” or “they hate me fiercely”

# 25:20
## zk7e
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “Do not let my enemies humiliate me” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## y36b
Going to Yahweh for protection is spoken of as taking refuge in him. Alternate translation: “go to you for protection!” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 25:21
## b36j
This speaks about “integrity” and “uprightness” as if they were persons who could keep another person safe. These abstract nouns can be stated as adjectives. Alternate translation: “May being honest and doing what is right preserve me” or “Preserve me, Lord, because I am honest and do what is right” (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## d4fj
“keep me safe”

## vj9z
“Save Israel” or “Redeem Israel”

## msf4
Here “Israel” represents the people of Israel. Alternate translation: “the people of Israel … our troubles” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 26:3
## qc7g
Here “eyes” represent a person’s thoughts and having something before one’s eyes represents being aware of that thing. The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “For I am always aware of your covenant faithfulness” or “For I am always aware that you are faithful to your covenant” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## am2g
The word “walk” is a metaphor for behavior. The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated with an adjective. Alternate translation: “I conduct my life according to your faithfulness” or “I behave the way I do because you are faithful” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## b17j

## hc11

# 26:6
## idg7
This seems to refer to a ritual washing of hands in water to symbolize freedom from sin and guilt. (See: [[translate-symaction]])

## u7rx
This was an action of worship that the Israelites were accustomed to doing.

# 26:8
## ywm8
Possible meanings are (1) if a person wrote this after the time of David, then the writer is referring to the temple in Jerusalem or (2) if David wrote this, then this refers to the tent that God told his people to set up so that they could worship him there.

## adz5
Here “glory” represents the presence and power of God, which is similar to a very bright light. Alternate translation: “the place where people can see the glorious light of your presence” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 26:9
## k89i
“Sweep away” here is a metaphor for destruction. Alternate translation: “Do not destroy me along with sinners” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## gb7w
The word “sweep” is understood. Alternate translation: “or sweep my life” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

## dsi8
The word “bloodthirsty” represents wanting to kill people. Alternate translation: “people who are eager to shed others’ blood” or “murderers” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## g7rx

## qm5d
This phrase shows that the writer is changing from speaking about wicked people to talking about himself.

## pgd5

This question emphasizes that there is no one that David should fear. Alternate translation: “I will not be afraid of anyone” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## gdw7

# 27:2
## b8ta
Destroying someone completely is spoken of as if it were devouring a person’s flesh. He did not mean that they wanted to eat his body. Alternate translation: “to destroy me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## afd9
These words mean the same thing. These are the evildoers who came near to him. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## gj21
This represents the writer’s enemies failing to fulfill their plans to harm the writer. Alternate translation: “did not succeed” or “failed” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 27:3
## a7hp
“though an army surrounds me” or “though an army puts its tents around me”

## z488
“I will continue to trust God to help me”

# 27:4
## p5pc
“I have asked Yahweh to let me do”

## vpq5
A person really wanting something and continually asking God for it is spoken of as if he were seeking to find something. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## gb9g
The wonderful character of God is spoken of as if it were physical beauty. Alternate translation: “to see how wonderful Yahweh is” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## cv9f

## mz3d

# 27:6
## a3t2
This represents the writer receiving pride or honor when he defeats his enemies. It can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “people will honor me when I win the fight against my enemies” or “God will honor me by enabling me to defeat my enemies” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

# 27:7
## p3lq
The “voice” often represents a person who speak or calls out. Alternate translation: “Yahweh, hear me” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## q1ev
This implies that Yahweh hears the writer’s prayer and Yahweh will do what the writer asks. Alternate translation: “answer my prayer” or “do what I request of you” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 27:8
## jx52

## lv4r

# 27:9
## uv72
The face here represents Yahweh’s attention, and hiding the face represents rejecting someone. Alternate translation: “Do not reject me” or “Do not stop taking care of me” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## n49l
David said “your servant” to refer to himself in a humble way. Alternate translation: “do not be angry with me” (See: [[figs-123person]])

## p7vh
The words “forsake” and “abandon” mean the same thing. The writer is emphasizing that he does not want God to leave him. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## j546
The words “and do not” are understood. Alternate translation: “and do not abandon me” or “and do not leave me” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

## sm12
The abstract noun “salvation” can be stated as “saves.” Alternate translation: God who saves me” or “because you are the God who saves me” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 27:10
## w897
“Even if my father and my mother were to forsake me.” He is not saying that they actually have done this or that they would do it. His point is that even if they did that, God would not abandon him. (See: [[figs-hypo]])

## n75n
“Yahweh will keep me” or “Yahweh will take care of me”

# 27:11
## z7b8
How a person should behave is spoken of as if it were a way or path that person should travel. Alternate translation: “Teach me how you want me to live” or “Teach me to do what you want me to do” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## r72j
Yahweh keeping the writer safe from his enemies is spoken of as if Yahweh leads the writer on a level path where he will not stumble and fall. Alternate translation: “Keep me safe” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 27:12
## gs3s
The abstract noun “desires” can be stated as a verb. Alternate translation: “Do not let my enemies do to me what they desire” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## s7ry
“Risen up” here is an idiom meaning that a witness stood in court to present testimony. Alternate translation: “have stood up in order to speak against me” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## ez4n
Here violence is spoken for as if it was something a person could breathe out. Alternate translation: “they say that they will do violent things to me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 27:13
## ts3j
This rhetorical question can be stated positively. Alternate translation: “Something bad would have happened to me” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## c72l

## wld8

# 27:14
## g4pq

## m8gs

## r4t6

# 28:7
## g4ne
The abstract noun “strength” can be stated as “strong.” Alternate translation: “Yahweh makes me strong” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## vh7h
This represents Yahweh’s protecting the writer. Alternate translation: “he protects me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## r9jp
Here “heart” represents the whole person. Alternate translation: “I trust” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## bl9l
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “he helps me” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## uts5
Here “heart” represents the whole person. Alternate translation: “I greatly rejoice” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 28:8
## pd6u
The abstract noun “strength” can be stated as “strong.” Alternate translation: “Yahweh makes his people strong” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## vd99
Yahweh keeping the king safe is spoken of as if Yahweh were a place that the king could go for safety. Alternate translation: “he keeps safe the one he appointed to be king” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## yh2k
The represents the king. (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 28:9
## at1a
This speaks about the people of God as if they were something God inherited. Alternate translation: “your possession” or “those who belong to you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## e7e7
The writer speaks about Yahweh as if he were a shepherd and the people are his sheep. A shepherd would carry a sheep if it needed help or protection. Alternate translation: “Be like their shepherd and protect them forever” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 29:intro
## b4tt
See [[PSA-b4tt]]
# 29:1
## kq7e
See [[PSA-kq7e]]
## bc7z
The phrase “sons of” is a way of saying “having the characteristics of.” Alternate translation: “you mighty men” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## i354
The abstract nouns “glory” and “strength” can be stated as adjectives. Alternate translation: “praise Yahweh because he is glorious and strong” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 29:2
## yv1p
The abstract noun “glory” can be stated as a verb or adjective. Alternate translation: “Honor Yahweh just as his name deserves” or “Proclaim that Yahweh is glorious just as his name deserves” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## rcj6
The phrase “his name” refers to Yahweh or his reputation. Alternate translation: “as is proper because of who he is” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## e4f6
The implied information is that the people were to bow down in worship. Alternate translation: “Bow down to worship Yahweh” (See: [[figs-explicit]] and [[translate-symaction]])

## da1b
The abstract nouns “splendor” and “holiness” can be translated as adjectives. Alternate translation: “because he is gloriously beautiful and holy” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 29:3
## dml8
See [[PSA-dml8]]
## t9g6
God’s voice is louder and clearer than all other sounds and noises. It can be heard over other loud sounds such as the sound of the waters. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “When Yahweh speaks his voice is louder than the sound of the sea” or “Yahweh shouts louder than the sound of the waters” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## z58f
This refers to the seas or the oceans. These waters make a very loud noise as the waves rise and fall.

## u41c
All occurrences of “voice” here represent Yahweh speaking. The writer is emphasizing that when Yahweh speaks, the sound is so loud it is heard over the waters, and it is so powerful it can destroy the largest trees. Alternate translation: “When Yahweh speaks, his voice” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## b7zk
This speaks about God speaking as if it were the sound of thunder. Just like the sound of thunder, Yahweh’s voice can be heard over large distances. Alternate translation: “The voice of the glorious God is loud like thunder” or “When the glorious God speaks it rumbles like thunder” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## srk7
“over the large bodies of water”

# 29:6
## s8av
See [[PSA-s8av]]
## kdn3
The ground of Lebanon shaking is spoken of as if it were a young calf skipping. This emphasizes that when Yahweh speaks, the power of his voice shakes the ground. Alternate translation: “He makes the land of Lebanon shake like a calf skipping” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## y9uu
jump lightly back and forth

## war4
The words “he makes” and “skip” are understood from the first phrase. They can be repeated here. The ground of Sirion shaking is spoken of as if it were a young ox skipping. This emphasizes that when Yahweh speaks, the power of his voice shakes the ground. Alternate translation: “he makes Sirion skip like a young ox” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]] and [[figs-simile]])

## n725
This is a mountain in Lebanon. It is also called Mount Hermon. (See: [[translate-names]])

# 29:7
## wk16
All occurrences of “voice” here represent Yahweh speaking. Alternate translation: “When Yahweh speaks he causes lightning to flash in the sky” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## rc8c
This refers to lightning.

# 29:9
## ht1n
Here “voice” represents Yahweh speaking. Alternate translation: “When Yahweh speaks, the sound causes” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## sqa7
“the large trees to shake”

## f33q
Removing the leaves of the trees is spoken of as if it was removing their clothing. Alternate translation: “strips off the leaves from the trees” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 29:10
## mk7u
This means that Yahweh rules. Alternate translation: “Yahweh rules” or “Yahweh is king” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## b6k6
Here “flood” refers to waters that cover the earth.

# 29:11
## vm7e
The word “peace” is an abstract noun. Alternate translation: “Yahweh blesses his people by causing them to prosper and to live peacefully” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 30:intro
## eee3
See [[PSA-eee3]]
# 30:1
## iaj9
See [[PSA-iaj9]]
## e8py
“This song was sung when the temple was dedicated”

## ig1t
The writer speaks of God rescuing him and keeping him from dying as if God had drawn him up from a deep well. Alternate translation: “you rescued me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 30:3
## gel6
Since “Sheol” was the place where dead people go, it refers to death. Alternate translation: “kept me from dying” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## sw64
Here “my soul” refers to the writer. Alternate translation: “brought me up” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## ryd7
The “grave” represents death. Alternate translation: “from dying” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 30:4
## jui4
The abstract nouns “thanks” and “holiness” can be stated as “thank” and “holy.” Alternate translation: “Remember that God is holy and thank him” or “Remember what God has done because he is holy and thank him” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 30:5
## n3py
“his anger lasts only a moment.” The abstract noun “anger” can be stated as “angry.” Alternate translation: “he is angry for only a moment” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## ls29
Here “moment” represents a short amount of time. Alternate translation: “a short time” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## zm7v
The abstract noun “favor” can be stated as the adjective “good.” Alternate translation: “but he is good to us all of our lives” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## vw11
This speaks about “weeping” and “joy” as if they were something that travels and arrives at a certain time. Alternate translation: “We may cry during the night, but the next morning we will be joyful” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 30:6
## v3a5
The word “confidence” is an abstract noun. The writer recalls a time when he was prospering and felt confident and safe. Alternate translation: “When I was confident” or “When I felt safe” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## p1kl
The word “shaken” is a metaphor for defeat. Alternate translation: “No one will defeat me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 30:7
## d155
The abstract noun “favor” can be stated as the verb “favored” or the adjective “kind.” Alternate translation: “when you favored me” or “when you were kind to me” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## m53d
The writer’s security is spoken of as if he were a strong mountain. Alternate translation: “you made me as secure as a high mountain” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## q4uk
This is an idiom. Alternate translation: “when you stopped helping me” or “when you rejected me” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## y2rt
“I was fearful” or “I was worried”

# 30:8
## m69p
The phrase “sought favor” means to ask for help. Alternate translation: “I pleaded for you to help me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## n1hs
The writer is referring to Yahweh in third person. It can be stated in second person. Alternate translation: “from you, my Lord” (See: [[figs-123person]])

# 30:9
## npv8
The writer uses this question to emphasize that he would be of no value to God if he were dead. Alternate translation: “There is no advantage if I die and go down to the grave.” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## h9v9
The writer uses these questions to emphasize that his dead and decayed body cannot praise God. Alternate translation: “The dust will certainly not praise you or tell others about how trustworthy you are.” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## ds6c
This refers to the body of the writer which will decay and become dust when he is dead. Alternate translation: “my decayed body” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 30:11
## fh4q
It was customary for the Jews to dance when they were very happy. The abstract nouns “mourning” and “dancing” can be stated as verbs. Alternate translation: “You have caused me to stop mourning and to dance with joy instead” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## y5wj
Sackcloth was associated with mourning and sorrow. Alternate translation: “You have caused me to no longer be sad” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## l9jm
The writer speaks of gladness as if it were a garment that he could put on. Alternate translation: “caused me to be glad” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 30:12
## b717
Here “my glory” refers to the writer’s soul or heart or inner being. This represents the entire person of the writer, who worships God because God has made him glad. Alternate translation: “I will sing praise to you” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## j2an

# 31:1
## ggk4
See [[PSA-ggk4]]
## yu4y
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## fs4i
Going to Yahweh for protection is spoken of as taking refuge in him. Alternate translation: “I go to you, Yahweh, for protection” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## f8jw
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “do not let others humiliate me” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 31:2
## x6bw
The phrase “be my rock of refuge” is a request for protection. The second phrase emphasizes the first phrase. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## tq1e
Yahweh is spoke of as if he were a huge rock that would protect the writer from attack. Alternate translation: “like a huge rock on which I can be safe” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## p9xb
Yahweh is spoken of as if he were a strong fortress in which the writer would be protected from his enemies. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 31:3
## m5q1
Yahweh is spoke of as if he were a huge rock that would protect the writer from attack. Alternate translation: “like a huge rock on which I can be safe” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## d9h8
Yahweh is spoken of as if he were a strong fortress in which the writer would be protected from his enemies. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## kti8
In this phrase “name” represents Yahweh. Alternate translation: “so that your name may be honored” or “so that I may worship you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## nm5d
The words “lead” and “guide” mean basically the same thing and strengthen the request that Yahweh lead him. Alternate translation: “lead me where you want me to go” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 31:4
## xp2k
The writer is spoken of as if he were a bird caught in a hidden net, and waiting for Yahweh to free him from the trap. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## pg5z
Yahweh is spoken of as if he is a place where the writer can hide from people who are attacking him. Alternate translation: “you always protect me” or “you give me constant protection” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 31:5
## e3hz
God is spirit, but he is here spoken of as if he has hands. Here “your hands” refers to Yahweh’s care. Alternate translation: “Into your care” (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

## ez3i
Here “my spirit” refers to the writer. Alternate translation: “I place myself” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## m7ux
“you are a God I can trust”

# 31:6
## d1f4
Here the word “worthless” refers to all idols. This can be clarified in translation. Alternate translation: “Idols are worthless. I hate those who serve them” (See: [[figs-distinguish]])

# 31:7
## z4ew
The words “glad” and “rejoice” share similar meanings and emphasize the intensity of joy. The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “I will be very glad because you are faithful to your covenant” (See: [[figs-doublet]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## x1wl
Both of these phrases express the idea that God knows about the writer’s troubles. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## ji14
Here “my soul” refers to the writer. Alternate translation: “my distress” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 31:8
## x76g
Here “my feet” refers to the writer. Alternate translation: “You have set me” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## d4bb
The Hebrews thought of wide open spaces as a metaphor for safety and freedom. Alternate translation: “a place where I am free” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 31:9
## iv54
“I am suffering greatly”

## amp8
The terms “soul” and “body” are used to describe the complete person. (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 31:10
## p8pm
Here “my life” refers to the writer. Alternate translation: “I have become very weak” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## nw2b
“because of my sorrow … because of my groaning”

## l7fj
The phrase “is weary” is missing, but is implied. Alternate translation: “my years are weary with groaning” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

## a1r3
Here “My strength” refers to the writer. Alternate translation: “I have become weak” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## b5c7
Here “my bones” refers to the physical health of the writer. Alternate translation: “my health is failing” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 31:11
## n8g3
“people insult me”

## w86t
“are shocked at my condition”

# 31:12
## w6b3
People do not think about dead people. The writer does not think people think about him. (See: [[figs-simile]])

## dnb7
The writer speaks of himself as if he was completely useless. “as useless as a broken pot” (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 31:13
## ll6r
It is implied that “many” refers to people. Alternate translation: “many people talking about me” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

## pf7q
“scary reports from many sources”

## d84i
This idiom means to kill someone. Alternate translation: “kill me” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 31:15
## pr1h
Here “your hand” refers to Yahweh’s power. Alternate translation: “You have the power to decide my future” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## c577
“from people who try to capture me”

# 31:16
## x22n
The writer speaks of Yahweh acting favorably towards him as if Yahweh’s face shone a light on him. Alternate translation: “Act favorably towards your servant” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## hjf7
The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “save me because you are faithful to your covenant” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 31:17
## fg5c
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “Do not let others make me feel ashamed” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## vud9
“I wish that God would disgrace wicked people!”

## mw8m
This refers to “wicked people. (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## n96w
Here “in Sheol” represents death. Alternate translation: “Let them die so they cannot speak” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 31:18
## rvr4
This can be translated in active form. Alternate translation: “May someone make these lying lips silent” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## jqf6
These represent lying people. Alternate translation: “people who lie” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## dig8
Here “the righteous” refers to people who are righteous. Alternate translation: “that say terrible things about righteous people” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## r22l
These terms have similar meanings. Alternate translation: “with a complete lack of respect”

# 31:19
## c7i2
This can be expressed with a verb. Alternate translation: “are the good things you do” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## dge4
Yahweh’s goodness is spoken of as if it was something that could be stored up like a harvest. Alternate translation: “that you are keeping ready to use” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ld4z
“those who respect you greatly”

## iu38
Going to Yahweh for protection is spoken of as taking refuge in him. See how you translated this in [Psalms 31:1](../031/001.md). Alternate translation: “those who go to you for protection” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 31:20
## q6pa
These phrases both mean that God protects them. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## v252
Yahweh’s presence is spoken of as if it is a strong building where the writer would be safe. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## dx2q
Here a “shelter” represents a safe place. Alternate translation: “You provide a safe place for them” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## jre5
Here “tongues” refer to the people who are speaking violent things against the writer. Alternate translation: “where their enemies cannot speak evil at them” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 31:21
## jkp6
The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “he showed me that he is wonderfully faithful to his covenant” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 31:22
## uq2j
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “You have removed me from your presence” (See: [[figs-activepassive]] and [[figs-idiom]])

## aku2
Here Yahweh is represented by his “eyes.” Alternate translation: “you” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## pa4l
Here “plea” can be expressed with a verb. Alternate translation: “you heard me plead for help” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 31:23
## a8kd
This refers to the faithful people. Alternate translation: “the people who are faithful” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## el6y
Here “pay back” is an idiom that refers to punishment. Alternate translation: “he gives the proud people all of the punishment that they deserve” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 32:intro
## le2f
See [[PSA-le2f]]
# 32:1
## w4yz
See [[PSA-w4yz]]
## tgw8
Possible meanings are (1) David wrote the psalm or (2) the psalm is about David or (3) the psalm is in the style of David’s psalms.

## pzp9
These phrases have similar meanings. They can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “who God forgives his transgression and covers his sin” (See: [[figs-parallelism]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

## sch5
Here sin that is forgiven is spoken of as if it were covered so that it can not be seen. Alternate translation: “whose sin is ignored” or “whose sin is deliberately forgotten” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 32:2
## k682
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “whom Yahweh sees as innocent” or “who is not guilty according to Yahweh” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## m29u
Here “spirit” refers to the person. Alternate translation: “in whom there is not deceit” or “who is completely honest” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 32:3
## s6cx
Here “my bones” refers to the writer. Alternate translation: “I was wasting away” or “I was getting weaker” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## svq8
This idiom means “continually.” Alternate translation: “all the time” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 32:4
## j9jl
These extremes include everything in between. Alternate translation: “all the time” (See: [[figs-merism]])

## xw1r
Here “hand” refers to Yahweh. The entire phrase is an idiom that means “you afflicted me.” Alternate translation: “you made me suffer greatly” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-idiom]])

## fkc1
David’s strength is compared to a small, green plant that turns brown and crumbles in the dry season. (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 32:6
## rpw8
“when they are in great trouble.”

## yl7l
Difficulties are spoken of as if they were a flood of water. Alternate translation: “Then when difficulties come like a flood of water, those people will be safe” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 32:7
## r54z
Yahweh is spoken of as if he was a safe place from the attacks of the writer’s enemies. Alternate translation: “You are like a place where I can hide myself from my enemies” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## u3z7
This metaphor apparently means that Yahweh’s protection of the writer is the cause for songs of victory to be sung. Alternate translation: “Because of you I will sing songs of victory” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 32:8
## x1lw
The words “instruct” and “teach” mean basically the same thing and emphasize careful instruction. Alternate translation: “I will teach you everything about the way” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## mh9j
Here the “I” is probably Yahweh who talks directly to David.

## s74m
Living in the correct way is spoken of as if it were a path that the writer should walk. Alternate translation: “how you should live your life” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## lj3f
Here “my eye” refers to Yahweh’s attention. Alternate translation: “and direct my attention to you” or “and watch over you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 32:9
## ry6h
The writer compares people with no understanding to horses and mules. Possible meanings are (1) the writer is speaking Yahweh’s words to his readers, “You all must not be like a horse … no understanding” or (2) Yahweh is speaking to the writer as though to a group of people. (See: [[figs-simile]])

## g1b3
Two tools that are used by people to guide horses and mules go where the rider wants them to go.

## cv6w
“where anyone wants them to go.” The “you” here is singular and refers to no one in particular.

# 32:10
## ann9
Yahweh being faithful to a person and protecting that person is spoken of as if Yahweh’s covenant faithfulness surrounded the person. The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “Because Yahweh is faithful to his covenant, he will protect the one who trusts in him” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 32:11
## zxp2
Here “in Yahweh” refers to what Yahweh has done for them. “Be glad because of what Yahweh has done” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## n71r
This refers to people. Alternate translation: “you righteous people” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## gs62
“shout joyfully” or “shout because of joy”

## ame7
Here “heart” refers to the person. Alternate translation: “people who are upright” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 33:intro
## m4ih
See [[PSA-m4ih]]
# 33:1
## b979
See [[PSA-b979]]
## x3gc
Here “in Yahweh” refers to what Yahweh has done for them. “Rejoice because of what Yahweh has done” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## jn1l
“to praise Yahweh is appropriate for upright people”

# 33:4
## mcg5
See [[PSA-mcg5]]
## t8rm
Here “upright” is used as a metaphor for something that is true. Alternate translation: “Yahweh always does what he says that he will do” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 33:5
## n6zg
These abstract nouns can be stated as actions. Alternate translation: “He loves doing what is right and just” or “He loves those who do what is right and just” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## e631
People everywhere in the world being able to see evidence of Yahweh’s covenant faithfulness is spoken of as if his covenant faithfulness filled the earth. The abstract noun “covenant faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “People everywhere on earth can see that Yahweh is faithful to his covenant” or “Throughout the earth, there is evidence that Yahweh is faithful to his covenant” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 33:6
## qhw8
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “By using his word, Yahweh made the heavens” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## bb33
This refers to Yahweh’s word. Alternate translation: “by his word” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 33:7
## xt7h
See [[PSA-xt7h]]
## k6ey
“like behind a dam.” The writer describes the creation of the sea as if God piles up all the waters together. (See: [[figs-simile]])

## eg5a
The writer describes the creation of the oceans as if God put them in a storehouse. Alternate translation: “he puts the oceans in their place, just like a man puts grain in a storehouse” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 33:8
## vc67
This refers to the people on the earth. Alternate translation: “Let everyone on earth” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## ame6
Here “stand in awe” is an idiom that means “be in awe.” Alternate translation: “honor him” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 33:9
## c3h8
Here “stood in place” is an idiom that means “was created.” Alternate translation: “started to exist” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 33:10
## x22s
See [[PSA-x22s]]
## zp3d
“Yahweh destroys” or “Yahweh breaks”

## r5ri
Here “nations” refers to the people of these nations. Alternate translation: “the alliances of the people of different nations” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## sn2l
An alliance is an agreement between two or more nations to support each other in a war against a common enemy.

## evm2
“the intentions of the peoples” Alternate translation: “the evil plans of the peoples”

# 33:11
## gp8c
Here “stand” is an idiom that means “endure.” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## ww4p

Here “his heart” refers to Yahweh. Alternate translation: “his plans” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## lea7
“for all future generations.” This is an idiom that means “forever.” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## w4nk

## ph21

## k4jm
The people Yahweh has chosen to worship him are described here as if they were an inheritance that he has received. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 33:14
## r7tm
The place where Yahweh lives is spoken of as if it is above the earth where people live. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 33:15
## ch4n
Here “hearts” refers to the thinking of these people. The writer speaks of Yahweh guiding the thinking of the people as if he were a potter who was shaping a bowl. Alternate translation: “guides their thinking as a potter shapes a bowl” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 33:16
## w54n
This could be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “A large army is not what saves a king” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## hgn8

# 33:18
## v87c
This word shows that a new theme begins in this Psalm. Alternate translation: “Look” or “Listen” or “Pay attention to what I am about to tell you”

## fy9c
Here “eye” refers to Yahweh’s attention. Alternate translation: “Yahweh’s attention” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## y8yf
The idiom to “count on” means to “wait for” or to “expect.” The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated as an adverb. Alternate translation: “those who expect him to act faithfully because of his covenant” or “those who wait for him to act because he is faithful to his covenant” (See: [[figs-idiom]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## z5yv

# 33:20
## j64c

## l55j

# 33:21
## ujv3
Here “hearts” refer to the people. Alternate translation: “We rejoice” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## eu9i
Here “holy name” refers to Yahweh’s holy character. Alternate translation: “in his holy character” or “in him because he is holy” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 33:22
## nn9g
Yahweh acting faithfully towards the people is spoken of as if Yahweh’s covenant faithfulness were with them. The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated with an adverb. Alternate translation: “May you always act faithfully towards us because of your covenant, Yahweh” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

“as we hope for your help”

# 34:13
## h79u
These two phrases refer to the same thing and it is said in different ways to emphasize its importance. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

# 34:15
## x87w
Here “the eyes of Yahweh” refer to his careful watching. “The righteous” is a reference to righteous people. Alternate translation: “Yahweh carefully watches over the righteous people” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-nominaladj]])

## ihz6
Here Yahweh is represented by his “ears.” To be directed toward something means to pay attention to it. Alternate translation: “he pays attention to their cry” or “he answers their cry” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 34:16
## b3yv
Yahweh will cause people to so completely forget them when they die that it is as if he used a knife to cut off any memory of them. Alternate translation: “so that when they are dead, people will forget them completely” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ib9f

## ers6
Here “is close” means “ready to help.” Alternate translation: “Yahweh is always ready to help” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## km9m
This is a nominal adjective that refers to people who are brokenhearted. Deep sadness is spoken of as if the person’s heart is broken. Alternate translation: “people who are very sad” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-nominaladj]])

## zhw6
People who are deeply discouraged are spoken of as if their spirits are crushed. Alternate translation: “people who are deeply discouraged” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 34:19
## s9nw
This refers to people who are righteous. Alternate translation: “the righteous people” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

# 34:20
## p78v
Here “all his bones” is literal, but it also implies that Yahweh takes care of the entire person. Alternate translation: “He provides complete protection for him, he will not be harmed in any way” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 34:21
## zrq9
Evil is described as if it were a man who can kill people. Alternate translation: “The evil deeds of wicked people will kill them” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## rj4c
This refers to wicked people. (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## a6li

## pl7j

## wb23
Going to Yahweh for protection is spoken of as taking refuge in him. Alternate translation: “go to him for protection” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 35:8
## iq5p
Destruction is spoken of as if it was a dangerous animal that would suddenly attack them. Alternate translation: “Let them be destroyed suddenly” or “Let them be surprised because you destroy them suddenly” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## d6rv
The schemes of the wicked are spoken of as if they were a net that they place to catch the writer. Alternate translation: “the net that they placed in order to capture me like an animal and harm me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## e9d9
This is the same metaphor as in verse 7. The net is intended to catch the writer. Alternate translation: “Let them fall into the pit that they dug for me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-explicit]])

## n85r
Possible meanings are (1) fall into the pit of verse 7 or (2) fall into destruction.

## q1k1

## dy1n

## fcx1

## kuz3
The words “poor” and “needy” mean basically the same thing and emphasize that Yahweh saves many who need his help. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## s32p

## v6yt
“What he says is”

## pir7

# 36:4
## d3zz

## w34n
