# 36:5
## wiw8
The greatness of God’s covenant faithfulness is spoken of as if it were an object that reached as high as the heavens. The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “Your covenant faithfulness … is very great” or “You … are as faithful to your covenant as the heavens are high above the earth” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## m314
The greatness of God’s loyalty is spoken of as if it was very high. Alternate translation: “is as high as the clouds” or “is enormously great” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 36:6
## s49q
These phrases describe the greatness of God’s righteousness and judgments as if they were very high and deep. Alternate translation: “as high as the highest mountains … as deep as the deepest sea” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## e8gt
“you help” or “you save”

# 36:7
## vs32
The word “precious” refers to how greatly the writer values Yahweh’s covenant faithfulness. The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “I greatly value how you are faithful to your covenant” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 36:8
## vy98
Eating much food as guests in a house is a metaphor for God providing all his people need. Alternate translation: “They will have all they need because you will provide it to them” or “You have plenty to give, and you will provide them with all they need” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## mw7h
There are two metaphors here. God’s abundant blessings are spoken of as if they are the water in a flowing river. Also, those who receive those blessings are spoken of as if they are drinking them like water. Alternate translation: “your precious blessings are like a river from which you will let them drink” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 36:9
## wc6m
“source of life”

## f7u5
Here “light” is a metaphor for true knowledge. Alternate translation: “when you enlighten us, we will know the truth” or “your light is what enables us to know the truth about you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 36:10
## d1ua
The writer speaks of Yahweh continuing to act faithfully towards the people as if Yahweh were to extend his covenant faithfulness or make it longer. The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated with an adverb. Alternate translation: “Continue to act faithfully to those who know you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## jtd4
The abstract noun “defense” can be stated as a verb. “Continue” is implied from the previous phrase. Alternate translation: “Continue to protect the upright of heart” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]] and [[figs-ellipsis]])

## qms7
Here “heart” refers to the people. Alternate translation: “the upright” or “people who act righteously” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 36:11
## z9yf
Here “foot” and “hand” refer to the evil people. These are not specific men. This refers to evil people in general. Alternate translation: “arrogant people … wicked people” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-genericnoun]])

## a5wg
“send me away” or “make me leave my place”

# 36:12
## mm9r
All three phrases describe the evildoers as defeated. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## q7yf
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “you have knocked them down” or “you have destroyed them” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## bmn7
“cannot get up”

# 37:intro
## tv7e
See [[PSA-tv7e]]
# 37:1
## bd2s
See [[PSA-bd2s]]
## a1ye
“Do not let wicked people upset you” or “Do not be bothered by what wicked people do”

# 37:2
## y2vk
Evildoers are spoken of as if they are grass and plants that dry up and die in the hot weather. These two similes both mean they will die. Alternate translation: “die” or “come to an end” (See: [[figs-simile]] and [[figs-parallelism]])

# 37:3
## eb2r
Faithfulness is spoken of as if it was an animal that would be strengthened by feeding in good pasture. Alternate translation: “nourish faithfulness” or “increase your faithfulness” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 37:4
## pbq2
Here “heart” represents the person’s inner being and thoughts. Alternate translation: “your deepest, inner desires” or “the things that you desire the most” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 37:5
## wt82
Here “give your ways” is an idiom that means to ask Yahweh to control your life. Alternate translation: “Ask Yahweh to guide your actions in life” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## i61n
This is to represent another in legal issues. Here, when one trusts in Yahweh, he will defend that person and grant justice to that person. (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 37:6
## lt22
Both of these phrases mean about the same thing. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## n8jl
This means “in full view of everyone.” Alternate translation: “as clear to see as the light of day” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## jt1t
This means “as visible as the noon sun.” Alternate translation: “as visible as the light at the brightest time of day” (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 37:7
## vgp6
“Be quiet”

# 37:9
## qq5y
The destruction of the wicked is spoken of as if they were a branch of a plant that was cut off and thrown away. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ijv6
“but those who trust in Yahweh”

## rvq6
The possession of the land is spoken of as if it will be received as an inheritance. Alternate translation: “will receive the land as their own possession” or “will live safely in the land” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 37:10
## zbl4
This idiom refers to the death of the evil man. Alternate translation: “will die and you will no longer see him” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 37:11
## ma58
This refers to the people who are meek. Alternate translation: “the meek people” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## bs1x
The possession of the land is spoken of as if it will be received as an inheritance. See how you translated this in [Psalms 37:9](../037/009.md). Alternate translation: “will receive the land as their own possession” or “will live safely in the land” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 37:12
## vej2
This does not refer to a specific man. It refers to wicked people in general. Alternate translation: “The wicked person” (See: [[figs-genericnoun]])

## k2zu
This does not refer to specific people. This refers to people who are righteous. Alternate translation: “the righteous person” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## y9px
The wicked man hates the righteous person so much that he grinds his teeth together to show his anger. (See: [[writing-symlanguage]])

# 37:13
## g21a
It is implied that “his day” will be a day of judgment. Alternate translation: “the day is coming when Yahweh will judge and punish him” or “the day is coming when Yahweh will judge and punish the wicked person” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 37:14
## wde8
This refers to the wicked people. Alternate translation: “The wicked people” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## yet9
Both “swords” and “bows” are weapons used to attack people. The fact that they are “drawn” and “bent” means they are ready to start attacking. Alternate translation: “have prepared their weapons in order to attack” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## f2i7
This destruction of the needy people is spoken of as if they were clay pots that would break into pieces when thrown down on the ground. Alternate translation: “to destroy” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## r9uh
These terms both refer to people who are powerless to defend themselves. Alternate translation: “people who are not able to resist them” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 37:15
## p5xq
Swords are examples of weapons and “hearts” represent the people. To “pierce the heart” is an idiom that means “to kill.” Alternate translation: “Their weapons will be turned against them and they will kill themselves” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-idiom]])

# 37:16
## d3e8
“It is better to be poor and righteous than to be wicked with great wealth”

## brs7
The nominal adjective “the little” refers to few possessions. The nominal adjective “the righteous” refers to a righteous person. Alternate translation: “Better are the few possessions that a righteous person has” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## w4rb
This refers to the wealth of the wicked people. (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

# 37:17
## psr9
Here “arms” represent the strength of the wicked people. Breaking their arms represents taking away their power. This could be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “For Yahweh will remove the strength of the wicked people” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

# 37:18
## f64m
To “watch over” means to protect someone. Here “the blameless” refers to the blameless people. Alternate translation: “protects the blameless people” (See: [[figs-idiom]] and [[figs-nominaladj]])

## ck1b
This is an idiom that means “continually.” Alternate translation: “every day” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 37:19
## itw1
This phrase refers to disasters, such as famine. Alternate translation: “when calamities occur” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 37:20
## y7p7
The writer compares Yahweh’s enemies to the flowers blooming in the fields. (See: [[figs-simile]])

## c5yy
The writer speaks of the destruction of the wicked as if they were weeds or wilted flowers in the field that are burned off after the harvest. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “Yahweh will destroy them as fire turns the weeds of the field into smoke” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

# 37:21
## bz3p
These mean the same thing and emphasize the generosity of the righteous. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 37:22
## u3r4
This is a contrastive form of Parallelism. Those who are blessed by God in contrast to those who are cursed by God. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## bf1j
This can be stated as active. Alternate translation: “Those whom God blesses” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## tev2
The possession of the land is spoken of as if it had been received as an inheritance. See how you translated this in [Psalms 37:9](../037/009.md). Alternate translation: “will receive the land as their own possession” or “will be allowed to live safely in the land” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## u6uk
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “those whom Yahweh curses” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## n6u3
The destruction of the wicked is spoken of as if they were a branch of plant that was cut off and thrown away. See how you translated this in [Psalms 37:9](../037/009.md). (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

These phrases mean basically the same thing and the idea is repeated for emphasis. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

# 38:2
## z5x4
The severity of Yahweh’s punishment of the writer is spoken of as if Yahweh had shot arrows into the writer. Alternate translation: “Your punishment is as painful as if you had shot arrows into me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## w3fq
Yahweh’s punishment of the writer is spoken of as if Yahweh was smashing the writer with his hand. Here, “hand” refers to Yahweh’s power. Alternate translation: “your power knocks me down” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

## c6im

## zm7m
The writer’s illness is so severe that it is as if a huge weight is pressing down on him. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## f3ph

# 38:16
## gan3
“will not delight over my trouble”

## bq5f
Here “my foot” represents the writer. The slipping of his foot is a metaphor that refers to the writer’s troubles and misfortunes. Alternate translation: “If I make mistakes that cause me trouble” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 38:17
## s48p
Possible meanings for this metaphor are (1) “I am so sick that I am about to die” or (2) “I will soon be ruined.” It may be best not to interpret the metaphor in the text. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## sbz5
“I am always in pain”

## ie1w

# 38:20
## ca7b
The actions of the writer’s enemies are spoken of as a financial transaction where they gave him evil things in exchange for good things. The abstract nouns “evil” and “good” can be stated as adjectives. Alternate translation: “They do evil thing to me after I was good to them” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## ai9q
The way the writer’s enemies accuse him is spoken of as if they were throwing accusations at him like rocks. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## bbb4
The writers desire for what is good is spoken of as if he were running after good things. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## czy3
These two phrases have very similar meanings. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## nrs8
Because Yahweh has not yet answered the writer’s request, he speaks of Yahweh as if Yahweh were standing far away from the writer. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 39:2
## fa7x
These two phrases mean the same thing and emphasize that the writer did not speak at all. Alternate translation: “I was completely silent” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 39:3
## u5ie
Here “heart” represents the whole person. The anxious thoughts of the writer are spoken of as if they were a fire burning inside him. Alternate translation: “I became very anxious when I thought about these things” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 39:4
## vey1
These phrases mean basically the same thing. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## bac9
“Show me how brief my life is” or “Show me how soon I will die”

# 39:5
## in3w
The writer speaks of his lifespan is if it could be measured by the width of his hand. Alternate translation: “only a very short time” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ej3j
This simile states that the length of the writer’s life is so short that it does not exist. This is an exaggeration to stress how short it is. Alternate translation: “the length of my life is barely any time at all” (See: [[figs-simile]] and [[figs-hyperbole]])

## l7in
Life is short, and the psalmist speaks of it here as if it were only as long as the time it takes for a person to breathe one breath. Alternate translation: “The time that humans live is as short as a single breath of a person” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 39:6
## wkn8
The lives of people are spoken of as if they are as insignificant as shadows. Alternate translation: “Everyone disappears like shadows do” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## i78f
Here it is implied that they do not know what will happen to their wealth after they die. The full meaning of this statement can be made explicit. (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 39:7
## y9ll
The writer asks this question to emphasize that people cannot help him. This rhetorical question can be translated as a statement. Alternate translation: “So now, Yahweh, I can expect to receive nothing from anyone else.” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## ll7d
These phrases mean basically the same thing. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## whi2

## hd77
“I am defeated completely”

## n2ex
God’s punishment of the writer is spoken of as if God was striking him with his fist. Here “hand” represents God’s judgment. Alternate translation: “your judgment on me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 39:11
## skf5
God will take away the things they value in the same way as a moth eats a piece of cloth. Alternate translation: “consume the things they desire like a moth eats away at clothing” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## uzd7
The writer speaks of the frailty of people as if they were mist that disappears quickly. Alternate translation: “everyone is completely fragile” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 39:12
## rx3j
These three phrases mean basically the same thing and show how strongly the writer wants God to respond to him. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## ae4r
The writer speaks of Yahweh’s lack of response to him as if Yahweh was deaf. Alternate translation: “Do not ignore me as if you could not hear me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## nnj1
The writer speaks of Yahweh’s lack of response as if Yahweh considered him to be a total stranger to him. Alternate translation: “I am like a complete stranger to you” (See: [[figs-simile]])

“Blessed is the man who trusts in Yahweh” or “Those who trust in Yahweh are blessed”

## z621
This refers to the people who are proud. Alternate translation: “proud people” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## f9yc
The Hebrew word is unclear. Possible meanings are (1) “lies” or (2) “false gods.”

# 40:5
## x7v4
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “no one can count all the things you think about us” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## kzt9
These phrases mean essentially the same thing. The first is stated in negative form, and the second is stated in positive form. (See: [[figs-parallelism]] and [[figs-litotes]])

# 40:6
## z1vh
This is an exaggeration to express that other things are much more important to God. Alternate translation: “Sacrifices and other offerings are not the things that delight you most” (See: [[figs-hyperbole]])

## xz9n
Here “ears” refers to the ability to hear. Alternate translation: “you have enabled me to hear your commands” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## mi62
This is an exaggeration to show that these things were not the most important to God. Alternate translation: “animals burned on the altar and other offerings for our sins are not what you require most” (See: [[figs-hyperbole]])

# 40:7
## jn6f
This refers to a scroll on which was written the word of Yahweh. Alternate translation: “the written scroll” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 40:8
## va1l
Here “my heart” refers to the inner being of the writer. Alternate translation: “I am always thinking about your laws within my inner being” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 40:9
## k2b6
“I have told a large assembly of people the good news of your righteousness.”

## epq1
This refers to the good news that God rescues his people. Alternate translation: “good news that because you are righteous, you rescue your people” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

## gk2t
Here “my lips” represents the writer, emphasizing his speech. Alternate translation: “I have not stopped myself from proclaiming these things” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 40:10
## vb9c
“I have not kept your righteousness a secret.” This can also be stated in positive form. Alternate translation: “I have openly told every one about your righteousness” (See: [[figs-litotes]])

## am3c
Here this refers to the writer’s inner being. (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## cn4q
This can be stated in positive form. Alternate translation: “I have told everyone in the great assembly about your covenant faithfulness or your trustworthiness” (See: [[figs-litotes]])

## bp5z
The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be stated as “faithful.” Alternate translation: “how faithful you are to your covenant” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## u78d
This abstract noun “trustworthiness” can be stated as “trustworthy.” Alternate translation: “how trustworthy you are” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 40:11
## qc48
Here “covenant faithfulness” and “trustworthiness” are spoken of as if they were living people who could protect the writer. Alternate translation: “I want your covenant faithfulness and your trustworthiness to always preserve” (See: [[figs-personification]])

# 40:12
## c6b2
Here troubles are spoken of as if they were objects that surround and trap the speaker. Alternate translation: “there are more troubles around me than I can count” or “more troubles come to me than I can count” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ra9w
This is stated in negative form to intensify the number.See how you translated this in [Psalms 40:5](../040/005.md). Alternate translation: “that are vast in number” (See: [[figs-litotes]])

## ff9r
This refers to the consequences of his sin. Alternate translation: “the consequences of my iniquities” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## qng1
The writer’s iniquities are spoken of as if they were his enemies who were harming him. (See: [[figs-personification]])

## x56q
Versions differ in how to understand this difficult passage. It may mean that the speaker is crying so much that he cannot see anything because of his tears.

## ixl8
Here “heart” refers to the writer’s inner confidence. Alternate translation: “I am very discouraged” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 40:14
## hl37
This can be reordered and stated in active form. Alternate translation: “Let those who pursue my life to take it awy be ashamed and completely disappointed” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## l9j5
“Please make them ashamed and completely disappointed”

## ff5k
Here “pursue my life” means they desire to kill the writer. The writer is represented by his “life.” Alternate translation: “who are trying to kill me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## knx2
This can be reordered and stated in active form. Alternate translation: “Let those who delight in hurting me be turned back and brought to dishonor” or “Please have someone turn back those who delight in hurting me and bring them to dishonor” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## k5tz
“unable to continue”

# 40:15
## fqa6
“Let those who say to me, ‘Aha, aha!’ be shocked because of their shame”

## i1aw
“I hope that they will be shocked when you shame them”

## rbg9
These words indicate that the speaker has seen the hearer doing evil that the hearer did not think anyone knew about. You can use here words in your language that mean the same thing but sound different. See how this is translated in [Psalms 35:21](../035/021.md). (See: [[figs-exclamations]])

# 40:16
## az21
These two phrases mean the same thing and emphasize the intensity of joy. Alternate translation: “be very joyful” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## yq7n
The abstract noun “salvation” can be stated as an action. Alternate translation: “love you because you saved them” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 40:17
## v567
These words mean the same thing and emphasize how helpless the writer is. Alternate translation: “very needy” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## ep4r
“the Lord cares for me”

## a8vb
These phrases mean the same thing. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## g2mh
“You are the one who helps me”

## zf6l
“you come to save me”

## c1t7
This can be stated in positive form. Alternate translation: “respond quickly” (See: [[figs-litotes]])

# 41:intro
## q9l9
See [[PSA-q9l9]]
# 41:1
## y6js
See [[PSA-y6js]]
## ay4z
“This is for the director of music to use in worship.”

## bd73
The words “he” and “him” refer to anyone who is concerned for the weak.

## glk5
“weak people” or “poor people”

# 41:2
## j2lj
These words refer to anyone who is concerned for the weak.

# 41:3
## lt8b
The phrase “the bed of suffering” refers to when a person lies in bed because he is sick. Alternate translation: “When he is sick and in bed, Yahweh will support him” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## ygd6
The phrase “a bed of healing” refers to when a person rests in bed and recovers from his sickness. Alternate translation: “you, Yahweh, will heal him of his sickness” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 41:5
## yg22
If a person’s name dies, it means that people forget that he had ever lived. Alternate translation: “when will his name perish” or “when will people forget about him” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]] and [[figs-idiom]])

# 41:6
## evn1
The words “my enemy” refers to any enemy in general, and not to one specific enemy.

## m4zm
Possible meanings are (1) “he says meaningless things” or (2) his enemies say things to make him think that they are his friends when they are not. Alternate translation: “he says deceitful things” or “they pretend to be concerned about me” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## c5vp
His enemies try to learn all of the bad things about him. Here the word “heart” refers the whole person. Bad circumstances are spoken of as if they were objects that can be gathered. Alternate translation: “he tries to learn about all of my disasters” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 41:7
## sq8r
Possible meanings are (1) “they hope that very bad things will happen to me” or (2) “they are planning to hurt me.”

# 41:8
## l22y
His enemies speak of “disease” as if it were a person who has captured him. Alternate translation: “He is sick with a fatal disease” (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## hfg4
Possible meanings are (1) “A fatal disease” or (2) “Something evil”

## cay3
Here the words “lying down” refer to lying in bed because of illness. That he will not “rise up” means that he will continue to lie down, which is a euphemism for death. Alternate translation: “now that he is sick in bed, he will die there” (See: [[figs-explicit]] and [[figs-euphemism]])

# 41:9
## jzy3
This is an idiom that means his friend betrayed him. Alternate translation: “has betrayed me” or “has turned against me” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 41:10
## r3b3
This is a request. Alternate translation: “Please, Yahweh, have mercy on me and raise me up” (See: [[figs-declarative]])

## cz3d
This means to raise him up from his bed, or to make him recover from his disease. Alternate translation: “make me well” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## h6l4
The writer speaks of revenge on his enemies as if it were paying to them what he owes. Alternate translation: “so that I may take revenge on them” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 41:11
## m2j9
The word “this” refers to what the writer will say next. For clarity, the clauses may be reversed. Alternate translation: “Because my enemy does not triumph over me, I know that you delight in me” (See: [[figs-events]])

## h7zl
This can also be translated in future tense, since Yahweh has not yet healed him. Alternate translation: “If you enable me to do that, with the result that my enemies do not defeat me, I will know that you are pleased with me” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 41:12
## dfw3
“you support me because of my integrity”

## jj35
The writer speaks of being in Yahweh’s presence as being in a place where Yahweh can see him and he can see Yahweh’s face. Alternate translation: “will keep me with you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 41:13
## s4va
See [[PSA-s4va]]
## xi7f
This refers to two extremes and means for all time. Alternate translation: “for all eternity” (See: [[figs-merism]])

## d4ws
The word “Amen” is repeated to emphasize approval of what has been said. Alternate translation: “May it certainly be so” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 42:intro
## mu68
See [[PSA-mu68]]
# 42:1
## t39i
See [[PSA-t39i]]
## rt7c
“This is for the director of music to use in worship.”

## c3mx
This may refer to a style of music. See how you translated this in [Psalms 32:1](../032/001.md).

## h2nj
The author compares his desire for God to the desire of a thirsty deer for water.

## mi8s
heavy breathing from an animal or person that is very tired or thirsty

## flj9
The author speaks of his strong desire for God as if it were a strong thirst for water. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 42:2
## xe9q
The author speaks of his strong desire for God as if it were a strong thirst for water. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## bsl8
The author does not ask this question to get an answer but to show his strong desire to be before God. (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

# 42:3
## mfk4
The author refers to his tears as if they are food that he eats. This means that he is so sad that he cannot eat. Alternate translation: “My tears are like my food and I eat nothing else” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-explicit]])

## nw17
This phrase refers to the entire day by referring to both its beginning and end. Alternate translation: “all day long” (See: [[figs-merism]])

## hy3m
This is an exaggeration. His enemies are not saying this constantly; they are saying it often. (See: [[figs-hyperbole]])

## sa8l
The author’s enemies use this question to mock him and to express that they do not see his God helping him. Alternate translation: “Your God is not here to help you” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

# 42:4
## d12n
This is an idiom that means to remember or think about something. Alternate translation: “remember” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## k59b
Here the word “soul” refers to the emotions. The author speaks of his soul as if it is a liquid that he pours out. The phrase means that he is expressing his emotional grief. Alternate translation: “I express my sorrow” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## c6f8
“the crowd of people”

## gv3q
This phrase uses two different words to express one idea. Alternate translation: “joyful praise” (See: [[figs-hendiadys]])

# 42:5
## xs1j
The author refers to his inner self as his “soul,” which represents himself. He asks these questions to rebuke himself. Alternate translation: “I should not be bowed down. I should not be worried” (See: [[figs-rquestion]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

## cc84
The writer speaks of depression or discouragement as if it were his soul being bent over. Alternate translation: “discouraged” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## fyf2
The writer continues to speak to his own soul and commands it to trust God. (See: [[figs-imperative]])

# 42:6
## lp5z
The writer begins to speak to God about his soul.

## s443
This phrase means to remember or to think about something. Alternate translation: “I think of you” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## u6xn
This is probably a reference to northern Israel, where the Jordan river originates. Alternate translation: “the land where the Jordan river begins” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## ka3s
mountain tops

## xh39
This is the name of a hill at the base of Mount Hermon. (See: [[translate-names]])

# 42:7
## c6aq
The word “deep” refers to deep waters, which here are likely the streams rushing down Mount Hermon. The writer speaks of them as if they are people calling out to one another as they hear the sound of their own descent from the mountain. (See: [[figs-personification]])

## exq2
The author speaks of his great misfortune and sadness as if they are deep waters that drown him with one wave after another. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## d5k7
The word “billows” is another word for “waves.” Together the two words emphasize the greatness of the waves. Alternate translation: “all of your great waves” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 42:8
## ef4n
The writer speaks of Yahweh’s covenant faithfulness as if it were a person whom he commands to be with him. The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “Yahweh will show me his covenant faithfulness in the daytime” or “Yahweh will show me in the daytime how faithful he is to his covenant” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## jsc8
Possible meanings are (1) “the song that he gives me” or (2) “the song about him”

## xm7t
“the God who gives me life”

# 42:9
## si6j
The writer speaks of God as if he were a huge rock that would provide protection from enemy attack. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## b1ik
To “go mourning” is to perform customs related to being very sad.

# 42:10
## bp1m
The writer describes his adversaries’ rebukes as his receiving a fatal wound. (See: [[figs-simile]])

## r4wg
This is an exaggeration; his enemies are not saying this constantly but are saying it often. (See: [[figs-hyperbole]])

## ae82
The writer’s enemies use this question to mock him and to express that they do not see God helping him. Alternate translation: “Your God is not here to help you” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

# 42:11
## evd8
The author refers to his inner self as his “soul,” which represents himself. He asks these questions to rebuke himself. See how you translated this in [Psalms 42:5](../042/005.md). Alternate translation: “I should not be bowed down, I should not be worried” (See: [[figs-rquestion]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

## wp6h
The writer speaks of depression or discouragement as if it were his soul being bent over. See how you translated this in [Psalms 42:5](../042/005.md). Alternate translation: “discouraged” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ghd7
The writer continues to speak to his own soul and commands it to trust God. See how you translated this in [Psalms 42:5](../042/005.md). (See: [[figs-imperative]])

## il4d

# 43:2
## quk8
Possible meanings are (1) “the God who protects me” or (2) “the God who gives me strength.”

## a96e
The writer asks these questions in order to complain to God and express his emotions, not to receive an answer. (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## cpw2
To “go about in mourning” is to perform customs related to being very sad.

## d84h
The word “oppression” can be translated as a verb. Alternate translation: “because my enemy oppresses me” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 43:3
## e7jd

## uhy4

## rr6l
