## s96j
This probably tells what musical style or tune to use when singing the psalm. Alternate translation: “sing this psalm using the tune of ‘Al Tashheth’” or “sing this using the Al Tashheth style”

## yl31
This means “Do Not Destroy.” Translators may either write the meaning or copy the Hebrew words. (See: [[translate-unknown]] and [[translate-transliterate]])

## g4tb
Possible meanings are (1) David wrote the psalm or (2) the psalm is about David or (3) the psalm is in the style of David’s psalms.

## jt8t
The meaning of the word “michtam” is uncertain. You may use the word “psalm” instead. This can be written as: “This is a psalm that David wrote.” See how you translated this in [Psalms 16:1](../016/001.md).

## wv56
Going to Yahweh for protection is spoken of as taking refuge in him. Alternate translation: “I go to you for protection” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## yn99
The psalmist speaks of God as if he were a mother bird that protects its babies by huddling them under its wings. Alternate translation: “I trust you to protect me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## s371
The abstract noun “destruction” can be stated as “destructive.” Alternate translation: “until this destructive storm is over” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 57:2
## r2mu
This explains why he will cry out to God. It can be translated with “because.” Alternate translation: “because he does all things for me”

# 57:3
## k9zh
The enemies’ fierce attack is spoken of as if they were crushing his body by marching on it. Alternate translation: “those who attack me severely” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## t1vd
God’s being kind and faithful is spoken of as if he were sending his kindness and faithful. The abstract nouns “kindness” and “faithfulness” can be stated as “kind” and “trustworthy.” Alternate translation: “God will be kind to me and trustworthy” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 57:4
## v2nz
The psalmist speaks of his enemies as if they were lions. Alternate translation: “I live among fierce enemies” or “Fierce enemies surround me like lions” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## e5fn
Destroying is spoken of as devouring or eating something up. Some versions understand the Hebrew text to mean “fiery beasts.” Both images speak of his enemies as if they were wild beasts. Alternate translation: “those who are ready to destroy me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## j2hr
The enemies’ spears and arrows are spoken of as if they were lions’ teeth. The psalmist continues to speak of his enemies as if they were lions. Alternate translation: “people who kill others with spears and arrows as lions kill with their sharp teeth” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## zdv3
Since both of these terms are weapons, if your culture knows only one, it is acceptable to use it alone. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## nz7w
The tongue represents what someone says, and the enemies’ cruel words are spoken of as if they were swords. Alternate translation: “whose cruel words are like sharp swords” or “who cause terrible trouble for me by what they say” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 57:5
## t2dt
The psalmist is asking God to show that he is exalted. Being exalted above the heavens represents being great. Alternate translation: “God, show that you are exalted above the heavens” or “God, show that you are great in the heavens” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ij37
The psalmist is asking God to show his glory. Alternate translation: “show your glory over all the earth”

# 57:6
## ywr3
His enemies’ plans to capture him are spoken of as if they had spread out a net on the ground to trap him. Alternate translation: “It is as though my enemies have spread a net out to trap me” or “They planned to capture me like people who spread out a net to trap an animal” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## pp5u
His enemies’ plans to capture him are spoken of as if they had dug a pit for him to fall into. Alternate translation: “It is as though they dug a pit for me to fall into” or “They planned to capture me like people who dig a hole in the ground to trap an animal” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## cj6r
The harm that came to his enemies when they tried to capture him is spoken of as if they fell into the trap that they had made for him. Alternate translation: “They themselves fell into the pit they had dug for me” or “But they themselves were hurt by what they planned to do to me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 57:7
## mvj7
Being confident is spoken of as one’s heart being firm rather than shaken or easily moved. The phrase is repeated to show that he has complete confidence in God and will not change. Alternate translation: “I am completely confident in you, God” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## gt62
Who he will sing to can be stated clearly. Alternate translation: “I will sing praises to you, God” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 57:8
## z1em
It can be stated clearly that the purpose of waking up is to sing praises to God. Waking up may be a metaphor for starting or preparing to do something. The heart represents the psalmist or his emotions. Alternate translation: “Wake up, my honored heart, to sing praises to God” or “I will prepare my honored heart to sing praises to God” or “I am honored to wake up and sing praises to God” (See: [[figs-explicit]] and [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

## yl5r
It can be stated clearly that the purpose of waking up is to sing praises to God. The psalmist speaks as though the lute and harp were people who could wake up to sing praises to God. Alternate translation: “Wake up, lute and harp, and sing praises to God” or “I will play the lute and harp while I sing praises to God” (See: [[figs-explicit]] and [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## hr4g
The dawn is spoken of as if it were alive, and getting up before dawn happens is spoken of as waking it up. The purpose of getting up before dawn is to praise God. Alternate translation: “I will get up before dawn” or “I will get up before the sun rises” (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-explicit]])

# 57:10
## vaa3
These two phrases are very similar in meaning. The greatness of God’s unfailing love and the greatness of his faithfulness are spoken of as if they could be measured in distance. (See: [[figs-parallelism]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## tna7
The greatness of God’s unfailing love is spoken of as if it could be measured in distance. Alternate translation: “Your unfailing love is as great as the distance from the earth to the heavens” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ywg7
The words “great is your” and “reaching” are understood from the previous phrase. Alternate translation: “great is your faithfulness, reaching to the clouds” or “your faithfulness is as great as the distance from the earth to the clouds” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 57:11
## yyx8
The psalmist is asking God to show that he is exalted. Being exalted above the heavens represents being great. Alternate translation: “God, show that you are exalted above the heavens” or “God, show that you are great in the heavens” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## n64e
The psalmist is asking God to show his glory. Alternate translation: “show your glory over all the earth”

## x97c
Possible meanings are (1) David wrote the psalm or (2) the psalm is about David or (3) the psalm is in the style of David’s psalms.

## xu51
The author uses this question to rebuke the rulers because they do not speak righteously. Alternate translation: “You rulers do not say what is right!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## f3j3
The author uses this question to rebuke the judges who do not judge uprightly. Alternate translation: “You people never judge people uprightly!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

# 58:2
## n278
The words “you” and “your” refer to the mighty men who are judges ([Psalm 58:1](../058/001.md)) and so is plural. (See: [[figs-you]])

## c5jn
The author answers the two questions he had just asked.

## d1u5
The heart refers to the people’s thoughts or plans. Alternate translation: “you commit wickedness in your thoughts” or “you think about doing wicked things” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## fc72
Doing violence in various places throughout the land is spoken of as distributing or spreading the violence throughout the land, as if violence were some kind of stuff or things. Alternate translation: “you yourselves do violent deeds everywhere in the land” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 58:3
## e66x
This is the same idea expressed in two different ways. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## d7k2
Doing wrong things is spoken of as if people are walking on a road, and they turn off and go the wrong way. Alternate translation: “they do wrong things” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 58:4
## mff7
The wicked things people say are spoken of as if they were poison. Alternate translation: “Their wicked words cause trouble as a snake’s poison harms people” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-simile]])

## f4ca
Wicked people who do not listen to advice or rebukes are spoken of as if they were snakes that do not respond to a charmer’s music. Alternate translation: “they refuse to listen like a deaf adder that stops up its ears” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## tt5a
An adder that does not respond to a charmer’s music is spoken of as if it could put something in its ears so that it will not hear. Alternate translation: “an adder that does not listen” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## w1f7
a kind of poisonous snake

# 58:5
## b6id
people who play or sing music in order to control snakes

## hi9v
What the snake charmers were skillful at can be stated clearly. Alternate translation: “no matter how skillful the charmers are at controlling snakes” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 58:6
## ptb3
See [[PSA-ptb3]]
## x2zu
In both of these phrases, the wicked people are spoken of as if they were lions, and making them powerless to kill people is spoken of as breaking their teeth. Alternate translation: “Take away their power to kill. Make them powerless like young lions whose teeth have been broken and fallen out” (See: [[figs-parallelism]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 58:7
## na9t
The wicked people are spoken of as if they were ice or water. No longer existing is spoken of as melting or draining away into the dry ground. Alternate translation: “Make them disappear like water that runs off” or “Make them vanish like ice that melts and drains into the ground” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-simile]])

## c9dm
“let their arrows be as though they had no points”

# 58:8
## hb5w
No longer existing is spoken of as melting and disappearing. Alternate translation: “Let the wicked vanish like a snail that melts and no longer exists” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## hi5z
small animal that the Israelites considered unclean and that looks like it is melting as it moves by sliding over slime it has produced

## uu2z
Not existing is spoken of as being like a baby that is born dead. Alternate translation: “like a baby who is born too early too live and see the sunlight” or “like a baby that was born dead” (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 58:9
## ut8v
The wicked are spoken of as if they were thornbush branches, and God’s swift punishment of them is spoken of as if he were to quickly blow them away or sweep them away. Alternate translation: “God will destroy wicked people faster than a whirlwind can blow away thornbush branches that have been put under a cooking pot and lit with fire” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## khw3
David is speaking to God’s people, so this is plural. (See: [[figs-you]])

## ka8t
“the heat from the burning thorn branches … the green thorn branches and the burning thorn branches”

# 58:10
## wz3e
The phrase “the righteous” refers to righteous people in general. Alternate translation: “Righteous people will rejoice when they see” (See: [[figs-genericnoun]])

## gi2k
Getting one’s feet wet by walking on blood is spoken of as washing the feet in blood. Alternate translation: “the righteous will make their feet wet in the blood of the wicked” or “the righteous will march on the blood of the wicked” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ll57
This exaggeration expresses that a great number of wicked people will die. Alternate translation: “so many wicked people will die that when the righteous march on their blood, it will seem as if they could wash their feet in it” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-hyperbole]])

## w4sd

“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## me33
This probably tells what musical style or tune to use when singing the psalm. See how you translated this in [Psalms 57:1](../057/001.md).

## il5y
Possible meanings are (1) David wrote the psalm or (2) the psalm is about David or (3) the psalm is in the style of David’s psalms.

## ks3t
The meaning of the word “michtam” is uncertain. You may use the word “psalm” instead. This can be written as: “This is a psalm that David wrote.” See how you translated this in [Psalms 16:1](../016/001.md).

## hk4w
A high place represents a safe place where his enemies cannot reach him. Alternate translation: “put me in a safe place” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## rjh7
Rising up against someone represents attacking him. Alternate translation: “attack me” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 59:2
## ica6
The word “bloodthirsty” contains “blood,” which refers to murder and “thirsty,” which refers to desire. Alternate translation: “people who desire to kill” or “people who like to kill people” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 59:3
## c6a4
David’s enemies are in hiding and are waiting quietly for the time when they can attack him. (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 59:4
## zre5
Deciding to do something and beginning to do it is spoken of as waking up. Alternate translation: “do something” or “take action” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## b239
What he wants God to see can be stated clearly. Alternate translation: “and see what is happening to me” or “and see what they are doing to me” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 59:5
## shi6
Deciding to do something and beginning to do it is spoken of as getting up. Alternate translation: “do something” or “take action” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## t4a1
The word “nations” here represents the people of the nations that do not honor God. Alternate translation: “the people of all the nations” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 59:6
## aej6
The word “they” refers to the wicked transgressors.

## r2ww
The psalmist speaks of his enemies threatening to attack people as if they were dogs howling, growling, or barking at people. Alternate translation: “they threaten to attack people” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## fcr7
Why they go around the city can be stated clearly. Alternate translation: “go around the city to attack anyone they find” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 59:7
## i5i6
Here the word “See” is being used to draw attention to something. Alternate translation: “Hear”

## rh1u
Saying terrible things is spoken of as belching. These terrible things may have been insults or threats. Alternate translation: “they say terrible things” or “they shout out terrible words” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## q9fv
burp loudly; allow air from the stomach to come out of the mouth with a loud, rude noise

## vs38
The cruel things that the wicked people were saying are spoken of as if they were swords. Alternate translation: “they say cruel things that cause people trouble as much as swords destroy people” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## d23a
This question is used to show that they believed that God would not hear and punish them. Alternate translation: “No one can hear us!” or “Your God does not hear us!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

# 59:8
## k3ws
“laugh at them scornfully” or “mock them.” God would laugh at them because they are worthless and powerless.

## x3cx
“you ridicule all the nations” or “you know that the people of the nations are fools”

## tjt6
ridicule

# 59:9
## av6p
God’s being the psalmist’s strength represents God protecting him. Alternate translation: “you are my strength” or “you are my protector” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## mi4w
A high tower is a place that people could go to for shelter from their enemies. The psalmist speaks of God protecting him as if God were a strong, safe shelter. Alternate translation: “you protect me like a high tower” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 59:10
## v7d9
This phrase implies that God will come to him in order to save him. The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated with an adjective. Alternate translation: “My God, who is faithful to his covenant, will come to save me” or “My God will come to save me because he is faithful to his covenant” (See: [[figs-explicit]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## tb7v
The abstract noun “desire” can be expressed with the verb “want.” Alternate translation: “what I want to happen to my enemies” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 59:11
## c9tk
“Cause them to wander around”

## yf94
God’s protecting the righteous is spoken of as if God were a shield. Alternate translation: “our protector” or “the one who protects us like a shield” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 59:12
## iz4q
The mouths and lips represent the things people say. Alternate translation: “Because they sin by what they say” or “Because of the sinful things they say” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## a3ed
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “let people capture them because of their pride” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## xb2v
“that they say”

# 59:13
## u1ga
Destroying them completely is spoken of either as burning them up or eating them. Alternate translation: “Be angry with them and destroy them completely so there will be no more of them” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## h4zf
Jacob here refers to Israel. Alternate translation: “in Israel” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## ct9i
“to even the most distance places on earth.” This represents all places on earth. Alternate translation: “everywhere on earth” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 59:14
## v4xe
The psalmist speaks of his enemies threatening to attack people as if they were dogs howling, growling, or barking at people. Alternate translation: “threatening to attack us” or “threatening to attack us like wild dogs” (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 59:15
## w18t
content, having everything they want

# 59:16
## a9we
High towers and refuges are places that people can go to for shelter from their enemies. The psalmist speaks of God protecting him as if God were a strong, safe shelter. Alternate translation: “you have protected me like a high tower and a refuge” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## vmt2
“whenever I have had troubles”

# 59:17
## q7yw
“To you, my strength” can be combined as one clause. Alternate translation: “You are my strength, so I will sing praises to you” (See: [[figs-sentences]])

## g4db
God’s being the psalmist’s strength represents God protecting him. Alternate translation: “my protector” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## m2u5
High towers are places that people can go to for shelter from their enemies. The psalmist speaks of God protecting him as if God were a strong, safe shelter. Alternate translation: “you have protected me like a high tower” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## shn4
The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated with an adjective. This can be expressed in a separate sentence. Alternate translation: “He is the God who is faithful to his covenant” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 60:intro
## wza8
See [[PSA-wza8]]
# 60:1
## ev3m
See [[PSA-ev3m]]
## usc3
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## vsl6
This probably tells what tune or musical style to use when singing the psalm. Alternate translation: “sing this psalm using the tune of ‘Shushan Eduth’” or “sing this using the Shushan Eduth style”

## m8be
This means “Lily of the Promise.” Translators may either write the meaning or copy the Hebrew words. (See: [[translate-unknown]] and [[translate-transliterate]])

## tb2l
The meaning of the word “michtam” is uncertain. You may use the word “psalm” instead. This can be written as: “This is a psalm that David wrote.” See how you translated this in [Psalms 16:1](../016/001.md).

## x59t
“Aram of the two rivers … the Aramean nation of Zobah.” These are places. (See: [[translate-names]])

## xt5a
This refers to Joab and the army that he led. Alternate translation: “Joab and his army” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## uk1f
“12,000 Edomites” (See: [[translate-numbers]])

## jey3
God’s rejecting people is spoken of as if he had thrown them away. Alternate translation: “you have rejected us” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## tsh1
God’s allowing Israel’s enemies to break through their defenses is spoken of as God himself had done it. Alternate translation: “you have allowed our enemies to break through our defenses” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 60:2
## cda8
See [[PSA-cda8]]
## rmg6
The psalmist speaks of the disaster in his country as if it were an earthquake. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## qsa7
Making the people strong again is spoken of as repairing the fissures in the ground or walls. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## n526
large cracks in the ground or walls

# 60:3
## k155
Here “see” represents “experience” or “suffer.” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## m2ay
Being helpless is spoken of as staggering around, barely able to stand upright. The abstract noun “staggering” can be stated as a verb. Alternate translation: “the wine that makes us stagger” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 60:4
## fj97
God’s guiding his people in battle is spoken of as if God were a human king or commander who had set up a banner for the army. Alternate translation: “you are like a king who sets up a banner” or “you command us in battle like a king who raises up a banner” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## f9q6
“battle flag.” This is a flag that a king or commander would raise up on a pole to show that the army should gather.

## xr7x
This can be stated with an active clause. However some versions have different interpretations of this phrase. Alternate translation: “to display against those who carry the bow” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## pya3
The phrase “those who carry the bow” refers to the enemy soldiers in battle. Alternate translation: “to display when he takes his army into battle against your enemies” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 60:5
## lb5k
God’s right hand represents his power. Alternate translation: “by your power” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## p226
Answering here represents responding to his request. Alternate translation: “respond to my request” or “answer my prayer” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 60:7
## ft6i
God speaks of the tribe of Ephraim as if it were his army. The helmet symbolizes equipment for war. Alternate translation: “Ephraim is like a helmet I have chosen” or “the tribe of Ephraim is my army” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## d6zr
a hard hat that soldiers wear to protect their heads from injury

## c5sk
God chose men from the tribe of Judah to be the kings of his people, and he speaks of that tribe as if it were his scepter. Alternate translation: “the tribe of Judah is like my scepter” or “Judah is the tribe through whom I rule my people” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 60:8
## k3r4
God speaks of Moab being unimportant as if Moab were a washbasin or a lowly servant. Alternate translation: “Moab is like a bowl that I use for washing” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## lax6
God was probably speaking of taking ownership of Edom as if he were symbolically throwing his shoe onto that land to show that he owns it. However some versions have other interpretations. Alternate translation: “I take ownership of the land of Edom” or “I throw my shoe onto the land of Edom to show that it is mine” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[translate-symaction]])

# 60:10
## ika5
The psalmist uses this question to express his sadness that it seems that God has rejected them. Alternate translation: “But God, it seems like you have rejected us.” or “God, you seem to have abandoned us.” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## v89k
The psalmist speaks of God helping their army as if God were to go and fight with them. Alternate translation: “you do not help our army when we go into battle” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 60:11
## sm5b
“is worthless”

# 60:12
## x5wt
“will defeat our enemies”

## i34s
The psalmist speaks of God helping their army defeat their enemies as if God were to trample down the enemies. Alternate translation: “he will enable us to trample down our enemies” or “he will make us able to defeat our enemies” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 61:1
## u44c
See [[PSA-u44c]]
## y257
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## w7m6
“people should play a stringed instrument with this song”

## dkq1
These clauses have a similar meaning. Alternate translation: “God, listen to me and answer my prayer” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 61:2
## z96p
Here the writer speaks of God as if he were a high rock that he could climb for protection. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 61:4
## fq5b
Going to Yahweh for protection is spoken of as taking refuge in him. Here there is a second metaphor that speaks of Yahweh’s protection as if he was a hen protecting her baby chicks under her wings. Alternate translation: “go to you for protection as a chick is safe under the wings of its mother” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 61:5
## yk96
The writer speaks of God’s blessings as if they were an inheritance that he has received. Alternate translation: “you have given to me the blessings” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## jwf1
Here “your name” means God himself. Alternate translation: “who honor you” or “who have an awesome respect for you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 61:6
## f381
These two clauses have similar meanings. The idea is repeated for emphasis. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## m1j7
“You will extend the king’s life” or “You will cause the king’s life to last a long time”

## dq7t
Here “years” refers to how long the king will live. Alternate translation: “he will live for many generations” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 61:7
## j14f
Here “to remain before God” means to be in God’s presence or to be with God. This can be stated clearly in the translation. Alternate translation: “God will be with him forever” or “God will be with the king forever” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 61:8
## ut6s
Here “name” stands for God himself. Alternate translation: “I will always sing praise to you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## yd7n
These refer to the promise to offer sacrifices to God every day.

# 62:intro
## dc2q
See [[PSA-dc2q]]
# 62:1
## fc8k
See [[PSA-fc8k]]
## a4ay
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## zun4
One of David’s chief musicians had this same name. This may refer to him. See how you translated this in [Psalms 39:1](../039/001.md). (See: [[translate-names]])

## l5l8
“he is the one who rescues me” or “he is the one who saves me”

# 62:2
## hy6d
The writer speaks of God’s ability to protect him as if God were a rock. Alternate translation: “He is the only one who can protect and rescue me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ngh3
The writer speaks of God’s ability to protect him as if God were a high tower. Alternate translation: “he keeps me away from the grasp of my enemies” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## s4ie
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “nothing can ever move me” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 62:3
## b6ts
“my enemies” or “all my enemies”

## z326
David uses a rhetorical question to express his frustration. No answer is expected. Alternate translation: “It seems like my enemies will never stop attacking me. I feel that I am as weak against you as a leaning wall or a broken-down fence.” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## c4q6
“attack me”

# 62:4
## n82a
“They intend to” or “They plan to”

## a18i
In these verses, David is referring to himself by “him.”

## j3uz
This refers to their speech or their words. (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## zqm3
This refers to their thoughts. (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 62:5
## nl4l
“for I place my hope in him”

# 62:6
## fy6x
The writer speaks of God as if he were a rock and a high tower. Both of these metaphors show how God provides protection from one’s enemies. Here “salvation” means that God rescues the writer. See how you translated this in [Psalms 62:2](../062/002.md). (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## izy6
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “nothing can move me” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 62:7
## c9fh
The writer speaks of God as if he were a rock that keeps one safe from his enemies. He also speaks of God as if he were a shelter that provides protection. Alternate translation: “God always gives me strength and protection” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 62:8
## yq3j
This refers to telling God your inner feelings as if you were pouring out a liquid. Alternate translation: “give your deepest concerns to God” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## ss3p
The word “us” refers to David and the people he is speaking to. (See: [[figs-exclusive]])

# 62:9
## zu93
This refers to men of all levels of wealth and importance. The phrases “are vanity” and “are a lie” have the same meaning. One cannot confidently trust in anyone. Alternate translation: “you cannot place your trust in men, no matter how important they are” (See: [[figs-merism]] and [[figs-parallelism]])

## ckm7
If you put all of these kinds of men together on a scale, they would have no weight. This means that they have no real value to you.

# 62:10
## ubx1
These two words have basically the same meaning. You cannot trust in money that you get by taking it from other people. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## eu3d
The writer speaks of riches as if they were trees or vines that could bear fruit. Alternate translation: “for they will provide nothing good for you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## j6sj
Here “fix your heart” is an idiom that means to desire something greatly. Alternate translation: “do not desire them” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 62:11
## x8ts
This means that God has said this more than once.

## kc1v
God being characterized by power is spoken of as if power belonged to him. The abstract noun “power” can be translated with an adjective. Alternate translation: “God is powerful” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 62:12
## n56f
God being characterized by covenant faithfulness is spoken of as if covenant faithfulness belonged to him. The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated with an adjective. Alternate translation: “You, Lord, are also faithful to your covenant” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## gl1p
The writer speaks of God’s rewards as if he were paying a wage for work. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 63:intro
## py5b
See [[PSA-py5b]]
# 63:1
## rct4
See [[PSA-rct4]]
## jrr4
Possible meanings are (1) David wrote the psalm or (2) the psalm is about David or (3) the psalm is in the style of David’s psalms.

## d7d1
sincerely

## c3we
These two clauses have basically the same meaning and are used together to emphasize how greatly the writer desires to be with God. Alternate translation: “my whole being greatly desires to be with you” (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## x4mg
“hot, dry desert”

# 63:3
## w2ui
The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated with an adverb and the abstract noun “life” can be translated with a verbal phrase. Alternate translation: “I value you being faithful to your covenant more than I value living, so my lips” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## cx75
Here “my lips” represents the whole person. Alternate translation: “I will praise you” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 63:4
## vx4a
Here “in your name” means “to you.” Alternate translation: “I will worship you and pray to you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 63:5
## x5ky
Here the writer speaks of knowing and worshiping God as being more satisfying than eating a good meal. Alternate translation: “I will be happier than a person who eats a meal of fat and choice food” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## y596
Here “with joyful lips my mouth” represents the whole person who will praise God joyfully. Alternate translation: “I will praise you joyfully” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 63:6
## a4ez
These two clauses have the same meaning. The ideas are repeated to emphasize how much the writer thinks about God. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

# 63:7
## ca2e
The writer speaks of God as if he were a bird protecting its young under his wings. Alternate translation: “I rejoice because you protect me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 63:8
## y8gh
“I need you” or “I depend on you”

## ua1a
Here, the right hand is used as a symbol of strength and power. Alternate translation: “you support me” or “you lift me up” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 63:9
## tm7l
This means they will die and go to the place of the dead. This can be stated clearly in the translation. Alternate translation: “will die and descend into the place of the dead” or “will die and go down into the place of the dead” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 63:10
## y78j
Here “the sword” represents death in battle, and “those whose hands use the sword” refers to enemies who kill them in battle. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “God will cause them to die in battle” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

## i1md
Here “they” refers to the corpses of those who die in battle. Alternate translation: “jackals will eat their dead bodies” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## ru7l
“jackals” here are a kind of long-legged wild dog. They feed on carrion, game, and fruit.

# 63:11
## q4st
David is speaking about himself. This can be stated clearly in the translation. Alternate translation: “I, the king of Israel, will” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## lcq4
The word “him” refers to “God.”

## a434
Here “the mouth” represents the whole person. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “but God will silence the liars” or “but God will silence those who lie” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

# 64:intro
## t6rs
See [[PSA-t6rs]]
# 64:1
## b1fk
See [[PSA-b1fk]]
## j144
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## y5d6
save

# 64:2
## aj26
Here “Hide” represents protecting, and “the secret plotting of evildoers represents” represents the harm that evildoers secretly plan to do to David. Alternate translation: “Protect me from the harm that evil doers secretly plan to do to me” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## czb5
The words “hide me” are understood from the previous phrase and can be repeated here. Alternate translation: “hide me from the commotion” or “protect me from the commotion”(See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

## u721
Possible meanings are that “commotion” refers to (1) a noisy disturbance. Alternate translation: “the noisy disturbance that the doers of iniquity make” or (2) a crowd that makes a noisy disturbance. Alternate translation: “the noisy crowd of doers of iniquity”

# 64:3
## zhn8
The writer speaks of his enemies’ tongues as if they were as sharp as swords. Here “tongues” represents the harsh words that the enemies speak. Alternate translation: “The harsh things that they say hurt me like a sharp sword” (See: [[figs-simile]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

## ugs8
The writer speaks of his enemies’ bitter words as if they were arrows being shot at him. Alternate translation: “bitter words which pierce me like arrows” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 64:5
## blg6
The evildoers do not expect an answer to their question because they think no one will see them. Alternate translation: “No one will see what we are doing” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

# 64:6
## jn8k
The writer speaks of man’s “inner thoughts” and “hearts of man” as if they were a deep body of water that no one can explore all the way to the bottom. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## mfc5
Both of these phrases refer to man’s private or inner thoughts. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 64:7
## g91b
See [[PSA-g91b]]
## a77p
The writer speaks of God’s punishment of the evildoers as if God were shooting arrows at them. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 64:8
## xs48
The writer speaks of God’s causing the evildoers’ plans to fail as if God were making them stumble in their paths. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “God will make them stumble” or “God will cause their plans to fail” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

## f4zp
Here “tongues” represents the words that they say. Alternate translation: “since the words that they say are against them” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 64:9
## gv21
“what God has done”

# 64:10
## v64d
Going to Yahweh for protection is spoken of as taking refuge in him. Alternate translation: “go to him for protection” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## pzy4
Here “upright in heart” is an idiom that means godly or righteous. Alternate translation: “all the people who are godly will praise him” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 65:intro
## zl1t

# 65:1
## g299

## qt1y
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## ce6n
This speaks of praise as if it were a person who could act on its own. Alternate translation: “To you alone, God in Zion, we will offer our praise” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## sw4a
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “we will do what we have promised you that we would do” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 65:3
## z8fr
David speaks about iniquity as if it were a person that is able to defeat or oppress. Alternate translation: “It is as if our own sins were defeating us” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## wz7b
The word “them” refers to our “iniquities.”

# 65:4
## s325
The words “you” and “your” in this verse refer to Yahweh.

## r5l8
This exaggeration expresses that the man is in the temple very frequently to worship Yahweh. Alternate translation: “worship often in your courts” (See: [[figs-hyperbole]])

## g4b9
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “The goodness of your house, your holy temple, will satisfy us” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## x47k
Here the word “we” refers to David and the people of Israel, but not to God, to whom he is speaking. (See: [[figs-exclusive]])

## re8y
“your house, which is your holy temple”

# 65:5
## g2mg
“Because you are righteous”

## q2jg
“you are”

## f2m8
These two phrases have similar meanings. Alternate translation: “of all the people who live throughout the earth and across the sea” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## m7rv
This refers to the people who live all over the earth. (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 65:6
## sza2
The writer speaks of God as if he wore his strength like a belt. Alternate translation: “showing that you are very powerful” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 65:7
## q7ky
These two phrases have the same meaning and are used together to create a vivid impression on the hearer or reader. Alternate translation: “the continuous roaring of the seas” (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## r4p4
a loud noise caused by the wind and waves

## uww2
This is also something that God makes quiet.

## dyr9
loud noise

# 65:8
## u5vn
proof or something that shows that another thing is true

## vup2
The phrase “the east and the west” refers to the people who live all over the earth. Alternate translation: “you cause people everywhere to shout joyfully” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-merism]])

# 65:9
## e5cr
This refers to the soil of the earth.

## mt8r
“you make the soil very good so that good things will grow in it”

## rfe2
This refers to the supply of water in the sky that God sends to water the earth and fill the streams. Alternate translation: “you fill the streams with water” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 65:10
## zg5e
The writer is speaking to Yahweh, so these words are all singular. (See: [[figs-you]])

## d2yu
“the earth’s furrows”

## v5qu
A furrow is a long narrow trench made in the ground for planting seeds or for watering the field where grains have been planted.

## l2ln
edges

# 65:11
## r7wm
The words “You” and “your” refer to Yahweh and so are singular. (See: [[figs-you]])

## pc5y
Here the “year” is given the human quality of wearing a crown. Alternate translation: “You have honored the year with a good harvest” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## q39j
Yahweh making the soil so good and fertile that it produces an abundant harvest is spoken of as if Yahweh were traveling through an empty land in a cart, leaving abundant food behind wherever he goes. Alternate translation: “everywhere you have been, you have left abundant food” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 65:12
## f7hf
There is so much dew in the pastures that they are said to drip with it. Alternate translation: “The pastures … are full of dew” or “Much dew drips in the pastures of the wilderness”

## m2ds
The writer speaks of the beauty of the hills as if they were joyful people, and of joy as if it were clothing. Alternate translation: “the hills are like people wearing joy” or “the hills are like joyful people” (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 65:13
## l7rv
The writer speaks of the pastures as being so covered with flocks that it is like the pastures are wearing a garment.

## le4m
a large field where animals feed on the grass

## h9k9
group of animals, such as sheep and goats

## kh7i
The pastures, hills and valleys are so bountiful, that they seem to shout and sing for joy. Alternate translation: “they are like joyful singing people” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## e1qd
The word “they” refers to the pastures and valleys.

## xwm8
See [[PSA-xwm8]]
# 66:1
## wxl5
See [[PSA-wxl5]]
## kzn5
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## cmh2
A “joyful noise to God” represents singing and shouting praises to God. Alternate translation: “Let all the earth sing and shout joyfully to God” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## j76g
This refers to all the people who live on the earth. Alternate translation: “everyone on earth” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 66:2
## si2u
These phrases have similar meanings and are used together to emphasize how wonderful God is. Alternate translation: “Sing about how wonderful God’s name is; sing wonderful praise about how great God is” (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## n3za
God’s name here represents God himself. Alternate translation: “his glory” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 66:3
## sr8b
The works of God cause us to be in awe and terrified because we know he is powerful and holy.

## id4t
“Because you have great power”

# 66:4
## p1ln
This refers to all of the people who live on the earth. Alternate translation: “All the people on earth will worship you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## y7hi
Here “your name” refers to God himself. Alternate translation: “they will praise and honor you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 66:5
## vn26
These words refer to God.

## y91w

## ebc3

# 66:6
## t4bb
These words refer to God.

## ipc9
This refers to the crossing of the Red Sea. (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## dbi6
The word “they” refers to God’s people, the Israelites.

## c4mh
The word “we” refers to the Israelites, their ancestors, David, and the people he is speaking to. (See: [[figs-exclusive]])

# 66:7
## fhu2
These words refer to God.

## v55x
These phrase “his eyes” refers to God himself. Alternate translation: “he sees” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## csw4
“let not the rebellious people exalt themselves” or “let not the rebellious people be proud”

# 66:8
## p33g
These two clauses have similar meanings. The idea is repeated to emphasize the importance of praising God. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

# 66:9
## nub8
These words refer to David and the people he is speaking to. (See: [[figs-exclusive]])

## qfj9
The writer speaks of God’s protection as preventing his people from slipping as they walk or falling off a cliff. Alternate translation: “he has not allowed us to fall into disaster” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 66:11
## eq4q
The writer speaks of God’s punishment as if God had captured his people in a net. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## wp2k
a trap for a bird or an animal

## ib6n
The writer speaks of what the people have endured as having to carry heavy loads on their backs. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 66:12
## el5w
This is a picture of being horribly defeated in battle. Alternate translation: “It is as if our enemies defeated us in battle and then drove their chariots over our fallen bodies” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ua43
God tested them with natural disasters like fires and floods. Alternate translation: “we suffered like people who suffer from fires and floods” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-merism]])

## t7hr
The writer speaks of the blessings that the people of Israel now have as if they had been brought into a wide open space where they are safe. Alternate translation: “open place where we are safe” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 66:14
## t3nu
Here “lips” and “mouth” refer to the words of promise that were spoken. Alternate translation: “which I promised” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 66:15
## fl6u
“smell of the smoke of sacrificed rams”

# 66:16
## kd6i
The word “soul” represents the whole person. Alternate translation: “I will tell you what he has done for me” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 66:17
## utu4
The word “mouth” represents the whole person who cries out to God. (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## s7eh
Here “tongue” represents words or speech. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “I praised him with my tongue” or “I praised him” (See: [[figs-activepassive]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

# 66:18
## f2m2
“loved sin” or “held iniquity”

## kk8n
Here “would not have listened” implies that God would not have answered his prayer. This can be made clear in the translation. Alternate translation: “would not have heard me call out to him” or “he would not have answered my prayer” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 66:19
## n9pa
These two clauses have similar meanings and are used together to emphasize that God has heard his prayer. Alternate translation: “But God has truly heard my prayer” (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## itl3
Here the author’s prayer is given the personal quality of having a voice. Alternate translation: “my prayer” (See: [[figs-personification]])

# 66:20
## sj37
Here “turned away’ represents ignoring his prayer. Alternate translation: “who has not ignored my prayer”

## p1vb
The phrase “has not turned away” is understood from the previous phrase and can be repeated here. The idea of “his covenant faithfulness” can be translated with the phrase “being faithful to his covenant.” Alternate translation: “and has not turned away his covenant faithfulness from me” or “and has not stopped being faithful to his covenant with me” (See: [[figs-explicit]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “people may know your ways on earth” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## ahn5

This means that people everywhere should honor God because of his blessings. Alternate translation: “I desire that all people everywhere on the earth may have an awesome respect for him” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 68:intro
## i82v
See [[PSA-i82v]]
# 68:1
## c4xg
See [[PSA-c4xg]]
## mf9s
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## e798
Possible meanings are (1) David wrote the psalm or (2) the psalm is about David or (3) the psalm is in the style of David’s psalms.

## ebe6
God beginning to act is spoke of as if he stands up. Alternate translation: “Let God begin to act” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## e3kc
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “let God chase away his enemies” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 68:2
## ea3v
God’s enemies are spoken of as if they are smoke that is easily blown away by the wind. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “Drive them away as the wind blows away smoke” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

## s3mi
God’s enemies are spoken of as if they are wax that is easily melted by a fire. Alternate translation: “cause them to disappear as wax melts before a fire” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ea8r
This refers to the wicked people in general. (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

# 68:3
## s74b
This refers to the righteous people in general. (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## e8rg
These means the same thing and emphasizes the amount of joy they feel. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 68:4
## u8td
This refers to God. Alternate translation: “to him” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## mtd6
God’s presence among people is spoken of as if he rides on the earth in a horse or chariot. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 68:5
## nn11
God is spoken of as a compassionate God who acts like a father to orphans. Alternate translation: “One who acts like a father to children who have no parents” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## jev5
God is spoken of as a merciful God who protects widows. Alternate translation: “a protector of widows” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 68:6
## ae7w
God is spoken of as if he places lonely people into families. “God provides families for those who have no one to live with” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## pki3
God is spoken of as the one who leads prisoners out of their confinement. Alternate translation: “God frees prisoners and makes them sing with happiness” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ri2g
This nominal adjective refers to rebellious people and can be translated with either an adjective or a noun. Alternate translation: “rebellious people” or “people who rebel against him” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## xq7k
God’s punishment of the rebellious is spoken of as if he forces them to live in a hot desert land. Alternate translation: “a very hot and dry land” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 68:7
## txl9
See [[PSA-txl9]]
## nqa1
These two phrases refer to the same event. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## vqt5
“you led your people”

## ba2j
God is spoken of as if he was a soldier marching ahead of the people of Israel. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 68:8
## t35q
“God caused it to rain”

## br66
This idiom here refers to God’s appearance before the Israelites. Alternate translation: “when God appeared to the Israelites” (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

# 68:9
## p896
The land of Israel is spoken of as if it was a person who could be weary, or could gain strength. Alternate translation: “you caused the land to produce good crops” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## h87l
The land that God gave to the Israelites is spoken of as if it was an inheritance that a father passed on to his children. Alternate translation: “the land that you gave to us Israelites” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 68:10
## k4fw
This refers to poor people in general. Alternate translation: “poor people” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

# 68:11
## uv8e
See [[PSA-uv8e]]
## t91n
The large number of people told the Lord’s message to others. They are spoken of as if there were a large army. Since this phrase is feminine, some versions translate it as, “the women who announced them … army.” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 68:12
## bm73
The kings represent themselves and their entire armies. It is understood that they flee because they are defeated by Israel’s army. Alternate translation: “Kings and their armies flee from us because they are defeated” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-explicit]])

## gj9s
things that are taken from the defeated army and brought to the victorious army’s home.

# 68:13
## u9e3
This means that some of the plunder is very valuable because it is covered with precious metals.

## m4ps
This question is used to rebuke the people who did not participate in the battle. Alternate translation: “Those who stayed among the sheepfolds should not have stayed; they should have gone to the battle.” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

# 68:14
## zi84
There were so many dead kings and soldiers on the mountain that they are spoken of as if they were snow covering the mountain. Alternate translation: “defeated so many enemy kings and soldiers there that they were like snowflakes covering Mount Zalmon” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## qik2
Here “kings” refers to their armies as well. Alternate translation: “scattered the enemy kings and their armies” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## d4j9
This is the name of a mountain. (See: [[translate-names]])

# 68:15
## j4i6
These two phrase have similar meanings and are used together to strengthen each other. Alternate translation: “a mighty and high mountain is the hill country of Bashan” (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

# 68:16
## g53a
This question can be written as a statement. Alternate translation: “The high hill country of Bashan should not look in envy at the mountain which God desires for the place he will live.” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

# 68:17
## gr2n
This is probably not meant to be an exact number, but to indicate a large number. Alternate translation: “many thousands” (See: [[translate-numbers]])

# 68:18
## z2qx
To “ascend” is to move up, to go toward the sky.

# 68:19
## g3s6
“carries our heavy loads every day.” The Lord’s care for his people is spoken of as if he was physically carrying their troubles as a burden. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## t8d1
The words “is our salvation” can be translated with the verb “save.” Alternate translation: “the God who saves us” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 68:21
## w9jd
God is spoken of as a warrior who will kill his enemies by striking them in their heads in order to kill them. Alternate translation: “will kill his enemies by striking them in the head” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-explicit]])

## kk8w
It seems to have been the custom for soldiers not to cut their hair during the time of war. Alternate translation: “the long-haired skulls” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## u633
Offending God is spoken of as walking among the offenses. Alternate translation: “habitually offend him” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 68:22
## f82v
The word “them” refers to God’s enemies.

## t4dp
This speaks of the most remote parts of the earth where people might try to escape from God as if they were the depths of the sea. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 68:23
## qyf9
The total destruction of Israel’s enemies is spoken of as if the Israelites had crushed them under their feet. Alternate translation: “totally defeat your enemies” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## c62p
The violence of from the destruction of the enemies is spoke of in very graphic form, as if the Israelites would be standing in the blood of their dead enemies. Alternate translation: “stepping in their blood” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## g8uz
The bloodshed from the battle against Israel’s enemies is spoken of as if it is so extensive that the dogs will lap up the flowing blood with their tongues. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 68:24
## k3xf
A procession is a group of people walking together in an orderly manner as part of a ceremony.

# 68:25
## kyt4
people who play musical instruments

# 68:26
## qq11
It may be helpful to change the order of these phrases. Alternate translation: “You who are from the fountain of Israel, praise Yahweh and bless God in the assembly”

## smi2
The word “fountain” is a metaphor for the ability of the man Israel to be the ancestor of many people: as much water comes from a fountain, so Israel is the ancestor of many people. This also implies that the call is to those who serve God as the man Israel did. Alternate translation: “true descendants of Israel” or “all of you descendants from Israel”(See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-explicit]])

# 68:27
## nt5p
“their group.” The word “their” refers to the leaders of Judah.

# 68:28
## f4wh
Some versions understand the Hebrew text differently: “Summon your strength, God” or “Use your strength, God”

## f4rw
“People of Israel, your God has decreed”

## wau7
The word “us” refers to the writer and the people of Israel, but not to Yahweh, to whom he is speaking. (See: [[figs-exclusive]])

# 68:29
## zq5a
The word “us” refers to the writer and the people of Israel, but not to Yahweh, to whom he is speaking. (See: [[figs-exclusive]])

## isi1
“When you are present in the temple at Jerusalem, show us your power”

## fem7
The abstract noun “power” can be stated as “strong.” Alternate translation: “Show us that you are strong” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 68:30
## c8e8
Many scholars believe these wild beasts are a metaphor that refers to the people of Egypt. This can be made explicit. Alternate translation: “the people of Egypt who are like wild beasts in the reeds” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-explicit]])

## g1z9
The peoples of other nations are spoken of as if they were a large group of cattle. Alternate translation: “the powerful nations, who are like herds of bulls” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## c6zu
to disperse or to cause something to spread quickly in different direction

# 68:31
## n487
It is implied that these princes come from Egypt in order to offer gifts to God in Jerusalem. Alternate translation: “Then the leaders of Egypt will bring gifts to you” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## c5dx
This refers to the people of Cush. Alternate translation: “The Cushites” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## i46u
This is a symbolic action that represents worship to God. Alternate translation: “lift up her hands to praise God” (See: [[translate-symaction]])

# 68:32
## gn8g
Here “kingdoms” refers to the citizens of the kingdoms. Alternate translation: “you people who are citizens of kingdoms all over the world” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 68:33
## x1i6
The word “Sing” is implied as the beginning of this verse. Here God is described as if he rides in a chariot in the sky. Alternate translation: “Sing to God who rides across the sky in his chariot” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## npf5
This idiom means he speaks powerfully. Alternate translation: “he shouts powerfully” or “he speaks loudly” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 68:34
## a3cn
“Ascribe” means to give credit to someone. Alternate translation: “Strength belongs to God”

## ul58
The abstract noun “strength” can be stated as “powerful.” Alternate translation: “in the skies he also shows that he is powerful” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 68:35
## m2ya
Here the author speaks directly to God. (See: [[figs-apostrophe]])

## sy6i
These two words mean basically these same thing. They emphasize how much strength God provides to his people. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 69:intro
## im3w
See [[PSA-im3w]]
# 69:1
## emd2
See [[PSA-emd2]]
## x1w1
“This is for the director of music to use in worship”

## jj9x
This may refer to a style of music. See how you translated this in [Psalms 45:1](../045/001.md).

## b6zx
The writer describes the troubles in his life as if he were drowning in a flood of water. Alternate translation: “for it feels like I am drowning in the waters” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 69:2
## tpg9
The writer describes the troubles in his life as if he were sinking in deep mud. Alternate translation: “For it feels like I am sinking in deep mud and will die” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ry13
thick mud

## u4k9
The writer uses a negative statement to stress how unstable and uncertain his condition is. (See: [[figs-litotes]])

## bt2v
The writer describes his problems as if he was drowning in a deep, raging river. Alternate translation: “t feels like I am in deep waters, and the floodwaters flow over me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 69:3
## qdk1
very tired

## d5w4
This idiom means the writer has cried so much that his eyes do not see well any longer. Alternate translation: “my eyes are swollen from tears” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 69:4
## ks2e
This is an exaggeration to express how many enemies the writer has. Alternate translation: “more than I can count, like the hairs on my head” (See: [[figs-hyperbole]])

## v3ns
This idiom means “kill me.” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 69:5
## z5mb
The abstract noun “foolishness” can be stated as “foolish.” Alternate translation: “the foolish things that I have done” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## c1z9
This can be expressed as a positive statement. Alternate translation: “you know all my sins” (See: [[figs-litotes]])

# 69:6
## l21p
“Do not let those … do not let those”

## d5j2
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “Please do not allow anyone to put those who wait for you to shame because of me” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## ana6
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “Please do not allow anyone to bring dishonor on those who seek you because of me” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## djs5
Seeking God represents either (1) asking God for help or (2) thinking about God and obeying him. Alternate translation: (1) “those who ask you for help” or (2) “those who worship and obey you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 69:7
## se7t
“On your behalf” or “For you”

## td6l
The rebukes of the writer’s enemies are spoken of as if they are a heavy load that he has had to carry. Alternate translation: “I have endured the insults of my enemies” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## l47r
The writer speaks of the shame that he feels as if it is a foul thing on his face that everyone can clearly see. Alternate translation: “I am thoroughly humiliated” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 69:8
## f38a
The writer speaks of himself as if he were not part of his own family. Alternate translation: “My brothers no longer know or accept me at all” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## au3m
These two phrases mean the same thing. They are repeated to stress his separation from his own family. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## w5cm
It is implied that “I have become” should be understood here. The writer speaks of himself as if he were not part of his own family. Alternate translation: “my brothers no longer know or trust me at all” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 69:9
## dwj8
The writer speaks of his zeal for God’s temple as if it was a wild animal that devours the writer. Alternate translation: “the zeal I have for your house consumes me” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## d4m8
This idiom means that the writer’s zeal for the temple takes over all of his thoughts and actions. Alternate translation: “completely controls all that I think and do” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## ckq9
The writer speaks of the rebukes of Gods’ enemies as if they were rocks that were thrown at the writer. Alternate translation: “those who rebuke you have also thrown their rebukes at me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 69:10
## y39q
The fact that the writer was fasting indicates that he was sad about the way people treated God’s temple. (See: [[translate-symaction]] and [[figs-explicit]])

## dn9i
“my enemies rebuked me because of it”

# 69:11
## la4h
Wearing rough, cheap clothing was a symbol of mourning over sin. (See: [[translate-symaction]])

## q7ys
The writer speak of himself as if he was the sad or foolish person in a proverb. Alternate translation: “I became the example of a sad person spoken of in their proverbs” or “they laugh at me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 69:12
## m9ar
Here “city gate” is associated with leadership of a town. Alternate translation: “The important people of the city” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## u3uq
The writer speaks of himself as if he was the person about whom the drunkards sing mocking songs. Alternate translation: “the drunkards of the city sing disgusting songs about me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 69:13
## t3wv
“in your accepted time” or “when you are willing”

## ye88
The abstract nouns “trustworthiness” and “salvation” can be stated as “faithfully” and “rescue.” Alternate translation: “rescue me because you faithfully love me, as you have promised to do” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 69:14
## glu5
These two phrases mean the same thing. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## ce9q
The writer speaks of his danger from his enemies as if he was sinking into a pit of mud. “Do not allow me to sink anymore in the mud” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## q3rm
Here “take away” refers to being removed from danger. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “take me away” or “rescue me” (See: [[figs-idiom]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

## zv92
It is understood that “let me be” is implied here. It can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “please rescue me out” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

## llk8
The writer speaks about his danger from his enemies as if he was drowning in deep water. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 69:15
## ks55
The writer speaks about his danger from his enemies as if flood waters were covering him completely. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## d558
The writer speaks of the deep as if it was a deadly animal that was about to eat him. Alternate translation: “the deep waters swallow me up like a dangerous animal” (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## iz9u
Here the “pit” is spoken of as if it has a mouth like a person and could eat the writer. Alternate translation: “Do not let the pit consume me” or “Do not let the pit of death close over me” (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 69:16
## ywk4
The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “you are good and faithful to your covenant” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## ir4z
“you are very merciful to me”

## w23e
The idea of turning towards someone means to pay attention to them or help them. Alternate translation: “help me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 69:17
## l6nz
To hide one’s face means to refuse to hear or help someone. Alternate translation: “Please help your servant” or “Please help me” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## fq4r
“in great trouble”

# 69:18
## a5r7
The writer asks God to redeem him as if the writer were a slave whose freedom God could purchase. Alternate translation: “free me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## emr2
The writer asks God to ransom him as if the writer were a captive whose release could be paid for with money. Alternate translation: “rescue me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 69:19
## jv1e
These abstract nouns can be stated as actions. Alternate translation: “how people have rebuked me, shamed me, and dishonored me” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## cbu1
Here “before you” means that God sees and knows all about them. Alternate translation: “you know who all my enemies are” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 69:20
## d7kg
This idiom means a person is extremely sad. Alternate translation: “offended me deeply” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## dm8h
The writer’s great sadness is spoken of as if he was full of a heavy weight. Alternate translation: “I am heavy with sorrow” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## zw1r
to feel sorrow or sadness

# 69:21
## lfl7
This is probably figurative. The food that people gave to the writer was so bad that it tasted like poison. Alternate translation: “They gave me food that tasted like poison” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 69:22
## bt4m
The writer would like for his enemies’ food to completely ruin them as if they were small animals caught in a snare or a trap. Alternate translation: “May their food ruin them like a snare … may it destroy them like a trap” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## fd3h
This refers to food that was served on the tables, possibly at a feast. Alternate translation: “their own food” or “sacrificial feasts” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 69:23
## v67i
The writer speaks of eyes that cannot see well as if they were darkened. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “Please make them unable to see anything” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

## d56n
Weak backs are spoken of as if they are shaking in weakness. Alternate translation: “cause their backs to be too weak for them to do anything” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## rry1
“their sides” or “their backs”

# 69:24
## x9dl
God’s demonstration of his anger is described as if he poured it out on his enemies like water. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## j3n9
anger of a person who has suffered injustice

## a5mh
“your burning anger” or “your strong anger”

## mws1
God’s judgment on his enemies is described as if he ran after them and caught them. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 69:25
## hl9y
This abstract noun can be stated as “abandoned.” Alternate translation: “become abandoned” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 69:26
## u691
“they persecuted the man”

## q569
Here to be “struck down” refers to punishment. Alternate translation: “you punished” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## x39c
Here to be “wounded” refers to causing them to suffer. Alternate translation: “those you have caused to suffer” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 69:27
## ha19
“Keep making a record of all their sins”

## ix9p
“very many sins”

## fv3w
To come into God’s victory is an idiom that means to receive a reward from him. Alternate translation: “do not let them receive your righteous reward” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 69:28
## qt7j
Here “them” refers to the names of the enemies. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “Wipe out their names in” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

## el1y
It is inferred that “let them” is understood. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “do not write down their names” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

# 69:29
## k8wx
The abstract noun “salvation” can be stated with the verb “save.” Here “on high” refers to a place of safety.” Alternate translation: “God, save me and put me in a safe place” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

# 69:30
## m7bv
Here “name” refers to God himself. Alternate translation: “God” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## bl7i
This abstract noun can be stated with the verb “thank.” Alternate translation: “by thanking him” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 69:31
## q988
It is understood that the ox and the bull are to be offered to God as sacrifices. Alternate translation: “better than sacrificing an ox or sacrificing a bull” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## axd8
This phrase distinguishes the full grown bulls from other younger cows. Alternate translation: “a bull that is full grown with horns and hooves” (See: [[figs-distinguish]])

# 69:32
## b8xa
This refers to meek people in general. Alternate translation: “Meek people” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## ky6t
Seeking God represents either (1) asking God for help or (2) thinking about God and obeying him. Alternate translation: “you who ask God for help” or “you who think about God” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## i99y
Here “hearts” refer to the people. Here “live” is an idiom that means to be encouraged. Alternate translation: “may you be encouraged” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-hypo]])

# 69:33
## arn6
Here “hears” means to respond. Alternate translation: “Yahweh answers” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## ij3h
This refers to needy people in general. Alternate translation: “needy people” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## eag2
“those who have suffered for him”

# 69:34
## k14w
Here heaven and earth and the seas are spoken of as if they are people who are able to praise God. (See: [[figs-personification]])

## p3qb
It is implied that “Let … praise him” should be understood here. Alternate translation: “let he seas and everything that moves in them praise him” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

# 69:35
## m398
Here “Zion” refers to the people in Zion. Alternate translation: “God will save the people of Zion” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## w8jf
The word “it” refers to the land of Judah.

# 69:36
## s9pk
Here “name” refers to God himself. Alternate translation: “who love God” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## g5lq
To be stopped or thwarted is spoken of as being turned back from their attack. Alternate translation: “stopped” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 70:3
## b66b
This is an expression of mocking laughter. You may replace “Aha, aha” with whatever laughing sounds like in your language. Alternate translation: “those who mock and laugh at me”

# 70:4
## hi48
Seeking God represents either (1) asking God for help or (2) thinking about God and obeying him. Alternate translation: “ask you for help” or “think about you and obey you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## fiv4
These two phrases mean basically the same thing and emphasize the intensity of gladness. Alternate translation: “rejoice greatly” or “be very glad” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## k76h
The abstract noun “salvation” can be stated as an action. Alternate translation: “love you because you saved them” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## ymr2

# 70:5
## k146
Here the words “poor” and “needy” mean basically the same thing and emphasize that he is unable to help himself. Alternate translation: “very needy” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## s6qa
The writer speaks of God as if he were running to the writer in order to help him. Alternate translation: “come quickly to help me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## r77i
Here the phrase “you rescue me” explains how God is his “help.” Alternate translation: “you help me by rescuing me” (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## ww8h
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “please come quickly” (See: [[figs-litotes]])

# 71:intro
## r8sf
