# 119:6
## v2e6
The writer does not want to be ashamed when he is in God’s presence.

## ecl7
“all that you have commanded us”

# 119:7
## hd5j
“a sincere heart.” A person who is sincere will do what is right. The heart refers to the center of emotions in a person. See how you translated “uprightness” in [Psalms 25:21](../025/021.md). (See: [[figs-idiom]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

# 119:8
## v49a
“Statutes” refers to God’s laws or commands.

# 119:9
## lp29
This question is used to introduce a new value to the word of God. This rhetorical question can be translated as a statement. Alternate translation: “This is how a young person can keep his path pure” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## gm1y
The writer compares living according to God’s law as a path kept clear of obstructions. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:10
## h5t8
This is an idiom. The heart refers to all of one’s emotions, feelings, desires, and will. Alternate translation: “with all my being” or “with everything in me” or “sincerely” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## kqg2
Here to disobey God’s commandments is described as straying off a path. Alternate translation: “Do not let me disobey your commandments” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:11
## f3ke
“I have put your words in my heart.” This is a metaphor that means “I have memorized your word.” The heart is pictured as a container that can hold what people think. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:14
## ktv7
“more than all the wealth”

# 119:15
## e5hd
These are parallel thoughts that have similar meanings, which are repeated for emphasis. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## v9ru
“think carefully about what you have instructed us”

## rb5a
This idiom refers to thinking clearly about what is being discussed. Alternate translation: “give careful thought” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 119:16
## il7r
to take pleasure

# 119:17
## fr7n
The writer called himself “your servant” to show his humility.

# 119:18
## jpj2
The author speaks of gaining understanding, knowledge and wisdom as being able to see. Alternate translation: Help me to understand” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## d25d
The author speaks of insight into the law as objects to marvel at. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## a35a
“in your instructions” or “in your commands”

# 119:19
## att5
Possible meanings are (1) the writers speaks of his short life on earth as if he were a foreigner who would not stay long in the land. Alternate translation: “I am like a foreigner living a short time in the land” or (2) the writer’s ignorance of God’s law as if he were a foreigner who did not know the laws of the land. Alternate translation: “I am ignorant like a foreigner in the land” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:20
## y84c
The writer speaks of his desires being very strong as if they were in pain. Alternate translation: “My inner being strongly desires to know” or “My soul aches because I want so much to know” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:21
## r8y6
Possible meanings are that (1) God will curse them or (2) they deserve God’s punishment. Alternate translation: “who deserve your punishment”

## k8t4
The writer speaks of disobeying God’s commandments as if they were a path that can be wandered off from. Alternate translation: “who go away from the path of your commandments” or “who disobey your commandments” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:22
## nqp7
“Keep me from” or “Rescue me from”

# 119:23
## z9ci
“Though rulers make plans to harm me and say bad things about me”

# 119:24
## pb1g
“Your covenant decrees make me very happy.”

## rta6
God’s decrees are spoken of as if they were people. Alternate translation: “they are like wise counselors to me” or “they give me wise counsel” (See: [[figs-personification]])

# 119:25
## v3c7
This is an idiom. Possible meanings are that (1) he thought that he would die soon, or (2) he lay in the dust because he was very sad, or (3) he realized that he desired the worthless things of the earth. (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## cn62
This is an idiom. Here “life” refers to purpose and significance, not just biological life. (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## ks95
“according to your promise”

# 119:26
## u8j6
What a person does or how he behaves is spoken of as if it were a road or way. Alternate translation: “what I have done” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:27
## x7qh
“amazing teachings”

# 119:28
## n45q
“because I am so sad”

## n4h6
“Make me strong.” This may refer to physical strength or spiritual strength.

# 119:29
## n1pn
The word “path” here refers to a way of behaving. Alternate translation: “Keep me from following the path of deceit” or “Prevent me from being deceptive” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## p23d
Possible meanings are (1) “lying” or (2) “believing lies” or “following lies.”

# 119:30
## u8gw
How a person behaves or acts is spoken as if it were a road or way. Alternate translation: “to be faithful to you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:31
## hf1b
Holding tightly to them refers to being committed to obeying them. Alternate translation: “I hold tightly to your covenant decrees” or “I am committed to obeying your covenant decrees” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## zc7g
This refers to the law of Moses.

# 119:32
## zq4i
The writer speaks of being focused or committed to obeying God’s commands as if one is running on a path. Alternate translation: “I will be committed to obey your commands” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## fzh3
This is an idiom. Possible meanings are (1) “you help me gain greater understanding of your commands” or (2) “you give me greater desire to obey your commands” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 119:33
## eg16
This is another way of describing the law of Moses.

## j4dt
Possible meanings are (1) “completely” or (2) “to the end of my life” or (3) “to the end of time.”

## uwv4
“obey your law”

# 119:35
## bh21
“Guide me according to your commandments” or “Teach me to obey your commandments.” God’s commandments are compared to a path that a person walks in obedience to God. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:36
## uc28
This is an idiom. The “heart” here refers to the will, desires, and choices that directs one’s life. Alternate translation: “Make me want” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## vct5
“to obey your covenant decrees.” This is referring to obeying the law of Moses.

## ah76
“the desire for riches.” This is referring to wealth gained by illegal methods or wrongdoing towards others.

# 119:37
## t9za
This is a metaphor that refers to one desiring things that have no eternal value. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## vdd9

## xeu1
“make my life strong” or “give me strength”

## yk2j

## yau8

## mk9g
God judges rightly and his decisions are good. Alternate translation: “Your judgments are righteous and good” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 119:40
## yl75
This refers to being aware of the situation. The focus is on knowledge or understanding, rather than just observing.

## d8v4
Possible meanings are (1) “I want very much to know your instructions” or (2) “I want very much to obey what you teach us to do.”

The word “righteousness” is an abstract noun and refers to being righteous. Alternate translation: “revive me because you are righteous” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## ci53
Possible meanings are (1) “Keep me alive” or (2) “Make me strong.”

## fa7w

## vms5
“an answer” or “a response”

# 119:43
## j9dg
Here the writer is represented by his “mouth.” Possible meanings are (1) “never prevent me from speaking the message about the truth” or (2) “never prevent me from speaking the true message.”

# 119:44
## mp4n
“I will obey”

# 119:45
## lq9x
To walk securely is to live one’s life securely. Alternate translation: “I will live securely in God” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-explicit]])

## h23e
To “seek” is to perceive, or gain understanding of God’s instructions as if one can see them. (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## uj95

## y49b

# 119:48
## v87b
This is an idiom which means to honor, cherish or respect God’s commandments. (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 119:49
## gb3p
“Remember your promise.” See how you translated this in [Psalms 20:3](../020/003.md)

# 119:50
## mlp7
This clause can be restructured. Alternate translation: “The reason for my comfort is that your promise has kept me alive in my affliction” (See: [[figs-sentences]])

# 119:51
## n3rr
This nominal adjective can be stated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “The proud people” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## f89y
to mock someone or something that is looked down on, doubted, or not honored

# 119:52
## nhe2
This is a reference to when the decrees, the Law, were given to Moses many years before. (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 119:53
## x2f1
This is an idiom. Anger is expressed as if it is a person that can grab another person. Alternate translation: “I have become very angry” (See: [[figs-idiom]] and [[figs-personification]])

## t7xf
“I have used your statutes as lyrics to my music” or “I have created songs from your statutes”

## ntb8

# 119:56
## ch5n
“my habit”

## ii8j
This is an idiom which means to follow or to obey those instructions. Alternate translation: “I have obeyed your instructions” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 119:57
## f7jf
This means Yahweh is all he wants. Just as the Levites did not receive vast territories of land for the Lord was to be their portion so the writer claims Yahweh as the satisfier of his needs. (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 119:59
## x88a
Here “feet” represent the whole person. To repent and choose to obey God’s laws is like turning one’s feet on a path to head in another direction. Alternate translation: “changed my direction” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:60
## uuk4
The writer expresses the same idea both positively and negatively in order to emphasize the urgency with which he obeys Yahweh’s commands. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 119:61
## i6di
In this metaphor, wicked or evil people tried to cause the writer to sin like a hunter seeking to catch an animal with a trap. Alternate translation: “My enemies have tried to catch me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:63
## tvy5
“I am a friend of all who honor you”

# 119:64
## p7l3
People everywhere in the world being able to see evidence of Yahweh’s covenant faithfulness is spoken of as if his covenant faithfulness filled the earth. The abstract noun “covenant faithfulness” can be translated as an adjective. See how you translated a similar phrase in [Psalms 33:5](../033/005.md). Alternate translation: “People everywhere on earth can see that you, Yahweh, are faithful to your covenant” or “Throughout the earth, there is evidence that you, Yahweh, are faithful to your covenant” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 119:65
## d39z
The writer refers to himself as “your servant.” Alternate translation: “to me, your servant” or “to me” (See: [[figs-123person]])

## k4vq
This is an idiom. “Your word” refers to the promises Yahweh has made to the writer. Alternate translation: “as you have promised” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 119:66
## x5n2
Some languages may require change in logical progression. Alternate translation: “Since I have believed in your commandments, teach me proper discernment and understanding” (See: [[figs-sentences]] and [[writing-intro]])

# 119:67
## ln6x
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “Before you afflicted me” or “Before you punished me” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## t586
Disobeying God is spoken of as if the person walked on the wrong path. Alternate translation: “I disobeyed you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## qc4x
Here “word” represents commandments. Alternate translation: “I obey your commandments” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 119:69
## f9re
This nominal adjective can be stated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “Arrogant people” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## g5zy
People telling many lies about a person is spoken of as if they made the person dirty by spreading lies over him. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ljt8
Here “heart” represents a person’s will. Alternate translation: “with complete commitment” or “completely” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 119:70
## kwi4
Here “hearts” represents the people’s wills. A person being stubborn is spoken of as if their hearts or wills were hard like a rock. Alternate translation: “They are stubborn” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:72
## ll7t
Here “mouth” represents what God says. Alternate translation: “The instructions you have spoken are” or “Your instructions are” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

This can be stated more generally. Alternate translation: “than a large amount of money” or “than great wealth”

## hf5d
God creating a person is spoken of as if God used his hands to shape the person the way someone may shape clay into an object. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## wc9b
Here “hands” represents God’s power or action. Alternate translation: “You” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 119:74
## u7a8
“because I trust what you say” or “I confidently believe what you say”

# 119:75
## zx24
God promises to reward the righteous and punish wrongdoers, so he is faithful to do what he says he will. The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated with an adjective. Alternate translation: “you punished me because you are faithful” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## zzf3

## i7zp
People returning in friendship to the writer is spoken of as if they physically turn towards him. Alternate translation: “come to me” or “unite with me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:83
## pgx9
A wineskin is ruined when it hangs for a long time in a smoke-filled place. The writer compares himself to a wineskin that has been ruined by smoke to emphasize that he feels useless. (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 119:84
## dl2z
The writer uses a question to request God to punish those who persecute him. This rhetorical question can be translated as a statement. Alternate translation: “Please do not make wait any longer. Punish those who persecute me.” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## jt81
The writer refers to himself as “your servant.” Alternate translation: “must I, your servant” or “must I” (See: [[figs-123person]])

# 119:85
## j1jf
The proud are seeking to capture the writer or cause him to do wrong. This is spoken of as if they were hunters digging holes to trap the writer like an animal. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## spv2
This nominal adjective can be stated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “Proud people” or “Those who are proud” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

# 119:87
## pds6
This is a polite way of speaking about someone killing someone else. Alternate translation: “They have almost killed me” (See: [[figs-euphemism]])

# 119:88
## x4ml
“According to your steadfast love.” The phrase “steadfast love” or “faithfulness” can be stated as an adverb. Alternate translation: “because you faithfully love me” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 119:126
## g82b
The writer is speaking to Yahweh in the third person. This can be stated in second person. Alternate translation: “It is time for you to act, Yahweh” (See: [[figs-123person]])

## n98z
This is an idiom. Here “have broken” means “disobeyed.” This is a way of saying the people have disobeyed God’s law. (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 119:128
## z4ux
A person carefully obeying all of God’s instructions is spoken of as if as if the instructions were leading a person and that person follows behind. Alternate translation: I carefully obey all of your instructions” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## p1py
People doing what is evil is spoken of as if they are walking on the wrong path. Alternate translation: “all the bad ways some people live” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:130
## m49k
The writer speaks of Yahweh’s words as if those words were fabric that is folded, and of the person who explains Yahweh’s words as if they are unfolding that fabric. Alternate translation: “The explanation of your words gives light” or “When someone explains your words, they give light” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## d6rx
The writer speaks of Yahweh’s words giving wisdom to a person as if his words were shining a light on them. Alternate translation: “The explanation of your words gives people wisdom” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:131
## qm6c
The writer speaks of his desire for Yahweh’s commandments as if he were a dog panting for water. Alternate translation: “I earnestly long for your commandments” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:132
## jqh6
To turn towards someone means to pay attention to that person. Alternate translation: “Pay attention to me” (See: [[translate-symaction]])

## ar7k
Here the word “name” represents Yahweh himself. Alternate translation: “love you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 119:133
## mja8
Here the word “footsteps” represents the writer as he is walking. He speaks of the way he lives, or his conduct, as if he were walking on a path. Alternate translation: “Direct me” or “Teach me how to live” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## y2w5
The writer speaks of sin as if it were a person who has authority over him. Possible meanings are (1) “do not let me habitually commit any sin” or (2) “do not let sinful men rule me” (See: [[figs-personification]])

# 119:134
## a4a4
The word “oppression” can be translated as a verb. Alternate translation: “Save me from people who oppress others” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 119:135
## g736
The writer speaks of Yahweh acting favorably towards him as if Yahweh’s face shone a light on him. Alternate translation: “Act favorably towards your servant” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:136
## jv4q
The writer speaks of his many tears as if they were streams of water. Alternate translation: “Many tears” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## sst5
“obey your law”

## hus8
Other possible meanings are “testimonies” or “laws.” See how you translated this in [Psalms 78:5](../078/005.md).

# 119:139
## z79n
This is an idiom. The phrase is an exaggeration for “I am extremely angry.” (See: [[figs-idiom]] and [[figs-hyperbole]])

# 119:140
## r9cv
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “I have tested your word many times” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## q5x5
The writer speaks of himself as if he were another person. Alternate translation: “I, your servant, love” or “I love” (See: [[figs-pronouns]])

# 119:141
## x2xe
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “People despise me” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 119:143
## q6qq
The psalmist speaks of distress and anguish as if they were people. Alternate translation: “I have become distressed and anguished” or “my body and my mind are suffering” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## fux2

# 119:148
## c1n8
This is an idiom. In Hebrew culture, the night was usually divided into three “watches” or periods. Alternate translation: “I am awake all night” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 119:149
## uw93

# 119:153
## i4e7
The psalmist speaks of affliction as if it were an object that people could see. Alternate translation: “Look at how much I am suffering” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## l7lr

# 119:155
## cc3z
God not saving a person is spoken of as if salvation were far from the person. The abstract noun “Salvation” can be stated as “save.” Alternate translation: “You will certainly not save the wicked” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## r4u3

# 119:161
## tq5i
The psalmist speaks of the heart as if it could be amazed. The heart is a synecdoche for the whole person. Alternate translation: “I am amazed at your word” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-personification]])

# 119:162
## n1dy
Possible meanings are (1) things that soldiers and robbers take from those they have defeated in battle or (2) things of great value or “treasure.”

# 119:170
## r59u
The psalmist speaks of the words he says in prayer as if they were people who want to speak to a king. Alternate translation: “May you hear my prayer” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:171
## x454
The psalmist speaks of his lips as if they were a container and his praise a liquid that could be poured out. Here the word “lips” is a synecdoche which represents the whole person. Alternate translation: “I desire to praise you much” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 119:172
## hk6w
The psalmist speaks of his tongue either (1) as if it were a person or (2) as a synecdoche for his whole being. Alternate translation: “me sing” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 119:173
## ui9f
The hand is a synecdoche for the whole person. Alternate translation: “Please help me” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 119:175
## z1ep
The psalmist speaks of Yahweh’s decrees as if they were a person who could help him. Alternate translation: “may I listen to your righteous decrees and so become wise and strong” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 119:176

# 120:2
## a439
Here the word “life” represents the person. Alternate translation: “Rescue me” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## yy4j
Here the phrases “their lips” and “their tongues” represent the people who speak lies and deceit. Alternate translation: “those who lie to me and try to deceive me” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 120:3
## rl7j
The writer asks this as a leading question to explain what God will do to liars. This question can be translated as a statement. Alternate translation: “This is how God will punish you, and this is what he will do to you, you who have a lying tongue.” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## k1uu
Here “a lying tongue” represents the person who speaks lies. Alternate translation: “you who tell lies” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 120:4
## tp2n
The writer speaks of God severely punishing liars as if God were shooting them with arrows. Alternate translation: “He will punish you severely, as if he were shooting you with warrior’s arrows” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## gu1s
This refers to how people forged the tip of the arrow in a fire. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “that he sharpened over burning coals of the broom tree” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 120:5
## mg3z
These two places were far away from each other. The writer is likely using the names metaphorically to represent living among cruel and barbaric people. Alternate translation: “It is as if I live in Meshech or among the tents of Kedar” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## qx4h
This phrase represents the people of Kedar who live in those tents. Alternate translation: “the people who live in Kedar” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 121:6
## p2y6
The contrasting terms “day” and “night” refer to those extremes and everything in between. Alternate translation: “God protects you from the elements at all times” (See: [[figs-merism]])

## wzt9

# 122:2
## d2gp
The writer briefly stops speaking to his audience and speaks directly to the city of Jerusalem. Jerusalem is spoken to as if it was a person who could hear the writer. (See: [[figs-apostrophe]] and [[figs-personification]])

# 122:6
## q9u2
This section states the content of the prayer that the writer wants his audience to pray. He asks them to speak directly to the city of Jerusalem, as if the city was a person who could hear them. (See: [[figs-apostrophe]] and [[figs-personification]])

# 122:7
## qxx3
This verse finishes the prayer that the writer wants his audience to pray. He asks them to speak directly to the city of Jerusalem, as if the city was a person who could hear them. (See: [[figs-apostrophe]] and [[figs-personification]])

## exb9
These two phrases have the same meanings and are used together to strengthen each other. Alternate translation: “May the people in Jerusalem live in peace” (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## d4tc
Here Jerusalem is referred to by the fortress walls that protects it. The terms “walls” and “fortress” refer to the same thing. Alternate translation: “within Jerusalem” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-parallelism]])

# 124:3
## n3uw
This is the end of a hypothetical statement that begins with the words “If Yahweh had not been on our side” in [Psalms 124:1](../124/001.md) and continues with the words “if it had not been Yahweh who was on our side when men rose up against us” in [Psalms 124:2](./002.md). It describes a result that did not happen because Yahweh was actually on their side. “They were not able to swallow us up alive because Yahweh was on our side.” (See: [[figs-hypo]])

## g8z9
This metaphor describes how the Israelites could have died to how a fierce animal would attack a smaller animal to eat. Alternate translation: “killed us” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## tq3h
Here “their anger” refers to the enemies who were angry. Alternate translation: “they were very angry with us” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## hgr6
This is the end of a hypothetical statement that begins with the words “If Yahweh had not been on our side” in [Psalms 124:1](../124/001.md) and continues with the words “if it had not been Yahweh who was on our side when men rose up against us” in [Psalms 124:2](./002.md). It describes a result that did not happen because Yahweh was actually on their side. “The water did not sweep us away, and the torrent did not overwhelm us because Yahweh was on our side” (See: [[figs-hypo]])

# 124:5
## j6yh
This is the end of a hypothetical statement that begins with the words “If Yahweh had not been on our side” in [Psalms 124:1](../124/001.md) and continues with the words “if it had not been Yahweh who was on our side when men rose up against us” in [Psalms 124:2](./002.md). It describes a result that did not happen because Yahweh was actually on their side. “The raging waters did not drown us because Yahweh was on our side” (See: [[figs-hypo]])

# 124:6
## thg5
The enemies are spoken of as if they were wild animals that would destroy the Israelites by eating them. Alternate translation: “destroyed as if we were eaten by wild animals” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## fr8c

a small trap of string or wire made for catching small animals or birds

## h3wt

## y7ss

# 126:2
## wxr3
Laughing is spoken of as if their mouths were a container and their laughter was in it. It can be made clear that this laughter was a response to their joy. Alternate translation: “we laughed for joy” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-explicit]])

## g1bj
The verbs “were filled” can be stated clearly. Singing is spoken of as if their tongues were containers and singing was in them. Alternate translation: “our tongues were filled with singing” or “we sang songs of joy” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## xir4
“the people of the nations said among themselves.” The pronoun is used before introducing what it references. This is very unusual.

# 127:intro
## ipx7
See [[PSA-ipx7]]
# 127:1
## nt9a
See [[PSA-nt9a]]
## m7vn
Possible meanings are (1) “song people sang while going up to Jerusalem for a celebration” or (2) “song people sang while going up the steps into the temple” or (3) “song whose words are like steps.” See how you translated this in [Psalms 120:1](../120/001.md)

# 127:2
## qvi2
A person who works hard often has to wake up earlier in the morning and return home late at night.

## vc2y
This is an idiom. Bread often represents the food a person needs every day in order to live. Alternate translation: “work hard for your daily needs” (See: [[figs-idiom]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 127:3
## qz98
property that a person can inherit from his ancestors. Children normally receive an inheritance from their parents. Inheritance goes from parents to children. This passage uses parents inheriting children from Yahweh as a metaphor for Yahweh being the only one who can give children. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 127:4
## iyl8
Arrows are very important to a warrior because they protect him in battle. Children are spoken of as if they are a warrior’s arrow. Alternate translation: “Having many children will help to protect you” (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 127:5
## vf7l
A quiver is a container for arrows. Having many children is spoken of as if the children were arrows in a quiver. Alternate translation: “a home full of children” or “many children” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 128:intro
## f8w6
See [[PSA-f8w6]]
# 128:1
## xub9
See [[PSA-xub9]]
## h11n
This phrase occurs in the passive voice to avoid implying that Yahweh is obligated to bless those who honor him. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “Yahweh will bless everyone who honors him” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 128:2
## xw8w
A man can be referred to by his hands because that is the part of the body he works with. Alternate translation: “What you provide” or “What you work for” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## b9im
The words “be blessed” and “prosper” share similar meanings and emphasize God’s favor. Alternate translation: “Yahweh will bless you and prosper you” or “Yahweh will make you blessed and prosperous” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 128:3
## x211
The wife is spoke of as a vine producing a lot of fruit. This implies that children are like fruit and the wife will have many children. Alternate translation: “very productive and give you many children” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## mf2p
Children are compared to olive plants because of the way they grow to surround something. Children will surround the table and make it full. Alternate translation: “you will have many children who will grow and prosper” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## vlk1
This refers to the place where a family gathers to eat. Often, all those who eat a man’s table are under his authority or control.

# 128:4
## v5em
This can be stated as an active verb. “Yahweh will bless the man who honors him” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 128:5
## iz4u
“throughout your lifetime”

# 128:6
## cd66
“May Israel have peace”

# 129:intro
## p9dv
See [[PSA-p9dv]]
# 129:1
## ut36
See [[PSA-ut36]]
# 129:3
## wpl7
The cuts from a whipping are spoken of as the plow of a plowman. A farmer plowed deep lines into a field. Alternate translation: “My enemies have cut me deeply on my back” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## nq4f
This is a continuation of the plowing metaphor. The “furrow” is the line the farmer plowed. Alternate translation: “they made their cuts long” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 129:4
## yzu9
Israel is spoken of as being bound by evil people. Alternate translation: “he has freed us from our enemies” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 129:5
## z781
Yahweh is not explicitly mentioned as the one who does these things. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “May Yahweh shame them and defeat them” (See: [[figs-activepassive]] and [[figs-idiom]])

# 129:6
## s2gl
The psalmist speaks of his enemies dying and being few in number. He compares them to the little bit of grass that grows on the roof of a house and withers and is not enough to cut or bundle. Alternate translation: “May they die and may there be few of them” (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 129:7
## s57h
These words finish the simile that begins in ([Psalms 129:6](../129/006.md)). The psalmist speaks of his enemies dying and being few in number. He compares them to the little bit of grass that grows on the roof of a house and withers and is not enough to cut or bundle. “May they be like the grass, which cannot fill … together” (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 129:8
## pu7b
“Yahweh bless you”

# 130:intro
## c2ly
See [[PSA-c2ly]]
# 130:1
## f4r9
See [[PSA-f4r9]]
## h3vi
The author’s sadness is spoken of as if it were a container. His sadness comes from the bottom of the container. Sadness is often spoken of as being a container that fills from the top to the bottom. Alternate translation: “Because I am very sad, I” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 130:2
## i2dr
The ears represent Yahweh, but because the author knows that Yahweh hears everything, he is really asking for Yahweh to respond. Alternate translation: “please listen” or “please respond” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## cvz1
The abstract noun “mercy” can be stated as “merciful.” Alternate translation: “to my pleas and be merciful to me” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 130:3
## fu8l
The speaker uses this question to express the futility of thinking that anyone could stand in this situation. This rhetorical question can be translated as a statement. Alternate translation: “no one could stand.” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## l8mj
“Stand” often represents escaping or surviving when someone attacks. In this case, it would be to escape from being punished. Alternate translation: “no one could escape from your punishment” or “no one could survive your punishment” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 130:6
## lj6l
“My soul” represents the psalmist. Alternate translation: “I” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## yb89
The psalmist is spoken of as if he were waiting on something with expectation. Alternate translation: “I hope” or “I trust” or “I desire for something” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## ge7s
The psalmist speaks of his desire for the Lord to help him as being greater than the desire that those who work all night have for the morning to come. (See: [[figs-simile]])

## cx47
These are men who guard towns or fields against enemies or robbers. Here it refers to men who have to stay awake at night doing this.

# 130:7
## ua2z
The people of Israel are spoken of as if they were a man. Alternate translation: “You people of Israel, hope in Yahweh” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 130:8
## i64f
The people of Israel are spoken of as if they were a man. Alternate translation: “who will redeem the people of Israel from all their sins” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 131:intro
## ej7h
See [[PSA-ej7h]]
# 131:1
## ct5z
See [[PSA-ct5z]]
## px11
Possible meanings are (1) “song people sang while going up to Jerusalem for a celebration” or (2) “song people sang while going up the steps into the temple” or (3) “song whose words are like steps.” See how you translated this in [Psalms 120:1](../120/001.md)

## kgc5
The heart and the eyes represent the person. Alternate translation: “I am not proud or haughty” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## tz2s
Possible meanings are “I do not expect to do great things” or “I do not think I am great.”

## xfb4
Things that are too hard for a person to understand are spoken of as if they are beyond the person or too far away from the person to be able to reach them. Alternate translation: “things that are too hard to understand” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 131:2
## r92s
The soul represents the person or his emotions. Being calm and peaceful is spoken of has having making one’s soul still and quiet. Alternate translation: “I am calm and peaceful” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## sep5
The soul represents the person or his emotions. Alternate translation: “I” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## sim5
The psalmist speaks of himself being content and resting as if he were a young child that no longer demands breast milk from his mother. Alternate translation: “content like a young child that no longer cries for breast milk but rests in his mother’s arms” or “content and resting” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 132:intro
## fp7w
See [[PSA-fp7w]]
# 132:1
## sq3d
See [[PSA-sq3d]]
## lvf4
“because of what happened to David”

## rsq8
“remember” or “think about”

# 132:2
## v7zr
This refers to God.

# 132:3
## qz8t
“King David said”

# 132:4
## s5lw
Sleep and rest are spoken of as if they are things that can be given. Here eyes and eyelids represent the whole person. Alternate translation: “I will not allow my eyes to sleep or my eyelids to rest” or “I will not sleep or close my eyes and rest” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 132:5
## q4n7
Building a place for Yahweh is spoken of as finding a place for him. Alternate translation: “until I build a place for Yahweh” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## ydb1
This refers to God.

# 132:6
## ii2y
The word “it” probably refers to where God’s sacred chest was. The phrase “in Ephrathah” probably refers to where they were when they heard about it. This can be stated clearly. Alternate translation: “we who were in Ephrathah heard about where the sacred chest was” or “we in Ephrathah heard that the holy box was in Jaar” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## nbj6
Jaar is probably another name for the city of Kiriath Jearim. This probably refers to the fields surrounding the city. (See: [[translate-names]])

# 132:7
## gcy9
Worshiping God at the covenant box is spoken of as bowing at the feet of the king who is sitting on his throne. This communicates humility and submission to God. Alternate translation: “we will go to God’s covenant box and worship him as king” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 132:8
## jkj6
The verb “come” can be stated clearly. “Arise, Yahweh, and come to your resting place” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## e7g1
The place God chose for people to worship him is spoken of as if it were a place where he rests or lives eternally. Alternate translation: “the place where you stay” or “your tabernacle” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ktv8
Possible meanings are (1) “come to the ark of your strength” or (2) “come, and make the ark of your strength come.” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

## pg13
“the ark that shows your great power”

# 132:9
## y1an
Integrity is spoken of as if it were clothing. Alternate translation: “May people recognize that your priests have integrity” or “I want people see how your priests always do what is right” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 132:10
## zns5
“Because of what happened to your servant David.” See how you translated a similar phrase in [Psalms 132:1](../132/001.md).

## e268
Here “turning away” means to reject someone. Alternate translation: “do not abandon the king that you anointed” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 132:11
## l5l7
Making a king’s descendant become king in his place is spoken of as placing him on that king’s throne. AT “I will cause one of your descendants to rule Israel in your place” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 132:12
## ir7p
Ruling as king is spoken of as sitting on the throne. Alternate translation: “rule as king” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ht92
Here “your sons” represents the descendants of David that would become king. Alternate translation: “your descendants” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 132:13
## ym8p
See [[PSA-ym8p]]
## kw5c
The author writes as though the city of Zion were a woman. (See: [[figs-personification]])

## wvs3
“Yahweh has desired Zion for Yahweh’s seat.” Here “seat” represents either (1) his throne where he would rule, or (2) the place where he would stay. (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 132:14
## t9p9
The author writes as though the city of Zion ([Psalms 132:13](../132/013.md)) were a woman. (See: [[figs-personification]])

## y9cs
The place God chose for people to worship him is spoken of as if it were a place where he rests or lives eternally. Alternate translation: “the place where I stay” or “my tabernacle” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 132:15
## afl2
God continues to speak about the city of Zion as if Zion was a woman. (See: [[figs-personification]])

## gvy6
“will abundantly bless Zion”

## md5k
Here “poor” refers to the poor people in Zion and “bread” probably represents food in general. Alternate translation: “will satisfy the poor people in Zion with food” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 132:16
## w9cn
Salvation is spoken of as if it is clothing. Possible meanings are (1) “I will cause the priests to behave in a manner worthy of ones whom I have saved” or (2) “I will save her priests” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 132:17
## vls7
God speaks of a powerful descendant of David as if he was the powerful horn of an animal. Alternate translation: “I will make a descendant of David become king after him” or “I will cause David to have a descendant who will be a powerful king” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## yc3b
God speaks of causing David’s descendants to continue to rule as king as if they were a lamp that would continue to shine. Alternate translation: “I will cause my anointed one’s descendants to continue to rule as king” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## dms8
“my chosen king” or “the king I have chosen”

# 132:18
## gp1f
Shame is spoken of as if it was clothing. This shame would result from losing in war. Alternate translation: “I will cause his enemies to be ashamed” or “I will cause his enemies to be defeated and ashamed” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## hdu2
The crown represents his rule, and greatness is spoken of as shining. Alternate translation: “he will be a great king” or “his greatness will shine” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## d9ck
This word is used to stress the importance of the statement that follows.

## s8hv
The relationships among fellow God’s people is spoken of as if they were brothers. Alternate translation: “for God’s people to live together peacefully as brothers” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 133:2
## qj4c
The goodness of unity among God’s people is spoken of as if it were like the fine oil that was poured on Aaron’s head. Alternate translation: “This unity is precious like the oil that was poured on Aaron’s head” (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 133:3
## r3pl
The goodness of unity among God’s people is spoken of as it if it were refreshing like dew. Alternate translation: “refreshing like the dew of Hermon” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## q5fz
This is a mountain in Israel that has snow on its peak year-round.

# 135:4
## e6pd
“Jacob” here refers to his descendants, the people of Israel. Alternate translation: “Yahweh has chosen Jacob’s descendants” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## tbz4
The beginning of the sentence can be stated clearly. Alternate translation: “he has chosen Israel to be his possession” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

# 135:5
## bu42
“I know that our Lord is above all gods.” Being greater than something is spoken of as being above it. Alternate translation: “that our Lord is greater than all gods” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 135:7
## g3hj
A storehouse is a place where things are kept for future use. This imagery shows God’s power to control the wind. Alternate translation: “causing the wind to blow by his power” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 135:9
## pln1
These two words mean basically the same thing and refer to the miraculous troubles that God had caused in Egypt. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## jjz5
The psalmist speaks as if the people of Egypt were listening to him. Alternate translation: “among you people of Egypt” or “among the people of Egypt” (See: [[figs-apostrophe]])

# 135:11
## tnk3
These are the names of two men. (See: [[translate-names]])

# 135:12
## xu2g
God’s gift of the land to the Israelites is spoken of as if it were inheritance from father to son. Alternate translation: “He gave us their land to have forever” or “He gave us their land to be ours forever” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 135:13
## z179
His name here represents his fame or reputation. Alternate translation: “Your fame” or “Your reputation” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 135:18
## wi2e
Being ignorant and powerless is spoken of as being like idols, which cannot speak, see, hear, or breathe. Alternate translation: “Those who make them are stupid and powerless like their idols” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## z43m
“and so are those who trust in the idols”

# 135:21
## l26a
God is spoken of as if he lived in Jerusalem because the temple where the Israelites worshiped him was there. Alternate translation: “he whose temple is in Jerusalem” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## wi2k
This is a reference to the sources of light for the earth, especially the sun and the moon. Alternate translation: “the sun and the moon and the stars”

## g78u
The condition of feeling shame is spoken of as if it were a place that the Israelites had been in. This is a reference to the many times when the Israelites’ enemies had defeated them in battle and shamed them. Alternate translation: “cared when we were shamed” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 136:24
## zn74
Causing people to be victorious and defeat their enemies is spoken of as giving them victory, as if victory were an object that can be given. Alternate translation: “has made us victorious over our enemies” or “has made us able to defeat our enemies” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## hm3q

# 138:2
## bda1

## p2fj
Here the word “name” represents Yahweh himself. Alternate translation: “give thanks to you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## t3ms
The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated with an adjective. The abstract noun “trustworthiness” can be translated with a verbal phrase. Alternate translation: “because you are faithful to your covenant and you are worthy of people trusting you” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

“what you have said” or “your commands and promises”

## zpz8

# 138:6
## sg1t
Yahweh is above all creation in power, position, and authority. Yet his interest is in those who are humble in spirit, servants to all. This is a simple contrast.

# 139:2
## rgf9
The psalmist uses these two actions to represent everything he does. Alternate translation: “everything I do” or “everything about me” (See: [[figs-merism]])

# 139:3
## u269
Here “path” stands for one’s behavior. “My path and my lying down” together represent everything about the psalmist. (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-merism]])

## i5s4

## yr6j

# 139:7
## w65n
These two questions are in parallel. The psalmist says that he cannot go away from God’s presence. Alternate translation: “I cannot escape from your Spirit.” (See: [[figs-rquestion]] and [[figs-parallelism]])

# 139:8
## tdr8
“Making one’s bed” refers to staying somewhere. Alternate translation: “even if I stay in Sheol” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 139:9
## v6q9
The author uses exaggeration to explain that wherever he is, God is there too. (See: [[figs-hyperbole]] and [[figs-hypo]])

## rt5q
In the ancient near east, the sun was often imagined as if it had wings which enabled it to fly across the sky. Alternate translation: “If the sun could carry me with itself across the sky” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## iph4
“very far away to the west”

# 139:10
## fx9r
“will help me”

# 139:11
## z546
The psalmist speaks of the night as if it were a blanket that could conceal him. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 139:12
## v3s8
The night, which is dark, is spoken of as if it were bright with light. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 139:13
## zvi1
“Inner parts” refers to the interior organs of a person, but here the expression probably stands for the entire body. Alternate translation: “You made my entire body (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 139:14
## t36w
Here “soul” probably refers to the psalmist’s innermost ability to be certain about God’s love and guidance. The translator may, however, treat “soul” here as metonymy for the psalmist’s mind and heart. Alternate translation: “I know this with all my heart” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 139:15
## wrz7
“made with great complexity”

## r8mk
This is probably a way of speaking about a mother’s womb (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 139:16
## i7h1
This expression implies that ancient Israelites imagined that God wrote down his plans in a book.

# 139:17
## e3mj
“I consider your thoughts very important” or “Your thoughts are very valuable to me”

## j6ja
“Your thoughts are so many.”

# 139:18
## y1h1
This hyperbole means that the writer would be unable to count God’s thoughts. Alternate translation: “there would be more than I could count” (See: [[figs-hyperbole]])

# 139:19
## g2az
The psalmist is only pretending to speak directly to the violent men whom he has in mind. Translators may decide to express this command as a wish. (See: [[figs-apostrophe]])

# 139:20
## t47k
“They rebel against your authority, God”

## lzi8
“your enemies lie about you”

# 139:21
## f3gc
These two sentences have similar meanings. The second one strengthens the thought in the first. Both of these questions actually make statements. Alternate translation: “Yahweh, I hate those who hate you! I despise those who rise up against you!” (See: [[figs-parallelism]] and [[figs-rquestion]])

## s4kn
rebel against

# 139:23
## e3ka
This is a request for God to tell the psalmist about any sinful thoughts that he may have. Alternate translation: “Please search me” or “I beg you to search me” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## s3gp
These two sentences have similar meanings. The second one strengthens the thought in the first. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

# 139:24
## r9qy
Here “way” stands for behavior. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## h9f8
Here “way” refers to trust and obedience in God. Anyone who “walks” this way will have everlasting life. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 140:intro
## qi17
See [[PSA-qi17]]
# 140:1
## g538
See [[PSA-g538]]
## gc5w
This is for the director of music to use in worship.”

# 140:2
## luc4
Here “battles” probably refers to conflict of any kind, including quarrels.

# 140:3
## pz2s
People who cause conflict by what they say are spoken of as if they had tongues of serpents. Of course, snakes do not do damage with their tongues, but with their bites and especially with poison. Neither can a person make his tongue sharp. Instead, here the idea of a sharp tongue stands for speaking in a way to cause trouble. And the idea the snakes have sharp tongues stands for the fact that many of them have poison. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 140:4
## b8fg
That is, the power of the wicked (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 140:5
## fa3u
The exact kinds of traps are less important than the idea that wicked and proud people are planning to make trouble for the psalmist. If your readers do not know much about different ways of trapping, you may need to reduce this to one line. Alternate translation: “have set a trap to catch me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-doublet]])

# 140:6
## w5qu
This is a call for help. Alternate translation: “listen to me as I call to you now for help” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 140:7
## c56x
A person’s head is in great danger during battle. Protecting the person’s head represents protecting the whole person. Alternate translation: “you protect me when I go to war” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## pz1z
Here “battle” probably stands for any kind of severe trouble (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 140:8
## c5jb
“please do not allow the wicked to have what they desire”

## hdj3
The adjective “wicked” can be translated as a noun phrase. Alternate translation: “wicked people” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

# 140:9
## gn44
This is a sign of being arrogant. Alternate translation: “are arrogant” (See: [[translate-symaction]])

## x51m
This is a prayer that God would make the evildoers suffer from the trouble that they caused by the things they said.

## a8kq
The trouble that they themselves caused by what they said. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## tmk5
That is, stop them from causing any more trouble. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 140:10
## yxz6
Images of fire stand for severe punishment for the wicked. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## pqf9
This is probably a reference to Sheol, the world of the dead.

# 140:11
## sf31
those who speak evil of others without cause (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## i174
“safe in this life”

## k1fm
Here evil is spoken of as if it were someone taking revenge on another person. (See: [[figs-personification]])

# 140:12
## em3r
The abstract noun “justice” can be stated as “just.” Alternate translation: “He will act in a just manner to help the needy” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 140:13
## wfl7
This represents Yahweh. Alternate translation: “to you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 141:intro
## j6r9
See [[PSA-j6r9]]
# 141:1
## f34t
See [[PSA-f34t]]
## gns6
“asking you for help”

## uq2e
The psalmist speaks as if Yahweh were a person who needed to come from another place to help him. What the psalmist wanted Yahweh to do can be stated clearly. Alternate translation: “come quickly to help me” (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-explicit]])

## f66k
“Please hear me when I call” or “I beg you to hear me when I call”

# 141:2
## d4jp
The psalmist asks Yahweh to accept and be pleased with his prayer the way he would accept and be pleased with incense. Alternate translation: “May the my prayer please you the way the sweet smell of incense pleases people” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## vz6a
The psalmist wants Yahweh to be pleased with him because he is praying and because of the words of his prayer. (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## f9h1
“the hands that I have lifted up.” Lifted hands are a metonym for prayer. People lifted their hands when they prayed or praised Yahweh. See how you translated “lift up your hands” in [Psalms 134:2](../134/002.md).

## vf7s
The means to be like the animal that was burned on the altar in the evening. The psalmist speaks as if he wants Yahweh to be as pleased with him as he is with those who bring animals to sacrifice. He wants Yahweh to be pleased because the psalmist is praying or because of the words of his prayer. (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 141:3
## kge1
The psalmist speaks as if evil words were prisoners trying to escape from his mouth. Alternate translation: “please help me not to say things that are evil” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## pt7y
“tell someone to guard”

## hf52
The psalmist speaks as if evil words were prisoners trying to escape from his mouth. Alternate translation: “please help me not to say things when I should not” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 141:4
## cg6p
“do sinful deeds”

## ft7c
“their special foods”

# 141:5
## z9wf
The psalmist speaks as if giving a rebuke were physically hitting someone. Alternate translation: “rebuke me” or “hit me so I will listen when he corrects me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## d396
The abstract noun “kindness” can be translated with an adverb. Alternate translation: “he will be acting kindly to me” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## vbt8
Possible meanings are that the psalmist speaks as if a person correcting him were putting oil on his head (1) to honor him. Alternate translation: “when he corrects me, I will know that the one who corrects me is doing a good deed to me” or (2) to make his head feel better. (See: [[figs-simile]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## sry9
The head is a synecdoche for the person. The litotes can be translated as a positive statement. Alternate translation: “may I accept it gladly” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-litotes]])

## m2xw
The words “wicked deeds” are a metonym for the people who do the wicked deeds. Alternate translation: “I always pray that Yahweh will stop wicked people from doing evil deeds” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 141:6
## k4ld
Possible meanings are (1) “Someone will throw their leaders down” or (2) “Their leaders will throw them down.” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## fj6j
ground that goes straight down a long way

# 141:7
## b6wd
Possible meanings are (1) “people have thrown our bones around in different directions” or (2) as a result of the fall from the cliffs (141:6) “our bodies are broken and our bones lie in disorder.”

# 141:8
## cjd2
The eyes are a synecdoche for the whole person. Alternate translation: “I am looking to see what you will do” or “I expect you to help me” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## wm6m
“I am asking you to protect me” See how “take refuge” is translated in [Psalms 118:9](../118/009.md). (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## wls6
The soul is a metonym for the whole person. Alternate translation: “me” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 141:9
## q9db
The psalmist speaks of deceiving a good man so the good man will sin or so that the evil people can defeat him as if it were laying a trap for an animal. The word “snares” is a metonym for the people themselves. Alternate translation: “people who are looking for ways to harm me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

## y879
Bible experts disagree on the exact meanings of these words. It would be best either to translate one of them with the word for a net or cage that contains the prey and the other as a rope or vine that catches the prey by the leg or neck or to translate both with the general word for “traps.” See how these words are translated in [Psalms 140:5](../140/005.md).

## g9xn
The verb may be supplied from the previous phrase. Alternate translation: “and protect me from the traps that those who do evil have set” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

# 141:10
## zb2q
The psalmist speaks of evil people deceiving good people as if hunters were trapping animals. Alternate translation: “Let the wicked fall into the net traps they have made to trap other people” or “Let the bad things the wicked planned for the righteous happen to the wicked instead”

## tm9v

# 143:1
## jk8k
See [[PSA-jk8k]]
## c8pp
The words “my prayer” are a metonym for the person who is praying. See how these words are translated in [Psalms 39:12](../039/012.md). Alternate translation: “Listen to me as I pray to you” or “Be willing to do what I ask you to do” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 143:2
## h1x7
To “enter into judgment” is an idiom that means to pronounce judgment. Alternate translation: “Please do not judge” or “I beg you not to judge” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## ab38
The psalmist speaks of himself as if he were speaking of another person. Alternate translation: “me” (See: [[figs-123person]])

## u6lh
Here sight represents judgment or evaluation. Alternate translation: “in your judgment no one is righteous” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 143:3
## p6sx
Here the word “soul” represents the person. Alternate translation: “pursued me” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## u666
Defeating an enemy is spoken of as a heavy object crushing a lighter object on the ground. Alternate translation: “has completely defeated me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 143:4
## j66k
“I am weak” or “I am extremely discouraged”

## yv4a
“I no longer have any hope”

# 143:5
## nii3
“think about”

## z21m
“all that you have accomplished” or “all the great things you have done”

# 143:6
## i96g
What one does with one’s body here is a metonym for the purpose of doing so. The Israelites would commonly pray while standing with their hands raised and spread out at their sides. Alternate translation: “pray to you with my hands lifted up at my sides” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## c8nl
The psalmist speaks of wanting to be with God as if he were in a parched land and he also was about to die of thirst. Alternate translation: “I want to be with you the way a person in a parched land who is very thirsty wants water” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## x1rn
The psalmist desires to know Yahweh. The intensity of his desire to know Yahweh is like one who is very thirsty. Alternate translation: “I long for you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## m3qk
The soul is a metonym for the person. (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## zc2r
A land where everything has died because there is no water.

# 143:7
## r837
Here the “spirit” refers to the whole person. Alternate translation: “I am weak” or “I am very discouraged” (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

## h5nt
This is a request. “I beg you not to hide from me” or “Please, do not hide from me”

## t1s2
The psalmist speaks of Yahweh refusing to do what the psalmist asks as if Yahweh were refusing to even look at the psalmist. This litotes can be stated as a positive. Alternate translation: “Do not refuse to listen to me” or “Please listen to me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-litotes]])

## yh17
Here the word “pit” refers to the place of the dead. This phrase is a euphemism for death. Alternate translation: “I will become just another dead person” (See: [[figs-euphemism]])

# 143:8
## cbz8
“Cause me to hear of your covenant faithfulness” or “Tell me of your covenant faithfulness.” The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated with an adjective. Alternate translation: “Let me hear of how you are faithful to your covenant” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## z9rb
Possible meanings are (1) “in the morning,” at the time many people thought was the best time to pray, or (2) “morning by morning,” every day.

## aut8
“Tell me”

## e86d
The psalmist speaks of the way people live as if it were a path on which they walk. Alternate translation: “how you want me to live” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## idb7
Possible meanings are (1) “I pray to you” or (2) “I believe that you will guide and protect me.”

# 143:9
## uh4d
Possible meanings are (1) “I flee to you so I can hide” and (2) “I flee to you so you will hide and protect me.”

# 143:10
## hfy5
“to do what you want me to do”

## u2i6
Possible meanings are (1) “help me to live righteously” or (2) “may my life be free of trouble” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## kpf6
Possible meanings are (1) this is a metaphor for righteous living or (2) “a level land,” a metaphor for life free of trouble. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 143:11
## drk5
Yahweh’s name represents his reputation and character. Alternate translation: “because of who you are” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 143:12
## d1cl
“the enemies who want to take my life”

## wp4f
“Show your covenant faithfulness by cutting off my enemies.” The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated with an adjective. Alternate translation: “Because you are faithful to your covenant, cut off my enemies” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## wl46
“the enemies of my soul.” My “life” may be understood as representing the speaker. Alternate translation: “my enemies” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 144:intro
## j9c6
See [[PSA-j9c6]]
# 144:1
## kh8j
See [[PSA-kh8j]]
## lg69
Possible meanings are (1) “the one who keeps me safe” or (2) “the one who gives me strength” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## r6cj
The words “hands” and “fingers” are synecdoches for “me.” If “war” and “battle” are the same word in your language, you can translate this as one line. Alternate translation: “who trains me for war and trains me for battle” or “who trains me for war” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]] and [[figs-doublet]] and [[figs-ellipsis]])

# 144:2
## k7jc
The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated with anadverb. Possible meanings are (1) “the one who faithfully loves me” or (2) “the one who faithfully protects me.” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## bpc6
The psalmist uses many metaphors to emphasize that Yahweh will protect him. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## naw2
David speaks of Yahweh as if he were a fortress that protects him from attack. Yahweh is the one who protects David from harm. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## v4eq
David speaks of Yahweh as if he were a shield that protects a soldier. Yahweh is the one who protects David from harm. See how this is translated in [Psalms 18:2](../018/002.md). (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ig17
Going to Yahweh for protection is spoken of as taking refuge in him. Alternate translation: “the one to whom I go so he will protect me” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## qyp9
“the one who enables me to defeat other nations”

# 144:3
## la8b
These questions can be translated as statements. Alternate translation: “Man is so small compared to everything else you have made that I am surprised that you take notice of man and that you think about the son of man” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## e6zt
two words for human beings. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 144:4
## hu1p
The writer compares humans to these thing to emphasize how short their lives are. (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 144:5
## cp6t
These words should probably be translated as requests, not commands, since the psalmist knows that God is greater than he is.

## as4e
Possible meanings are (1) tear the sky open or (2) bend the heavens like a tree branch bends when someone walks on it or as one bends a bow before shooting arrows.

# 144:6
## jip6
These should probably be translated as requests, not commands, since the psalmist knows that God is greater than he is.

## ye36
“so they do not know what to think or what to do”

# 144:7
## w63l
David speaks as if God were on land above a flood and had physical hands with which he could pull David out of a flood. The flood is a metaphor for the troubles caused by the “foreigners.” Alternate translation: “You who are able to act, help me overcome my troubles” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## a8fn
Here “hand” refers to power. Alternate translation: “from the power of foreigners” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 144:8
## i188
Here the word “mouths” represent the people who speak. Alternate translation: “They speak lies” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## f1nz
Possible meanings are (1) David speaks of the custom of raising the right hand to swear that what one is about to say in court is true, “they lie even when they swear to tell the truth,” or (2) the “right hand” is a metaphor for power, “everything they have gotten, they have gotten by telling lies.” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 144:9
## wz6d
Possible meanings are (1) “a song no one has ever sung before” or (2) “a song I have never sung before.”

# 144:10
## rad1
You may end a sentence at the end of [Psalms 144:9](../144/009.md) and start a new sentence here. “you. It is you who give … kings. It is you who rescued”

## t9g4
David speaks of himself as if he were someone else. “me, David, your servant”

## r919
David speaks of evil people as if they were the swords they use as weapons. Alternate translation: “from evil people who were trying to kill him” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## a7t7
“Please rescue me and free me”

## vu7l
The people are represented by their “mouths.” See how you translated these words in [Psalms 144:8](./008.md). Alternate translation: “They speak lies” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## me9z
Possible meanings are (1) David speaks of the custom of raising the right hand to swear that what one is about to say in court is true, “they lie even when they swear to tell the truth,” or (2) the “right hand” is a metaphor for power, “everything they have gotten, they have gotten by telling lies.”See how you translated these words [Psalms 144:8](./008.md). (See: [[figs-metaphor]])
