# 145:18
## kq17
Here “is near” means “ready to help.” Alternate translation: “is always ready to help all those who call to him” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## v98h
The abstract noun “trustworthiness” can be stated as an action. Alternate translation: “to all who tell only the truth when they pray” or “to all whom he trusts when they pray” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 145:21
## asw2
Here the words “My mouth” represent the one speaking. Alternate translation: “I will speak” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## t2tr
“tell everyone how good Yahweh is”

## nc4f
The word “name” is a metonym for Yahweh himself. See how “may his glorious name be blessed” is translated in [Psalms 72:19](../072/019.md). Alternate translation: “let all people bless him” or “let all people do what makes him happy” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 146:intro
## s9dj
See [[PSA-s9dj]]
# 146:1
## xb8v
See [[PSA-xb8v]]
## jq1j
Here “soul” represents the writer’s inner being. The writer is commanding his inner being to praise Yahweh. This can be translated as a statement. Alternate translation: “I will praise Yahweh with all my soul” or “I give praise to Yahweh with all my life” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 146:2
## isg7
“until I die” or “while I live”

# 146:3
## x34i
Here “princes” represents all human leaders. (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## br6l
The abstract noun “salvation” can be stated as “save.” Alternate translation: “in any person because they cannot save you” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## ure6
“in humankind” or “in people”

# 146:4
## xqq1
This is a polite way to refer to someone dying. Alternate translation: When a person dies” (See: [[figs-euphemism]])

## c8h2
This means that just as God made the first human, Adam, from the soil, so will a person’s body decay and become soil again when he dies. (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 146:6
## ci47
The words “heaven” and “earth” represent everything that exists in the physical universe. (See: [[figs-merism]])

## ca4t
The abstract noun “trustworthiness” can be stated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “remains trustworthy” or “remains faithful” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 146:7
## zbn6
“He decides matters fairly”

## kk2i
This nominal adjective can be stated as adjectives. Alternate translation: “for oppressed people” or “for those whom other people oppress” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## key9
This nominal adjective can be stated as adjectives. Alternate translation: “to hungry people” or “to those who are hungry” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

# 146:8
## tjb6
Causing a blind person to see is spoken of as if Yahweh were opening the person’s eyes. Alternate translation: “causes the blind to see” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## pav7
This nominal adjective can be stated as adjectives. Alternate translation: “blind people” or “those who are blind” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

## ey4k
Yahweh helping someone is spoken of as if he were physically helping someone to stand up. Alternate translation: “Yahweh helps those who are discouraged” or “Yahweh helps those who are weak” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ml15
This action is a sign of distress or mourning. (See: [[translate-symaction]])

# 146:9
## l8p2
God helping someone is spoken of as if he were physically lifting them up. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 146:10
## kr81
Here “Zion” represents all the people of Israel. The writer is speaking to the people of Israel as if they were there listening to him. Alternate translation: “your God, people of Israel” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-apostrophe]])

## il4h
The words “will reign” are understood. Alternate translation: “will reign for all generations” or “will reign forever” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

# 147:intro
## z5be
See [[PSA-z5be]]
# 147:1
## u7wi
See [[PSA-u7wi]]
## g689
The object may be supplied from the previous phrase. Alternate translation: “it is pleasant to sing praises” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

## i9pm
“praise is fitting” or “praise is appropriate”

# 147:3
## ip6s
The writer speaks of the people’s sorrow and discouragement as if they were physical wounds, and of Yahweh encouraging them as if he were healing those wounds. Alternate translation: “He encourages those who are sad and helps them to heal from their emotional wounds” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 147:5
## sq6c
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “no one can measure his understanding” or “his understanding has no limit” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 147:6
## ret4
The writer speaks of Yahweh honoring those who are oppressed as if Yahweh were lifting them up from the ground. Alternate translation: “Yahweh honors the oppressed” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## j87w
The writer speaks of Yahweh humiliating the wicked as if Yahweh were forcing them to lie on the ground. Alternate translation: “he humiliates the wicked” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 147:7
## x7xx
“while playing a harp”

# 147:9
## y81a
The verbal phrase can be supplied from the previous line. Alternate translation: “he gives food to the young ravens when they cry” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

## hrg8
“whey they chirp” or “when they call”

# 147:10
## ih2w
“Strong horses do not delight him”

## vg8p
Possible meanings are (1) “strong legs” is a metonym that represents how swiftly a man can run. Alternate translation: “men who can run swiftly” or (2) “strong legs” represents the strength of the whole man. Alternate translation: “how strong a man is” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 147:11
## fe9n
The abstract noun “faithfulness” can be translated with and adjective. Alternate translation: “who trust him because he is faithful to his covenant” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 147:12
## c1ra
The writer speaks to Jerusalem, which he also calls Zion, as if it were a person. The names of the city are metonyms for the people who live in it. Alternate translation: “people of Jerusalem … people of Zion” (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

# 147:13
## v5j1
The phrase “the bars of your gates” represent the city as a whole. Yahweh will make Jerusalem secure from enemy invasion. Alternate translation: “For he protects Jerusalem” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## kjw5
The writer speaks of those who live in Jerusalem as if they were Jerusalem’s children. Alternate translation: “he blesses those who live in Jerusalem” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 147:14
## jv5d
“He brings peace.” Possible meanings are (1) Yahweh causes the people who live in Jerusalem to prosper materially and financially or (2) the word translated as “prosperity” means “peace” and Yahweh keeps Jerusalem safe from enemy attack.

# 147:15
## a37s
The writer describes God’s command as if it were a messenger that moves quickly to deliver God’s message. (See: [[figs-personification]])

# 147:16
## c1ee
These emphasize how easy it is for him to do these things. He covers the ground with snow as easily as a person covers something with a wool blanket. And, he removes the frost as easily as the wind blows ashes. (See: [[figs-simile]])

# 147:17
## nl42
Yahweh scatters hail as easily as a person would scatter bread crumbs. Alternate translation: “He dispenses the hail easily, as if it were crumbs” (See: [[figs-simile]])

## ljb8
“He sends”

## iq6h
small pieces of ice that fall from the sky like rain

## sid1
The writer uses this question to emphasize that it is difficult to endure the cold weather that Yahweh causes. Alternate translation: “no one can live in the cold he sends.” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

# 147:18
## db1u
The writer speaks of Yahweh’s command as if it were his messenger. The word “command” can be translated with a verb. Alternate translation: “He commands the ice to melt” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 147:19
## h3ti
These two lines mean the same thing and emphasize that Yahweh gave his law only to Israel. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

## m4av
The verbal phrase can be supplied from the previous line. Alternate translation: “He proclaimed his statutes and his righteous decrees to Israel” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

## c558
The words “statutes” and “righteous decrees,” along with “word” in the previous line, all refer to the law of Moses. If your language does not have different words for these terms, you may combine the two lines into one, using either “Jacob” or “Israel” for the people who received them. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 147:20
## s9ly
The other nations do not know Yahweh’s decrees.

# 148:intro
## ug77
See [[PSA-ug77]]
# 148:1
## hy45
See [[PSA-hy45]]
## y3gp
“Praise Yahweh, you in the heavens … you in the sky.” These two lines are parallel, with phrase “the heights” meaning the same thing as “the heavens” in the previous line. (See: [[figs-parallelism]])

# 148:3
## ri28
The writer speaks to the sun and moon as if they were people and commands them to praise Yahweh. Alternate translation: “Praise Yahweh, sun and moon, as people do” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## qw9e
The writer speaks to the shining stars as if they were people and commands them to praise Yahweh. Alternate translation: “Praise Yahweh, shining stars, as people do” (See: [[figs-personification]])

# 148:4
## ek5l
The phrase “highest heaven” is an idiom that refers to heaven itself. The writer speaks to heaven as if it were a person and commands it to praise Yahweh. Alternate translation: “Praise Yahweh, highest heaven, as people do” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## vf7i
The writer speaks to “the waters that are above the sky” as if they are people and commands them to praise Yahweh. The verbal phrase can be supplied from the previous line. Alternate translation: “praise him, you waters that are above the sky, as people do” (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-ellipsis]])

## ut7b
The writer speaks of a place above the sky where water is stored and from which the rain comes.

# 148:5
## ch3d
Here the word “name” represents Yahweh himself. Alternate translation: “Let them praise Yahweh” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## tcm6
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “he created them” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 148:6
## c9ty
Possible meanings are (1) “he gave a command that is permanent” or (2) “he gave a command that they will not disobey.”

## n8cn
“he gave”

# 148:7
## n48i
This phrase represents every creature that lives in the depths of the oceans. Alternate translation: “all creatures in the ocean depths” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 148:8
## s17i
The writer speaks to these natural phenomena as if they are people and commands them to praise Yahweh. (See: [[figs-personification]])

## u52w
“stormy wind that does what Yahweh commands”

# 148:9
## e5cz
The writer continues to speak to things that are not human as if they were people and commands them to praise Yahweh. (See: [[figs-personification]])

# 148:10
## b65a
The words “wild” and “tame” are opposites. Together they encompass all animals. Alternate translation: “all animals” (See: [[figs-merism]])

# 148:11
## j3b1
See [[PSA-j3b1]]
## w92u
The word “nations” represents the people who live in those nations. Alternate translation: “people of every nation” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 148:12
## g9p4
The writer uses two merisms, one related to gender and one related to age, to represent every person. (See: [[figs-merism]])

# 148:13
## r7cb
Here the word “name” represents Yahweh himself. Alternate translation: “Yahweh, for he alone” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## lr9t
The writer speaks of Yahweh’s greatness as his glory being high above earth and heaven. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 148:14
## qn5e
The writer speaks of strength as if it were the horn of an animal. Lifting up an animal horn was a symbolic action that represented military victory. Alternate translation: “He has made his people strong” or “He has given his people victory” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[translate-symaction]])

## wv8t
“so that all his faithful ones praise him”

## n4ru
The writer speaks of Yahweh loving his people as if his people were physically close to him. Alternate translation: “the people he loves” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 149:intro
## au8i
See [[PSA-au8i]]
# 149:1
## p2dk
See [[PSA-p2dk]]
## e71a
Possible meanings are (1) “a song you have never sung before” or (2) a song no one has ever sung before.

## vlr1
“praise him with songs”

# 149:2
## r1nd
Possible meanings are (1) “rejoice because he made them” or (2) “rejoice because the one who made them is good.”

## jyp7
The words “their king” is likely a reference to God. Possible meanings are (1) “rejoice because he is their king” or (2) “rejoice because their king is good.”

# 149:3
## isj6
The word “name” is a metonym for Yahweh himself. Alternate translation: “praise him” or “tell people how great he is” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## pu1i
a musical instrument with a head like a drum that can be hit and with pieces of metal around the side that sound when the instrument is shaken (See: [[translate-unknown]])

# 149:4
## hrp8
The abstract noun “salvation” can be translated with a verbal phrase. Alternate translation: “glorifies the humble by saving them” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## t8tz
This can be restated to remove the nominal adjective. Alternate translation: “those who are humble” (See: [[figs-nominaladj]])

# 149:5
## b5tj
The translation can make explicit that this refers to when a person lies down at night to sleep in a bed. Alternate translation: “as they lie down to sleep at night” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 149:6
## s1s6
The mouth represents the whole person. Alternate translation: “May they always be ready to praise God” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## pq93
If swords are not known, use the name of a local weapon. The word “sword” is a metonym for being ready to fight in war. Alternate translation: “may they always be ready to go to war for him” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

# 149:7
## c66f
The phrase “the nations” is a metonym for the people who live in the nations. Alternate translation: “the people of the nations” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 149:8
## ka3y
These are made of heavy metal and restrict the movement of prisoners.

## ety5
a pair of chains or bands with a chain between that limits the movement of both a person’s hands or feet.

# 149:9
## jie7
The abstract noun “judgment” can be stated as “judge.” Alternate translation: “They will judge and punish the people of those nations as God wrote should be done” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

# 150:intro
## r7f5
See [[PSA-r7f5]]
# 150:1
## jx5k
See [[PSA-jx5k]]
## djp3
God’s temple was often referred to as his holy place. This was the most common place to go to worship God.

# 150:2
## e6ff
“the great things he has done.” God’s “mighty acts” can possibly mean (1) natural such as thunderstorms and earthquakes or (2) miraculous such as healings and great victories in battle.

# 150:3
## uqx4
See [[PSA-uqx4]]
# 150:4
## m4dg
A tambourine is a musical instrument with a head like a drum that can be hit and with pieces of metal around the side that sound when the instrument is shaken. (See: [[translate-unknown]])

# 150:5
## yat3
two thin, round metal plates that are hit together to make a loud sound (See: [[translate-unknown]])

# 150:6
## c7iw
See [[PSA-c7iw]]
## ht6z
This is an exaggeration that calls on all people who are alive to praise God. (See: [[figs-hyperbole]])
